# Mission Control — Autonomous Bug-Hunt Loop Log

This file is the **handoff document** for the `mission-control-bughunt` scheduled task,
which fires **every 2 hours** (cron `0 */2 * * *`, local time) and uses the **/graphify** skill.
It is SEPARATE from `LOOP_LOG.md` (the `mission-control-evolve` consolidation/feature loop) —
do not cross-contaminate the two.

Each run MUST, in order:

1. **Read this file top to bottom** before doing anything else — never re-fix or re-report a
   bug already listed under "Run History"; pick up the "Next Targets" the previous run queued.
2. **Run /graphify** (Skill tool, `skill: "graphify"`) to scope the hunt area — use
   `graphify query/path/explain` rather than blind grep; run `graphify update .` after editing code.
3. **Pick the SINGLE highest-operator-impact item.** Hunt ALL bug classes across the whole stack
   (logic / visual-UI / coding / misconfiguration; frontend + `hermes-bridge.py` backend + the seams),
   AND each run check the operational spine: kanban lifecycle (delegation / completion / BLOCKED+FAILED
   visibility) and **deliverable integrity** (does every produced output have a visible, retrievable home,
   or is it a lost deliverable? — see "Systemic Threads"). Prioritize lost/hidden deliverables + broken
   lifecycle visibility over cosmetics. Only act on something provable from specific code.
4. **Fix it minimally**, matching the surrounding style.
5. **Test**: `npm run build` + `npm run lint` must pass; add a standalone check for pure-lib logic;
   verify in the Vite preview when it's a UI bug and the bridge is up. State any layer you couldn't verify.
6. **Append** a dated, numbered entry to "Run History" (bug, fix `file:line`, how verified), then
   **rewrite "Next Targets"** with the next focus area + leftover suspicious spots. Never delete history.

**Rules:** ONE solid fix per run beats many shaky ones. Keep all LIVE Hermes-backed functionality
intact. The working tree may carry unrelated inherited churn from the `mission-control-evolve` loop —
leave it untouched; touch only the files for your fix + this log. Do NOT push or open PRs.

---

Carry this sub-lens forward to the still-un-swept #6 verbs [kanban lifecycle route/escalate/cascade/sweep/promote/dispatcher, specify, boards/cron].) (iter #85: swept those #6 verbs — kanban lifecycle wrappers/specify/run_cron/boards/cron/leads/content-media/sessions/transcribe ALL CLEAN [thin-over-#69/#70-STORE, save-immediately, ValueError/KeyError→4xx]; the backend route-logic surface is now largely DRAINED. Freshest backend remaining = the REST of `mc_diag` [doctor/overview/insights/gateway/auth/`_MCP_LINE` parser — only `skills()` was deep-read]; else ROTATE to area #1 `src/lib` pure-logic re-sweep [last full audit #15]. iter #93 closed the autonomous-dispatcher quota-burn STOP-FIRING half (`skip_exhausted` + `DEFAULT_DISPATCH_ATTEMPTS`); iter #94 closed its VISIBILITY half (`escalate_exhausted` + `retry_exhausted` diagnostic now use the same default ceiling → dispatch-exhausted no-budget tasks are flagged/escalatable, not silently parked). ---

## Systemic Threads (standing, multi-run — HIGHER priority than isolated bugs)

**THREAD — BEST-EFFORT MULTI-STEP MACRO / NO-ATOMIC-ROLLBACK (lifecycle+deliverable-integrity, added iter #101):** when one operator action fans out into N independently-persisting sub-steps (each saves its own mutation, there is NO surrounding transaction), the macro must NOT let a single sub-step's exception abort the rest and discard the report of what already committed. Canonical instance closed #101: `sweep_board` (`mc_store.py:1548`) ran its 5 self-heal sub-verbs (reconcile→cascade→reassign→escalate→promote) as bare sequential calls — each `_save_tasks`/`_save_meta`s independently — so one raising verb (e.g. a corrupt `m["links"]` entry → cascade/promote's `for p, c in m["links"]` `ValueError`) propagated out, 500'd the whole call, committed reconcile+cascade's board mutations but threw away their counts, and skipped escalate+promote entirely (retry-burned tasks stay unescalated, ready work unpromoted); the operator path (`OperationsCenter.tsx:352`) collapsed the 500 to a bare "⚠ sweep failed" WITHOUT even refreshing the half-mutated board (`fetchTasks` gated on `res.total>0`). Fixed by running each sub-verb best-effort (`_run` per-verb try/except → records the verb name in an `errors` list, returns an `{"error":…}` sub-result, keeps sweeping); `errors` is threaded through `SweepResult.errors?` (`api.ts`) + surfaced in the Ops Center sweep message (`· ⚠ N failed: …`), and the `total==0`-but-errored case says "no changes applied" not the false "already healthy". RULE for any fan-out macro over independently-persisting sub-steps: (1) does one sub-step raising abort the others / lose the already-committed work's report? (2) is each sub-step isolated so the macro degrades to partial success instead of total 500? (3) is the partial-failure VISIBLE to the operator (which steps failed), not swallowed into a green all-clear or a blank fail? NEXT likely instances: the board-state READ/diagnostic helpers the sweep verbs depend on (`diagnostics`/`dispatchable_tasks`/`_dead_agents`/`_retry_budget`/`_failed_attempts`) — same corrupt-record class one layer up — and any future cron/worker macro that chains multiple writes. **ROOT CAUSE OF THE CORRUPT-LINK SUB-CLASS CLOSED iter #102 (at the source, not just contained):** the very `for p, c in m["links"]` `ValueError` this thread cited as the canonical sweep-killer was unguarded in EVERY direct link consumer too (`diagnostics`/`show_task`/`_would_cycle`/`_cycle_nodes`), so a single malformed link 500'd the Board Diagnostics panel / drawer parent-child list / cycle guard — paths that do NOT go through `sweep_board`'s #101 isolation. Fixed at the load boundary: `_meta()` now normalizes `m["links"]` via `_clean_links()` (keep only well-formed 2-element pairs, drop scalars/wrong-arity/None, self-heal on next save), so no malformed link can reach ANY `for p, c in` site. The corrupt-TASK side of this class was audited CLEAN (`dispatchable_tasks` isinstance-guards its row, the retry helpers isinstance-guard numerics). **The corrupt-AGENT sub-class was CLOSED iter #103 — and #102's note here was WRONG:** `list_agents` does NOT synthesize `name` (`assignees` does, but it is a different, internally-clean source); `list_agents` (`mc_store.py:1718`) returned the raw on-disk list un-normalized, so a non-dict / name-less member in a hand-edited `agents.json` `KeyError`/`TypeError`/`AttributeError`'d the roster GET `agents_with_counts` (`a["name"]`) + every agent CRUD verb (`get_agent`/`create_agent`/`update_agent`/`delete_agent`) and even the `.get("name")` sweep/diagnostic sets (`.get` on a non-dict). FIXED at the load boundary exactly like `_clean_links`: `list_agents` now returns only `dict` members with a non-blank `str` name, defending all consumers + self-healing on the next `_save_agents`. **The corrupt-record class is now DRAINED across the persisted stores: links (`_meta`/`_clean_links` #102), tasks (CLEAN #102), agents (`list_agents` #103) — do NOT re-chase it on `mc_store`.** RULE addition: any list-of-pairs / list-of-records loaded from a persisted store and unpacked positionally (`for x, y in …`) must be shape-normalized at the `_read`/`_meta` load boundary, not guarded ad-hoc at each call site — one normalization is strictly safer than N scattered try/excepts and self-heals the file. **LATENT (carried, do NOT dedicate):** `sweep_board`'s DRY-RUN preview can diverge from the live sweep (each dry verb plans against the *current* board, so e.g. promote's dry preview undercounts what the live sequential sweep actually promotes after reassign re-owns a task) — documented in the docstring; an accurate preview needs a threaded in-memory board overlay (too big for one surgical run). **RULE EXTENSION (iter #104) — the boundary is not just PERSISTED stores; it is ANY untrusted-shape input deserialized then accessed positionally/by-key.** The `claude` CLI's `--output-format json` stdout is the same class one seam over: `run_claude` (`mc_brain.py:168-180`) `json.loads`'d the envelope but guarded only `JSONDecodeError`, so VALID-but-non-object JSON (bare array/string/number/bool) reached `envelope.get("result")`/`.get("is_error")` → `AttributeError` that ESCAPES every call site's `except ClaudeError` (`mission-control-bridge.py:865/902/1443/1830/1851/1934/3279`) into an opaque 500 on the CENTRAL LLM round-trip. FIXED by `isinstance(envelope, dict)`-normalizing at the parse boundary (non-dict → the same raw-stdout fallback as the decode-error path), matching the existing design intent (the `:1950` "falls back to raw" comment). RULE for any subprocess/HTTP/file payload you `json.loads` then `.get()`/unpack: assert the parsed value is the shape you expect (`isinstance(..., dict)`/`list`) at the parse site — a parser that defends invalid-JSON but not valid-wrong-SHAPE-JSON is only half-guarded. `claude_json`'s extraction is already fully guarded (wraps every decode error in `ClaudeError`); `MCSessions` SQLite store audited clean.

**THREAD — RETRY-WITHOUT-CEILING / AUTONOMOUS-LOOP QUOTA-BURN (lifecycle+cost, added iter #93):** any autonomous loop that RE-FIRES a failed unit of work needs a bounded attempt ceiling, AND that ceiling must default to something finite — a budget that is "None unless explicitly set" is effectively infinite for the common case. Canonical instance closed #93: the task dispatcher requeued a failed task to `ready` (`dispatch_task`, `mission-control-bridge.py:518`) and `dispatchable_tasks` (`mc_store.py:1110`) re-offered it every tick with no attempt cap; the only backstop (`escalate_exhausted`/`retry_exhausted` diagnostic) was gated on `max_retries is not None`, which defaults to None (`_blank_task:144`) → a doomed task burned a full `run_claude` turn every 30s forever. Fixed with `DEFAULT_DISPATCH_ATTEMPTS` (def 3) + a `skip_exhausted` filter on the daemon's pick path (manual override preserved). RULE for any auto-retry/auto-fire loop (dispatcher, cron `_fire`, future workers): (1) is there a finite attempt ceiling, (2) does it apply even when no explicit per-item budget is set, (3) does hitting the ceiling leave a VISIBLE state (blocked/flagged) rather than a silent park? **CLOSED iter-94 (visibility half):** `escalate_exhausted` (`mc_store.py:927`) + the `retry_exhausted` diagnostic (`:538`) now use the SAME `_retry_budget(t) or DEFAULT_DISPATCH_ATTEMPTS` ceiling as the dispatcher, so a dispatch-exhausted no-budget task is flagged in Board Diagnostics, counted into the SWEEP gate, and escalatable→`blocked` with a recorded reason (lock-step with the dispatcher's stop-firing threshold — symmetry test confirms both flip at the same fail count). The thread is now closed on BOTH halves (stop-firing #93 + visibility #94). When auditing a NEW autonomous loop, check all three; the cron `_fire` path is CLEAN here (interval/cron jobs stamp `last_run` every fire → self-limiting) but a future per-task worker loop is the likely next instance. **THIRD surface closed iter-95 (queue honesty):** the #94 visibility half covered the DIAGNOSTICS/ESCALATE side, but the ⚡ DISPATCHABLE drawer's own queue still listed dispatch-exhausted `ready` tasks unmarked — the GET `/api/mc/dispatcher` endpoint (read-only, by #93 contract) calls `dispatchable_tasks(limit=20)` WITHOUT `skip_exhausted`, so an exhausted task the autonomous daemon now silently steps over was shown as "1 · next to fire / the exact sequence the dispatcher would fire". Fixed by making `dispatchable_tasks` ALWAYS compute the ceiling and emit a per-row `dispatch_exhausted` flag (mc_store.py:1166-1186; drop only when `skip_exhausted`), surfacing it in the drawer (red ⚑ glyph + EXHAUSTED chip/row-tag + footer count) and correcting the now-stale GET docstring (the list is a SUPERSET of the auto-fire set). RULE addition for this thread: when an auto-loop's stop-firing predicate diverges from a read-only PREVIEW of the same queue, the preview must FLAG the rows the loop will skip — a queue that silently includes skipped rows lies about fire order.

**THREAD — DELIVERABLE-DESTROY-ON-FAILURE (deliverable-integrity, added iter #90):** the MIRROR of the iter-#84 calendar class. #84 was "a mutation that persists ONLY after a fallible side-effect" (a failure DROPS new work); this is the inverse — "a write that OVERWRITES a good deliverable with empty/partial data when the upstream side-effect failed silently." Canonical instance closed #90: `sentinel_news_pipeline.build_and_cache_digest` unconditionally re-wrote `latest.json`/`digest_<today>.json` even when every `fetch_*` swallowed its error and returned `[]`, clobbering the served digest AND blocking self-heal (the bridge only re-runs the pipeline when `latest.json` is ABSENT, `mission-control-bridge.py:3448`). RULE for any cache/deliverable producer that aggregates from fallible sources: an empty/degraded result must NOT overwrite the last-good artifact — early-return (leave the cache, let the next cycle retry) rather than persist nothing-shaped data; and persist the artifact BEFORE any fragile/decorative I/O so the write isn't gated behind it. When auditing a NEW producer that writes a "latest"/"current" file from scraped/aggregated inputs, check: does an all-sources-failed run distinguish itself from a genuine empty, and does it preserve the prior good file? **SECOND instance closed #91:** `scrape_creators` (`mission-control-bridge.py:3055`) overwrote `creators-feed` with `{items:[]}` on an all-Apify outage (every `_http_json` swallowed into `errors`), wiping the last-good viral feed shown in both ContentFactory and the Intelligence Deck; fixed with a `fetched_any` discriminator so the no-clobber guard fires ONLY on a true total outage, never on a genuine "all posts too old" empty. **AUDITED CLEAN #91:** `sync_metricool_brands` (`:2763`) wholesale-overwrites `metricool-brands` but is already guarded — `if not cache["brands"]: raise 502` (`:2790`) precedes the save, so an empty/failed sync can't clobber. **THIRD instance closed #92:** `generate_ai_digest` (`mission-control-bridge.py:3169`, `POST /api/mc/ai-digest`) saved the synthesized `ai-digest` store unconditionally — its HARD-failure paths were already guarded (404 on no-cache/no-stories, 502/503 inside `_llm_json` on a real LLM error), but a degenerate-yet-well-formed reply slipped through: `claude_json` parses an empty `{}` and `_llm_json` wraps a bare array into `{"items":…}`, both passing the dict check with NO summary/ideas → a content-free shell `{summary:"",ideas:[]}` was SAVED, clobbering the last-good digest (panel goes blank). Fixed by raising 502 ("LLM returned an empty digest — kept the previous one; retry") before the save iff `not has_summary and not ideas`, keying on CONTENT not raw shape so a summary-only OR ideas-only digest still saves. **LENS NOW DRAINED across the aggregated-artifact producers:** sentinel pipeline (#90), creators-feed (#91), ai-digest (#92), metricool-brands (CLEAN #91); the leads/calendar/content-ideas `_save_store`s are operator-edited collections (not fallible-source aggregations) and out of this thread's scope. Reopen only when a NEW `_save_store("…", …)` of a scraped/LLM-aggregated artifact appears. **LATENT (carried from #90, do NOT dedicate):** `sentinel_news_pipeline.py`'s `📢`/`✅` `print`s raise `UnicodeEncodeError`→exit 1 under the bridge's `capture_output=True` subprocess on a Windows cp1252 stdout — harmless for the deliverable now that save precedes them (#90), but a `latest.json`-missing bridge run still exits non-zero (→ 502 instead of serving) until the cache exists; an ASCII-only or `errors="replace"`-wrapped stdout would fully close it. Fold into a sweep that touches the file. **(iter #97 re-trace correction:** since #90's `save_digest_cache` runs BEFORE every non-ASCII print and the bridge re-checks `latest_path.exists()` AFTER the subprocess (`mission-control-bridge.py:3497`), a stories-present run that crashes on the print still leaves the digest on disk → returned 200, NOT 502 — so the cp1252 crash is FULLY MASKED on the only call site, lower-impact than this note first implied; still carried-latent.) **(iter #97 NEW instance of the broader deliverable-LOSS class — a normal-path silent drop, not failure-triggered):** `build_and_cache_digest` deduped on `story["url"]`, collapsing distinct blank-url stories (Atom `<link href=..>` / link-less RSS) into one and dropping them from the digest — FIXED with a title-fallback dedup key (`:154`). Lens: any dedup keyed on a field that can be legitimately blank/missing silently merges DISTINCT items; key on a composite (`url or title`) or skip-blank instead. **(iter #98 — the LAST unguarded aggregated-artifact producer, sibling of #92):** the #92 drain-note parked the "content-ideas `_save_store`s" as out-of-scope operator-edits — CORRECT for the `consume`/`skip` mutations, but WRONG for `generate_content_ideas` (`mission-control-bridge.py:3437`, `POST /api/content/ideas`), which is itself a fallible LLM aggregation (`_llm_json` over viral feed × Sentinel news × brand doc) and was overlooked. It saved `result` UNCONDITIONALLY (input-only guard at `:3410`, never the output), so a degenerate well-formed reply (`{}` / explicit `"ideas": null` / `{"items": …}` bare-array wrap) saved `{strategy_note:"", ideas:[]}`, clobbering the last-good deck AND resetting `used:[]`/`skipped:[]` (taste-state loss). FIXED with the exact #92 content-empty guard (`not has_note and not ideas` → 502 before save, keeping the prior deck). **The aggregated-artifact-producer drain is now genuinely complete: sentinel pipeline (#90/#97), creators-feed (#91), ai-digest (#92), content-ideas-generate (#98), metricool-brands (CLEAN #91); the leads/calendar/`consume`/`skip` `_save_store`s remain true operator-edits, out of scope.** Reopen only when a NEW `_save_store` of a scraped/LLM-aggregated artifact appears.

**THREAD — PRIMARY↔FALLBACK PARITY (deliverable/lifecycle-visibility, added iter #99):** any store/component that has a PREFERRED data path (a bridge aggregator GET) AND a degraded CLIENT-SIDE fallback (derive from raw kanban tasks when the GET fails) must keep the two paths' projections in lock-step — a divergence means the SAME data renders differently (or disappears) depending only on whether the GET happened to succeed, which the operator can't predict or diagnose. Known instances in `useContentStore.ts`, all the same root cause (a backend projection was fixed but the client mirror wasn't): `platformFor()` vocabulary (full-name vs IG/TT/X short codes — fixed pre-#99, see `:48-53`); `isoDate()` LOCAL-vs-UTC calendar boundary (off-by-one, fixed iter #43, `:72-82`); and **CLOSED #99: the drafts status set** — backend includes `todo/pending/ready/blocked/failed` (`mission-control-bridge.py:2335`) but the fallback filtered `=== 'ready'` only, dropping blocked/failed content tasks from the Factory drafts queue + hardcoding `status:'ready'`; fixed to mirror the backend set (`['ready','blocked','failed']` since normStatus folds todo/pending→ready) and emit the real status. RULE when auditing/adding a fallback: enumerate every projected field (status set, platform code, date basis, dedup key) and confirm the fallback computes it identically to the bridge handler; when you fix a backend projection, GREP the client store for the same field's fallback and fix BOTH. Likely next instances: any OTHER store with a `try { await getX() } catch { …derive client-side… }` shape (`useLeadStore`, `useGhostStore`, `useBriefingStore` — check whether each derives a field the bridge now computes differently). **AUDITED iter #100 — those three named candidates are DRY:** all three are SINGLE-PATH (derive from a single GET and on failure set an error state; no degraded client-side derivation that could diverge) — `useLeadStore`/`useGhostStore` off `getMcAgents`, `useBriefingStore` off `getMcBriefing`/`getSentinelDigest`. `grep catch src/stores/*` confirms `useContentStore` is the ONLY store with a genuine `getX() → catch → derive-from-kanban` dual path. **FOURTH instance closed #100 (in `useContentStore`, date-basis field):** the fallback calendar used `isoDate(t.created_at)` only, never honoring an explicit date written into the task title/body, while the backend derives `date` via `_extract_date(title+body)` FIRST (`mission-control-bridge.py:2346`) — so a "Launch post 2026-07-15" task landed on its target day via the GET but its CREATION day on the fallback; FIXED with a client `extractDate()` mirroring the backend's two regexes + precedence (`src/stores/useContentStore.ts`). **KNOWN RESIDUAL in the same store, NOT fixed (platform-code field):** client `platformFor()` recognizes `reel`/`tweet`/`thread`/`video`/`article`/`seo` (→ IG/X/YT/WEB) that the backend `_detect_platform` does NOT, so the same task gets a specific badge on the fallback but `MULTI` on the normal path. Aligning is fiddly + risky: the backend uses whole-word matching for short codes (#16) but the client uses plain `.includes()` substring, so naively copying the client's extra keywords to the backend would introduce substring false-positives on the PRIMARY path ("f`reel`ance"→IG, "p`article`"→WEB, "free`lance`"); aligning the OTHER direction (drop the client's extra keywords) degrades the fallback's classification for no gain. Low operator value (a badge label, mostly on a degraded path). Reopen only with a unified whole-word matcher applied to BOTH sides. So the PRIMARY↔FALLBACK PARITY thread is now well-drained on the only dual-path store: `platformFor` vocab (pre-#99), `isoDate` boundary (#43), drafts status set (#99), calendar date-basis (#100) — all closed; platform keyword-SET the one logged residual.

**THREAD — PATH-FROM-USER-PARAM (security, added iter #88):** any bridge endpoint that builds a filesystem path from a request-controlled value must sanitize/pin that value BEFORE the join — the bridge runs CORS `*` (`mission-control-bridge.py:36`/`:659`), so an unvalidated path param is a drive-by arbitrary-file primitive from any page in the operator's browser. Known instances: `serve_media` (`:2894`, sanitizes ✓), `get_sentinel_digest_by_date` (`:3508`, pinned to `[0-9][0-9_-]{0,31}` as of #88 ✓). When auditing a NEW path-handling route, check it against this class; when adding one, copy the `re.fullmatch`/`re.sub` guard. Do NOT loosen either guard to admit `.`/`\`/`/`.

These come from the iter #3 deliverable-flow investigation. Mission Control is the command center; a task's
output must have a visible, retrievable home or it's a **lost deliverable**. The backend PERSISTS deliverables
correctly (`task.result`, `latest_summary`, `runs[].summary`, worker-log file, `workspace_path`, `branch_name`),
but the UI surfaces them only through **`TaskDetailDrawer`**, reachable only from Operations Center board cards.
Work these top-down; each is likely several runs. Reuse `TaskDetailDrawer` (already renders result/summary/runs)
rather than building new surfaces.

- [x] **LIFE-1 (LOW/MED) — drawer actions swallow errors — FIXED iter #11 (LIVE-VERIFIED).** `TaskDetailDrawer.tsx`
  `act()` ran `await fn(); await load();` with no catch and **ignored the boolean** every store verb returns — so a
  failed verb (claim/complete/block/promote/reassign/comment/link…) just silently reloaded with no operator-visible
  reason. **Fix (2 files):** (1) `act()` now wraps in try/catch/finally, checks the returned `ok`, and on `false`
  captures `useTaskStore.getState().error` into a new `actError` state (rendered as a dismissible red banner under the
  ACTIONS grid; the catch also covers any throw from the callback bodies like `if(ok)onClose()`). (2) store `mutate()`
  now stashes `bridgeDetail(err)` instead of `errMessage(err)` — so the surfaced reason is the bridge's real FastAPI
  `detail` / CLI stderr (e.g. "task 't_x' not found") not axios's generic "Request failed with status code N"; this also
  upgrades the only other consumer of `useTaskStore.error` (WorkflowBuilder). **Live-verified (bridge up):** confirmed
  the bridge returns `{"detail":"task '…' not found"}` on a rejected verb (curl, no mutation); then in the :5219 preview
  opened a real todo task's drawer and, via a **zero-mutation** monkeypatch of `promoteTask` (dynamic-imported the same
  store module, made it resolve `false` + set error exactly like a real reject), clicked PROMOTE → the red error line

- [x] **LIFE-2 (MED) — terminal `archived` status had no board column → leaked into TODO — FIXED iter #37.** `mc_store`

  (`useGhostStore.mapAgentsToTopology` + `useLeadStore.mapAgentToLead`):** these sum a SET of statuses for an agent's queue depth, so
  a NON-terminal/non-running held status omitted from the set silently UNDER-counts (the inverse of the catch-all mis-file). The
  canonical held set is `ready/todo/blocked/review/scheduled/triage` (`done`/`completed`/`archived`/`failed` excluded as terminal/adverse;
  `running` is its own bucket). Both mappers were fixed in lock-step to this set — `useGhostStore` iter #79, `useLeadStore` iter #80 — so
  the two are now SYNCHRONIZED and the bucket-completeness lens is DRAINED on them; if a NEW mc status lands, BOTH must gain it together.

  the dot is the canonical-deliverable cue (`task.result` is THE deliverable field per the deliverable-flow map) with no

- [x] **LIFE-3 (MED) — stale `completed_at` made a revived task masquerade as DONE — FIXED iter #69.** `block_task`/`fail_task`
  stamp `completed_at` (terminal marker); `unblock_task` clears it on revive but `promote_task`/`schedule_task`/`requeue_task`
  did NOT, so reviving a blocked task (PROMOTE/SCHEDULE are drawer-offered on `blocked`) left the stamp and `get_activity`
  emitted a false green "completed" row for the now-pending task in the War Room + Ghost feeds. Fixed by clearing
  `completed_at` in all three revive verbs (`mc_store.py:337/342/1168`), mirroring `unblock_task`. **Standing lens this
  produced (`completed_at`-invariant):** `completed_at` is set IFF the task is in an ended state (done/blocked/failed); ANY
  verb that transitions a task to a non-terminal/active status (ready/running/scheduled/triage/review) must clear it — grep
  any new `_mutate` verb that sets such a status for a missing `t["completed_at"] = None`. (`reclaim`/`reassign(reclaim)`
  only touch `running` tasks, which never carry the stamp, so they're exempt.) Same operational-spine class as the iter
  #47/#55 blocked-as-running masquerade. **Symmetric closure iter #70:** the lens also covers the AUTO/self-heal
  verbs — `escalate_exhausted` (`mc_store.py:947`) and `cascade_dependencies` HOLD (`:1355`) now SET `completed_at`
  when they flip a task to `blocked` (mirror `block_task`), and `cascade_dependencies` PROMOTE (`:1366`) CLEARS it
  when it revives a held child to `ready` (mirror `unblock_task`). HOLD-set + PROMOTE-clear are inseparable (stamping
  on HOLD without clearing on PROMOTE would reintroduce the #69 false-green-completed row via the cascade path).
  `reconcile`/`route_triage`/`promote_ready`/`reassign_dead_agent` were swept CLEAN (they only touch running↔ready /
  triage→todo / todo→ready, statuses that never carry the stamp). **The `completed_at`-invariant is now upheld by
  EVERY status-mutating verb in `mc_store.py` — manual (#69) and automatic (#70).**
- [x] **CRON-PARSE-PARITY (LOW/MED, recurring) — the UI schedule parser must agree byte-for-byte with the daemon, or a job "looks scheduled, never runs" — instances closed #27/#28/#58/#71.** `src/lib/cronSchedule.ts` (operator's countdown) and `mc_scheduler.py` (what actually fires) are two hand-kept copies of the same grammar; ANY leniency the UI has that the daemon lacks renders a phantom next-fire for a job the daemon silently drops. Closed instances: `every`-spacing (#?), unit coverage `30s`/`5min`/`every30m` (#27/#28/#58), and **#71 — `parseInt` truncates trailing garbage (`'15m'`→15) where Python `int()` raises; `range.split('-')` drops a 3rd bound where `partition`+`int` rejects.** `expandField` now routes every token through a `strictInt` (`/^[+-]?\d+$/`) and requires exactly-two range bounds. **Standing lens:** when touching EITHER parser, diff it against the other field-by-field; a standalone `tsx` parity harness (parse each fixture in BOTH, assert `parseSchedule(x).kind === mc_scheduler.schedule_kind(x)`) is the canonical check. Remaining theoretical micro-divergences are exotic (`'5_0'` underscore-int, etc.) and not worth chasing without a real report.

- [x] **SKILL-DESC (LOW, hidden-deliverable) — every skill's description was parsed then discarded — FIXED iter #85.** `mc_diag.skills()` (`mc_diag.py:92`, feeds `GET /api/mc/skills` → Arsenal SKILL REGISTRY) read each `SKILL.md` frontmatter `description:` into `desc` but emitted `"category": category or desc or "skill"` with `category = source` (always `"plugin"`/`"local"`, always truthy) — so the short-circuit ALWAYS returned `source` and `desc` was dead code: the operator saw bare skill names grouped into two source-redundant buckets with no hint of what any skill does. Fixed by emitting a real `"description"` field (`category` stays = source so grouping is byte-identical), adding `McSkill.description?` (`api.ts`), and surfacing it in the Arsenal chip `title` tooltip + the skill filter. Proof: 9/9 live skills now carry a description (was 0), grouping preserved. **Standing lens (computed-then-discarded):** any backend parser that extracts a human-useful field (description/summary/reason/label) must EMIT it to a field the UI renders — a `X or Y`-style short-circuit where `X` is structurally always-truthy silently buries `Y`; grep new aggregators in `mc_diag`/the bridge for an extracted-but-unreferenced local. Same family as DELIV-3/DONE-CARD (output produced, no visible home), on the capability surface.
- [x] **CHAT-TS (LOW/MED) — chat transcript history was re-stamped to load-time — FIXED iter #81 (LIVE-confirmed).** `useChatStore.selectSession` decoded each loaded message's timestamp with a `typeof === 'string'` guard, but the native session store (`mc_brain.MCSessions`) stamps messages with `time.time()` — epoch SECONDS as a JSON **number** — so the guard always missed and fell back to `tsNow()`, collapsing every reopened conversation's history onto the open-time clock (ChatTerminal renders `formatTime(msg.timestamp)`). Fixed with a `msgTime()` helper (number→×1000→ISO, string→passthrough, invalid→now). **Standing lens (bridge-value-shape):** any value crossing the bridge boundary that the frontend type unions as `string | number` (or any epoch field) must be DECODED for BOTH shapes — a `typeof === 'string'`/`'number'`-only guard that silently falls back is a latent data-loss bug; the bridge stamps epochs as Python `time.time()` floats (SECONDS), so multiply ×1000 before `new Date()`. Same seconds-vs-ms family as the WarRoom `*1000` thread, but here the failure was a type-shape mismatch, not a unit error. **LENS DRAINED iter #82:** applied this lens across the WHOLE frontend — all `string|number`/`number|string` `api.ts` fields (`started_at`/`ended_at`=dead, `posted_at`=not-date-decoded, `elapsed`=unused) + every `new Date(...)` in `src/` are correctly decoded; no lone `typeof`-guard-with-silent-fallback remains. Re-open only on a NEW bridge field typed as a shape union. Iter #82 also surfaced an ADJACENT date-class hole (now FIXED): a `new Date(externalData).toISOString()` THROWS `RangeError` on a bad date (vs `toLocaleString()` which degrades) — guard any `.toISOString()` on uncontrolled bridge/cache data with a `Number.isNaN(d.getTime())` check. **Iter #83 completed the date-class lens (BAD-DATE thread):** the `toLocale*` family is the MIRROR trap — `new Date(bad).toLocaleTimeString()`/`toLocaleString()`/`toLocaleDateString()` do NOT throw, they return the literal string `"Invalid Date"`, so a try/catch around them is DEAD and the garbage leaks to the UI. Fixed `ChatTerminal.formatTime` (was try/catch-wrapped → showed "Invalid Date"; now `Number.isNaN(getTime())`→`--:--`). **Rule for ALL date renders on external data:** the only correct guard is an explicit `Number.isNaN(new Date(x).getTime())` check BEFORE formatting — never rely on try/catch (`toLocale*` won't throw) and never leave `.toISOString()` unguarded (it will). Frontend now swept clean for both variants (`msgTime`#81, `safeStamp`#82, `formatTime`#83); re-open only on a NEW date render of an uncontrolled field.
- [x] **DISPATCH-EXHAUST-VISIBILITY (MED, lifecycle/quota-burn class) — a doomed `ready` task burned Claude quota invisibly; now fully surfaced — CLOSED on ALL FOUR surfaces #93→#96.** The autonomous dispatcher re-fired a failed-then-requeued `ready` task EVERY tick with no attempt ceiling (the escalate/diagnostic backstops only covered tasks with an explicit `max_retries`, which most lack). Closure arc: **#93** added `DEFAULT_DISPATCH_ATTEMPTS` (env `MC_DISPATCH_MAX_ATTEMPTS`, def 3) + a `skip_exhausted` filter so the daemon STOPS auto-firing a doomed task (manual force-dispatch keeps the override); **#94** made the `retry_exhausted` diagnostic + `escalate_exhausted` use the SAME default ceiling so the parked task is VISIBLY diagnosed/escalatable→`blocked`-with-reason; **#95** added a per-row `dispatch_exhausted` flag on `dispatchable_tasks` (the GET endpoint is a superset of the auto-fire set) + red ⚑ markers/header-chip in the ⚡ DISPATCHABLE drawer body so the "next to fire" queue stops lying; **#96** added a red `· N⚑` segment to the ⊙ AUTONOMY ⚡ DISPATCHABLE TAB BADGE so the glance-level emerald "ready" count no longer counts auto-skipped rows as fireable (worst case: all-exhausted queue read emerald "N" when 0 fire). **Standing lens (engine-vs-glance honesty):** when an endpoint deliberately returns a SUPERSET (so an operator can manually override) of what an autonomous engine will act on, EVERY summary surface over that list — drawer row, header chip, AND tab badge — must visibly segment the subset the engine SKIPS; a flat count that conflates "listed" with "will run" is a quota-/expectation-level lie. Grep any new glance-level count fed by `dispatchable_tasks`/a `skip_*`-filtered list for the missing exhausted/skipped split. Do NOT revert any of the four; do NOT make a manual endpoint pass `skip_exhausted=True` (breaks the override); do NOT make the badge emerald count EXCLUDE exhausted (it mirrors the drawer header total + the ⚑ segment carries the subset). See memory: hermes-kimi-quota-burn (the Claude-era instance of that class).
- [x] **MUT-SIGNAL (LOW/MED, honest-signal class) — a mutation handler returned hardcoded `success:true` for a 0-row write — FIXED iter #87 (LIVE pre-fix repro).** `session_rename`/`session_delete` (`mission-control-bridge.py:2041`/`:2048`) ran SQLite `UPDATE`/`DELETE` that affect 0 rows for a missing/raced `session_id` yet always returned `success:true`, while the sibling `session_get` 404s — so the UI's optimistic `useChatStore.rename` painted a new title that the next `/sessions` poll silently reverted (phantom rename). Fixed by returning `cursor.rowcount > 0` from `MCSessions.rename`/`.delete` (`mc_brain.py:288`/`:292`) and 404-on-false in both handlers, matching `session_get`. **Standing lens:** a mutation handler must report the DB's real affected-row count — an UPDATE/DELETE that matched nothing is a 404, never a success. Re-apply this lens to any other write verb that returns a fixed `success`/`ok` without consulting `rowcount`/an existence check.

1. ~~**`mapMcToOp` is a lossy status projection**~~ — RESOLVED iter #35. The trigger documented here
   ("any consumer that reads `tasks[].status`") materialized: `useAgentCrud.tsx:125`'s spawn-agent
   dropdown renders `[{status}]` per task, so `todo/triage/review/scheduled` tasks showed as `[PENDING]`.
   Fixed in `src/stores/useTaskStore.ts` — widened the `OpTask['status']` union (`:55`) + made
   `mapMcToOp` (`:131`) pass each mc lifecycle status through faithfully (`completed→done` the lone
   normalization, unknown→`pending` fallback). Build + standalone-logic VERIFIED. Do NOT re-report.
2. ~~**WarRoom activity timestamp**~~ — RESOLVED (not a bug). Iteration #2 confirmed `hermes-bridge.py`
   `/api/hermes/activity` (L583-593) emits task lifecycle stamps verbatim in epoch **seconds**, so WarRoom's
   `new Date(a.timestamp * 1000)` is correct. GhostNetwork's `norm()` is just defensive. Do NOT "fix" this.
3. ~~**Operations BLOCKED column vs chip mismatch**~~ — RESOLVED iter #7. FAILED is now its own column +
   chip in `src/pages/OperationsCenter.tsx`; BLOCKED column == BLOCKED chip, FAILED column == FAILED chip.
4. ~~**`OperationsCenter` OLDEST READY: correct-by-accident math**~~ — RESOLVED iter #46. The chip rendered
   `ago(Math.floor(Date.now()/1000) - oldestReady)` where `oldest_ready_age_seconds` is already an age — the
   caller fabricated a fake timestamp so `ago`'s internal `now - ts` would cancel back to `age` (two `Date.now()`
   reads cancelling). Live-exercised since iter #35 (8 ready tasks; ~8.67d). Fixed by extracting `fmtAge(seconds)`
   (formats a duration directly), re-expressing `ago(ts)=fmtAge(now - ts)`, and rendering `fmtAge(oldestReady)`.
   Build+lint+standalone old-vs-new equivalence proof (all buckets MATCH). No visible change. Do NOT re-report.
5. ~~**`useChatStore.send` catch re-derives the transcript key**~~ — RESOLVED iter #15. The catch now appends the
   error to the same `key` the user message used (`src/stores/useChatStore.ts:235`), so a send failure during a
   mid-flight conversation switch no longer lands the error in the wrong chat. Do NOT re-report.

- **FAIL-STATE (MED, operational-spine, NEW — fully characterized this run): `failed` task status is UNREACHABLE.** No store
  method or endpoint ever sets `status="failed"` (`mc_store.py` lifecycle = claim→running, complete→done, block→blocked,
  unblock/promote→ready, schedule→scheduled, archive→archived, reassign — grep-confirmed no `failed` setter anywhere; the
  per-task circuit-breaker BLOCKS, it does not fail). Yet `failed` is *read* in 5 places (briefing :1295/:1313, activity :574,
  pipeline :1425-1426/1441, stats). **Consequence:** the iter #7 FAILED column + FAILED chip in `OperationsCenter.tsx` are
  permanently dead (always 0), and **failures are NOT distinguishable from blocks** (the task's explicit operational-spine
  question) because the only way to record a failure is `block_task`. This is vestigial Hermes-era surface (the old dispatcher
  stamped `failed`). Two coherent fixes for a future run — decide deliberately, do not do both: (A) ADD a `fail_task(reason)`
  store transition + `POST /api/mc/tasks/{id}/fail` + a frontend `failTask` action + drawer FAIL button (mirrors `block_task`;
  makes the FAILED machinery reachable) — but this is a multi-surface FEATURE, slice it; or (B) if failures are intentionally
  modeled as blocked-with-reason, REMOVE the dead FAILED column/chip to stop showing an always-empty lane. Iter #17 left it as a
  hook for an external process, so prefer (A)'s store+endpoint slice only if there's real demand; otherwise leave as documented.
  **PARTIAL MITIGATION iter #25:** the notification path no longer ignores failures — a task that dead-ends to `blocked` now raises an OS toast + an in-app Notification Center entry rendered as a distinct **amber BLOCKED** outcome (vs green DONE), so failures are visible AND distinguishable *in the bell*.
  **OPTION (A) FULLY SHIPPED — FAIL-STATE CLOSED END-TO-END (backend iter #30 + trigger iter #31):** ✅ **Backend (iter #30)** — `mc_store.fail_task(task_id, reason)` (`mc_store.py:319`) + `POST /api/mc/tasks/{id}/fail` (`mission-control-bridge.py:782`, reuses `BlockTaskPayload`) mirror `block_task` exactly (status→`failed`, `completed_at` stamp, `failed` event carrying the reason — the shape the iter-#6 drawer banner / iter-#7 column / iter-#25 notifier already read), making `failed` a REACHABLE status. ✅ **Trigger (iter #31)** — `failMcTask()` (`api.ts:203`) + `failMcTaskById` verb (`useTaskStore.ts:400`, via the iter-#11 `mutate()` error path) + a drawer **FAIL** button (`TaskDetailDrawer.tsx`, `ALLOW.fail = todo/ready/running/review/triage/blocked`, darker-red tone vs BLOCK). A real operator action can now mark a task failed, and the entire dead cluster — FAILED column, FAILED chip, amber notifier outcome, drawer reason banner — lights up with no further read-side work. Verified build+lint+zero-mutation live-HTTP route probe; a real-task live-DOM mutation was deliberately not done (would churn operator data — the render side was already verified piecemeal in iters #7/#25/#6/#29). Option (B) [remove the dead lane] is OBSOLETE; do NOT remove the FAILED column/chip — it is now live. ✅ **Activity-feed leak (iter #32)** — the LAST surface that still collapsed `failed`→`blocked` was `/api/mc/activity`'s event synthesis (`mission-control-bridge.py` `get_activity()`); a `failed` task (now reachable via the FAIL button, `completed_at` stamped) was emitted as `"blocked · {title}"` so the War Room AGENT SIGNAL feed + Ghost Network Activity Stream showed it as a block. Fixed to emit a distinct `failed`/`failed` (frontend vocab already renders it). **FAIL-STATE is now distinguishable from blocked on EVERY operator surface — column, chip, notifier, drawer banner, AND the live activity feed. NOTHING REMAINS OPEN on FAIL-STATE. Do NOT re-fold failed→blocked in the activity synthesis.**
- **CF-NEXTRUN (LOW): `_next_run` only understands `30m`/`2h`/`1d` intervals** (`mc_store.py:579`); a cron-expression or
  natural-language schedule returns `None`. **Lower-priority than thought: no `cron.json` exists on the live board (zero cron
  jobs), so present operator impact is nil** — verify against how the UI renders a null next_run before bothering.
- **`_extract_date` (LOW, latent): MM/DD-vs-DD/MM misparse + no single-digit / no validation** (`mission-control-bridge.py:1510`).
  Regex `\d{2}/\d{2}/\d{4}` always reads parts as MM/DD, so a DD/MM date (`25/12/2026`) → invalid `2026-25-12` ("Invalid Date" in
  the Content Factory calendar); single-digit dates (`6/5/2026`) don't match at all. **Zero present impact** — scanned all live
  task data, NO slash-dates exist. Fix only if it surfaces.
- **`_gather_idea_inputs` viral_lines bare subscripts (LOW, latent): `v['creator']/'platform'/'likes'/'comments'/'views'/'caption']`**

### 2026-06-22 — Iteration #104 (focus: LIVE-PROBED first [bridge UP `:8767`, `/api/ping` `{ok:true, uptime_seconds:13831}` — process RESTARTED again since #103 (~3.8h), so the bridge serves current code; `/api/mc/health` `cli_ok:true`/`claude` 2.1.183], then executed iter #103 Next-Targets (b)2 — ROTATED to a genuinely-new lens/cluster: the `mc_brain` `claude` CLI invocation/JSON-parse seams under the MALFORMED-CLI-OUTPUT lens. Found + fixed a real uncaught-crash gap on the CENTRAL LLM round-trip.)
- **Audited:** first re-scoped via /graphify (`query "get_briefing aggregate from sources / on failure"` → `get_briefing()` `mission-control-bridge.py:2166`). Confirmed `get_briefing`/`get_content_pipeline` aggregate ONLY from internal `STORE.*` (already corrupt-record-hardened #102/#103) with no fallible external sources, so the partial-source-degradation lens is weak there — correctly rotated to the fresher (b)2 frontier. Then deep-read `mc_brain.py` end-to-end (`run_claude`/`claude_json`/`MCSessions`).
- **Bug (medium, malformed-CLI-output / shape-normalize-at-load-boundary class):** `run_claude` (`mc_brain.py:168-180`) parsed the CLI envelope with `envelope = json.loads(stdout)` and guarded ONLY the `JSONDecodeError` case (invalid JSON → wrap raw stdout). But `--output-format json` stdout that is VALID JSON yet NOT an object (a bare array `[1,2,3]`, string, number, or `true` — all legal JSON) flowed straight into `envelope.get("result")` (`:176`) and `envelope.get("is_error")` (`:180`), where `.get` raises `AttributeError: 'list' object has no attribute 'get'`. This is the CENTRAL LLM round-trip used by EVERY brain action (chat, content-gen, AI digest, cron jobs, dispatcher). Critically, the AttributeError is NOT a `ClaudeError`, so it ESCAPES every bridge call site's `except ClaudeError` mapping (confirmed at `mission-control-bridge.py:865/902/1443/1830/1851/1934/3279`) → surfaces to the operator as an opaque FastAPI 500 instead of the clean COMMS-FAILURE message the code carefully constructs. The existing JSONDecodeError fallback + the `:1950` comment ("…--output-format json output is non-JSON, run_claude falls back to raw") prove the DESIGN INTENT was already graceful degradation — the valid-non-object case was simply the un-covered half.
- **Fix (`mc_brain.py:168-180`):** after `json.loads`, set `envelope = None` on decode error, then coerce with a single `if not isinstance(envelope, dict): envelope = {"result": stdout, "is_error": proc.returncode != 0}` — folding BOTH the invalid-JSON and valid-non-object cases into the same raw-stdout-as-answer fallback (the established "shape-normalize at the load boundary, not ad-hoc per-call-site" RULE from the corrupt-record thread #102/#103, now applied to the CLI-output boundary). `envelope` type widened to `Any`.
- **Verified:** `python -m py_compile mc_brain.py` OK; standalone harness monkeypatching `subprocess.run` over 6 stdout shapes (bare array/string/number/bool, normal object, invalid JSON) → ALL degrade gracefully post-fix, normal object STILL extracts `result`/`session_id` intact; replicated the OLD logic inline to PROVE the pre-fix `AttributeError: 'list' object has no attribute 'get'` was real (not hypothetical); `npm run build` GREEN (frontend untouched). Patch note iter-104 (bug/medium) added. Bridge live but no DOM change (backend-only); UI verification N/A.
- **Files touched:** `mc_brain.py` (`run_claude` non-dict-envelope guard), `.mc/patch-notes.json` (iter-104), `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry + Systemic Threads + Next Targets + Focus-Area Rotation), `graphify-out/*` (ran `graphify update .`). No commit/push (loop rules); inherited churn left untouched.

### 2026-06-22 — Iteration #103 (focus: executed iter #102 Next-Targets (b) — the LAST un-probed corrupt-record sub-class: a corrupt-AGENT record reaching `a["name"]` hard-subscripts in the roster GET + every agent CRUD verb. **Audited.** LIVE-PROBE: bridge UP `:8767`, `/api/ping` `{ok:true, uptime_seconds:6651}` (~1.8h — **the running process RESTARTED since #102** [was ~234029s/~65h, predating #69–#102]; the #69–#102 deliverable/lifecycle backlog + the #93→96 dispatcher arc + #101 sweep isolation + #102 link-normalization are now ALL LIVE — the long-standing "bridge restart is the highest-value unlock" is finally satisfied). Re-extracted `mc_store.py` AST into the graph cache (semantic step skipped — no LLM key, as prior runs).

**Findings — REAL GAP (the corrupt-AGENT sub-class #102 flagged as un-probed):** `list_agents()` (`mc_store.py:1718`) returned the raw on-disk list with NO per-member shape normalization (`return data if isinstance(data, list) else []`). The safe consumers use `a.get("name")` (`diagnostics`'s roster set `:536`, `escalate_exhausted`-feeding `:764`/`:802`, the sweep reassign set `:1513`) — but those `.get()` calls THEMSELVES `AttributeError` on a non-dict member (a bare string/None in `agents.json`). Worse, the **roster GET** `agents_with_counts()` (`:1728-1733`, served by `STORE`-backed `/api/mc/agents`) and **every agent CRUD verb** — `get_agent` (`:1741`), `create_agent` (`:1746`), `update_agent` (`:1757`), `delete_agent` (`:1782`) — HARD-subscript `a["name"]`, so a single name-less or non-dict entry from a hand-edit / partial write of `agents.json` `KeyError`/`TypeError`/`AttributeError`s and 500s the entire roster panel + all agent management. This is the exact corrupt-record class as #101 (links) / #102 (links root cause), one layer up on the agent surface, and the LAST sub-class #102's Next-Targets left un-probed. `assignees()` (`:483`, synthesizes `name` from `.get("assignee")`) and `_dead_agents` (`:698`, works off the passed roster-set + task `.get`) are internally CLEAN — the risk is purely the un-normalized `list_agents` source.

**Fix (file:line).** `mc_store.py` — `list_agents()` (`:1718`) now normalizes at the load boundary (same discipline as #102's `_clean_links`/`_meta`): after the `isinstance(data, list)` guard it returns only members that are `dict` AND have a non-blank `str` "name" (`isinstance(a.get("name"), str) and a["name"].strip()`). One normalization defends EVERY consumer at once (roster GET + all CRUD + the `.get("name")` sweep/diagnostic sets) and self-heals the file on the next `_save_agents` (create/update/delete persist the filtered list — a name-less/non-dict member can never represent a usable agent, so dropping it is correct).

**Verified.** `py_compile` GREEN. Standalone integration test (real `MCStore` in a temp dir, corrupt `agents.json` = `['just-a-string', {'role':'researcher'}, {'name':None,...}, {'name':'   '}, {'name':'scout',...valid}, None]`): pre-fix `agents_with_counts`'s `a["name"]` raised `TypeError`/`AttributeError` (confirmed by re-running the old comprehension against the same list); post-fix `list_agents`/`agents_with_counts`/`get_agent` all return cleanly keeping ONLY `scout`, `create_agent`/`update_agent`/`delete_agent` self-heal the file to `['scout']` while preserving the rename's `role`, and the `{a.get("name")}` roster set no longer admits `None`/garbage. `npm run build` GREEN (Python-only change; no TS touched). Patch note iter-103 (lifecycle/medium) appended. Live-DOM deferred (Vite preview still blocked by space-containing parent cwd).

One normalization defends EVERY consumer at once (`diagnostics`/`show_task`/`_would_cycle`/`_cycle_nodes`/cascade/promote/sweep) and self-heals the persisted file on the next `_save_meta` (a wrong-shape entry can never represent a real edge, so dropping it is correct — distinct from a dangling link, which keeps its `missing_dependency` diagnostic).

### 2026-06-22 — Iteration #100 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [bridge UP `:8767`, `/api/mc/health` `cli_ok:true`/`claude` 2.1.183/uptime ~61h [219637s], board `{done 37, archived 1}` all-terminal, `oldest_ready_age_seconds:null` — running process STILL predates #69–#100], then executed #99's Next-Targets (b): the PRIMARY↔FALLBACK PARITY thread — GREP'd the stores for the `try { await getX() } catch { …derive client-side… }` shape and audited each fallback's projected fields against its bridge handler.)
- **SCOPE:** Per #99's (b), scoped via /graphify (`query` located the 3 named candidates: `useLeadStore` `:93`, `useGhostStore` `:145`, `useBriefingStore` `:22`) and read all three end-to-end. **All three are SINGLE-PATH, not the dual-path shape the thread targets:** `useLeadStore.fetchLeads` derives leads from `getMcAgents` only (no preferred-GET + degraded fallback; its `sumKeys` bucket logic already swept #63/#64/#80); `useBriefingStore.refresh`/`refreshSentinel` call `getMcBriefing`/`getSentinelDigest` and on failure just set `error`/`sentinelError` (no client derivation); `useGhostStore.fetchTopology` likewise derives from `getMcAgents` with no fallback. So item (b)'s named candidates are **DRY** for this lens — confirmed by `grep catch src/stores/*` that the ONLY store with a genuine `getContentPipeline()` → `catch` → derive-from-kanban dual path is `useContentStore` (the #99 store). Applied the thread's own RULE ("enumerate EVERY projected field — status set, platform code, date basis, dedup key — and confirm the fallback computes it identically to the bridge handler") to that one true dual-path store, since #99 only closed the *drafts status set*.
- **THE BUG (deliverable/lifecycle-visibility — medium; the date-basis sibling of the #99 drafts-status + #18/#43 platform/date stragglers):** `get_content_pipeline` derives each kanban CALENDAR entry's `date` as `_extract_date(title+" "+body)` FIRST — an explicit date written into the task text — falling back to `created_at` only when none is found (`mission-control-bridge.py:2346-2348`). But `useContentStore.refresh`'s client fallback calendar always used `isoDate(t.created_at)` (`:150` pre-fix), NEVER honoring an explicit date. So a content task whose title encodes its target date (e.g. "Launch post 2026-07-15") showed on 2026-07-15 via the normal pipeline GET but **jumped to its CREATION day on the degraded fallback path** — landing on the wrong calendar cell or dropping out of ContentFactory's UPCOMING filter, purely based on whether one HTTP call succeeded. Exact "different result depending on whether the GET succeeded" class the same file's `platformFor()` (`:48-53`) and `isoDate()` (`:72-82`) comments call out as already-fixed siblings; the calendar date-basis was the un-migrated straggler.
- **FIX (`src/stores/useContentStore.ts`, 1 file):** added an `extractDate(text)` helper that mirrors the backend `_extract_date` EXACTLY — `/(\d{4}-\d{2}-\d{2})/` (ISO, checked first) else `/(\d{2}\/\d{2}\/\d{4})/` reordered MM/DD/YYYY→`${yyyy}-${mm}-${dd}` else `null` — and changed the fallback calendar projection to `date: extractDate(\`${t.title} ${t.body ?? ''}\`) ?? isoDate(t.created_at)`. Same regexes + same precedence as the bridge, so both paths extract identically (even an identically-"mis"-parsed date is parity, which is the goal); when no explicit date exists it still falls to the local-YMD `isoDate(created_at)` already aligned with ContentFactory's LOCAL `upcoming` boundary (#43). **Intentionally did NOT touch the platform keyword-set divergence** I also found (client `platformFor` matches `reel`/`tweet`/`thread`/`video`/`article`/`seo`; backend `_detect_platform` doesn't) — aligning it risks substring false-positives on the PRIMARY path ("f**reel**ance"→IG, "p**article**"→WEB) for low badge-label value; logged under Next Targets/Systemic Threads as a known residual, not fixed.
- **VERIFIED:** standalone Node parity harness (`extractDate` on 6 cases: ISO-in-title, US MM/DD/YYYY→YYYY-MM-DD reorder, none→null, ISO-wins-when-both-present, no-date, embedded-date) → **6/6 PASS**. `npm run build` GREEN (tsc -b + vite, 925ms; chunk-size warning pre-existing). `npx eslint src/stores/useContentStore.ts` → No issues found. Patch note iter-100 (deliverable/medium) prepended + JSON validated (100 notes, newest-first). **Could NOT live-verify the degraded path in-browser** — it renders only when the pipeline GET fails while the tasks GET succeeds (rare; all-terminal board has no dated content task to exercise it), and Vite-preview DOM is still blocked by the space-containing parent cwd. Covered by build+lint+the static parity harness against the live-correct backend regexes.

### 2026-06-21 — Iteration #94 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [bridge UP `:8767`, `/api/mc/health` `cli_ok:true`/`claude` 2.1.183/uptime ~49h, board `{done 37, archived 1}` all-terminal — no live lifecycle to chase; running process still predates #69–#94], then executed the iter-#93 Next-Targets (b) DIRECT FOLLOW-ON — closed the VISIBILITY HALF of the iter-#93 dispatcher fix.)
- **SCOPE:** /graphify fast-path query scoped the dispatcher/escalation seam, then deep-read `mc_store.py` `_retry_budget`/`_failed_attempts`/`diagnostics()`/`escalate_exhausted`/`dispatchable_tasks` + the bridge daemon (`TaskDispatcher._loop`→`dispatch_task`) + the sweep macro + the OperationsCenter DIAGNOSTICS consumer.
- **THE GAP (lifecycle/visibility — medium):** iter-#93 made the autonomous dispatcher STOP re-firing a doomed task after `DEFAULT_DISPATCH_ATTEMPTS` (3) via `dispatchable_tasks(skip_exhausted=True)` using `ceiling = _retry_budget(t) or DEFAULT_DISPATCH_ATTEMPTS`. But the two surfaces that make a stuck task VISIBLE/actionable — the `retry_exhausted` diagnostic (`mc_store.py:531`) and `escalate_exhausted` (`:927`) — were BOTH still gated on `budget is not None` (i.e. an explicit `max_retries`, which most tasks DON'T set). So a budget-unset doomed task was parked in `ready` by the dispatcher yet NEVER flagged in Board Diagnostics, NEVER counted into the SWEEP-button gate, and NEVER escalatable → it sat silently stuck. Asymmetry: dispatcher gave up at 3, but nothing downstream noticed.
- **FIX (`mc_store.py`, 1 file):** both surfaces now use the SAME effective ceiling `_retry_budget(t) or DEFAULT_DISPATCH_ATTEMPTS` as the dispatcher — (1) `diagnostics()` retry block (`:538`) drops the `budget is not None` guard, computes `ceiling`, flags `retry_exhausted` at `attempts >= ceiling`; (2) `escalate_exhausted` (`:927`) computes `ceiling`, drops the `budget is not None` term from `exhausted`, reports `attempts/ceiling` in the reason + `max_retries: ceiling` in the entry & `escalated` event, and removes the now-dead "no retry budget (max_retries unset)" skip branch. Explicit-budget tasks are UNCHANGED (ceiling == their budget). LIFE-3 holds: escalate's block path already stamps `completed_at = _now()` (`:961`) on the shared branch — the new default-ceiling path reuses it.
- **VERIFIED:** (1) `py_compile mc_store.py` OK. (2) standalone 15-assertion test (temp-root `MCStore`, real `create_task`/`record_task_run`/`diagnostics`/`escalate_exhausted`) — ALL PASS: budget-unset <3 fails NOT flagged/escalated; ==3 fails NOW diagnosed AND escalated→blocked WITH reason (no `blocked_no_reason`) + `completed_at` stamped (LIFE-3) + `max_retries`==ceiling; explicit budget 5 unchanged (3 fails not flagged, skip-reason shows `/5`); explicit budget 2 still works; done task never escalated. (3) SYMMETRY proof: stepping fails 0→3, the dispatcher's `dispatchable(skip_exhausted)` flips to False at EXACTLY the same fail count (3) the task becomes escalatable→True — lock-step, no gap. (4) `npm run build` GREEN (frontend untouched; chunk-size warning pre-existing). Live-DOM deferred (board all-terminal; running bridge predates the route — same standing blocker as #69–#93).

### 2026-06-21 — Iteration #93 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [bridge UP `:8767`, health `cli_ok:true`/`claude` 2.1.183/uptime ~47h, board `{done 37, archived 1}`, `oldest_ready_age_seconds:null` — all-terminal, no live lifecycle to chase], then executed the iter-#92 Next-Targets (b) lead — opened the two never-swept operational-spine SOURCES `scripts/ensure_bridge.py` + `mc_scheduler.py`/cron-fire internals. - **SCOPE:** read the two queued SOURCES end-to-end + their seams. `mc_scheduler.py` (pure schedule-matcher, self-test passes) CLEAN; `scripts/ensure_bridge.py` CLEAN — its `GET /api/ping` probe is real (`mission-control-bridge.py:673`, live-200), so the watchdog never false-relaunches / double-binds `:8767`. - **THE BUG (lifecycle/quota — high):** the autonomous **task dispatcher** (`TaskDispatcher._loop` → `dispatch_task`, `mission-control-bridge.py:583`/`:490`; enabled in production via `ensure_bridge.py` `MC_DISPATCHER_ENABLED=1`) requeues a FAILED task to `ready` (`dispatch_task` `:518`) so it can be retried. But the picker `STORE.dispatchable_tasks` (`mc_store.py:1110`) offered ANY `ready`+assigned task with NO regard to how many times it had already failed — so a task that can never succeed (bad prompt, agent model quota out, impossible work) was re-fired through a FULL `run_claude` turn EVERY dispatcher tick (default 30s), forever, silently burning Claude quota + cost. The existing retry backstop (`escalate_exhausted` `:887`, the `retry_exhausted` diagnostic `:525`) is gated on `budget is not None` — i.e. it ONLY acts on tasks with an explicit `max_retries`, and `_blank_task`/`create_task` default `max_retries=None` (`:144`), so the COMMON dashboard task had NO ceiling at all and no escalation ever fired. This is the Claude-era instance of the documented kanban retry-loop quota-burn class (memory: hermes-kimi-quota-burn).
- **FIX (`mc_store.py` + 1 daemon call site, 2 files):** added `DEFAULT_DISPATCH_ATTEMPTS` (env `MC_DISPATCH_MAX_ATTEMPTS`, default 3) and a `skip_exhausted: bool=False` param to `dispatchable_tasks`. When set, it drops any task whose `_failed_attempts` ≥ `(_retry_budget(t) or DEFAULT_DISPATCH_ATTEMPTS)` — reusing the SAME failed-attempt counter the escalate verb uses. The autonomous daemon passes `skip_exhausted=True` (`mission-control-bridge.py:593`); the **manual** dispatch endpoint + dry-run preview leave it OFF (`:1381`/`:1396`) so an operator can ALWAYS force a re-run by hand and tasks with an explicit `max_retries` still honor their own budget. `dispatchable_tasks` stays read-only (mutates nothing) — the loop is broken by not OFFERING the doomed task, not by mutating it. A task that hits the ceiling now sits visibly in `ready` (no longer fake-busy flickering ready↔running) instead of bleeding quota.
- **VERIFIED:** (1) `python -m py_compile mc_store.py mission-control-bridge.py mc_scheduler.py` OK. (2) `python mc_scheduler.py` self-test ALL PASS (untouched, regression guard). ### 2026-06-21 — Iteration #92 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [bridge UP `:8767`, health `cli_ok:true`/`claude` 2.1.183, board `{done 37, archived 1}`, `oldest_ready_age_seconds:null` — all-terminal, no live lifecycle to chase], then executed the iter-#91 Next-Targets (b) lead — apply the **DELIVERABLE-DESTROY-ON-FAILURE** lens to the LAST un-swept aggregated-artifact producer, `generate_ai_digest`. Found + fixed the present high-impact 3rd instance of the thread.)
- **SCOPE:** targeted read of the precisely-named handoff target rather than a blind grep — `generate_ai_digest` (`mission-control-bridge.py:3169`, `POST /api/mc/ai-digest`) + its chokepoint `_llm_json` (`:3252`) + `claude_json` (`mc_brain.py:175`). Ran `graphify update .` after the edit (2123 nodes / 3913 edges / 103 communities).
- **THE BUG (deliverable-integrity — high; 3rd instance of DELIVERABLE-DESTROY-ON-FAILURE after #90 sentinel + #91 creators-feed):** the consolidated AI Digest (`ai-digest` store; one-paragraph news summary + viral content ideas, served by `GET /api/mc/ai-digest`) is synthesized by Claude and persisted with `_save_store("ai-digest", digest)` (`:3207` pre-fix). The HARD-failure paths are already guarded — `latest.json` missing → 404 (`:3175`), no stories → 404 (`:3178`), and a true LLM failure (ClaudeError / quota / non-object JSON) raises 502/503 inside `_llm_json` (`:3257-3266`) BEFORE the save. But a **degenerate-yet-well-formed** reply is NOT: `claude_json` happily `json.loads`-es an empty `{}` (`mc_brain.py:203`), and `_llm_json` WRAPS a bare JSON array into `{"items": […]}` (`:3262-3264`) — both pass the dict check yet carry NO `summary`/`ideas`. So `parsed.get("summary","")==""` + `(parsed.get("ideas") or [])==[]` → `digest` is a content-free shell `{summary:"", ideas:[], story_count:N}` that was SAVED unconditionally, CLOBBERING the last-good served digest. The operator's AI Digest panel goes blank though a good one existed (GET only re-shows whatever's cached). Sibling `sync_metricool_brands` (`:2763`) is guarded (empty→502 before save, confirmed #91); this one was the gap.
- **THE DISCRIMINATOR:** the guard keys on CONTENT, not the raw `parsed` shape — a digest is worth saving iff it carries a non-blank `summary` OR at least one idea. `has_summary = isinstance(digest["summary"], str) and digest["summary"].strip()` (also defends a non-string summary from an `AttributeError`); `not has_summary and not digest["ideas"]` ⇒ empty synthesis ⇒ do NOT clobber. A real digest with EITHER a summary OR ≥1 idea still saves normally (no false-preserve).
- **FIX (`mission-control-bridge.py:3207-3214`, 1 file):** before `_save_store`, if the synthesized digest is content-empty, `raise HTTPException(502, "LLM returned an empty digest — kept the previous one; retry")`. The raise precedes the save, so the prior good `ai-digest` cache is untouched and `GET /api/mc/ai-digest` keeps serving it; the operator gets an actionable retry signal instead of a silently-blanked panel. Mirrors #90/#91 (preserve last-good on failure) and the `sync_metricool_brands` empty→502 pattern.
- **VERIFIED:** (1) `python -m py_compile mission-control-bridge.py` OK. (2) Standalone 7-case behavioral harness replicating the post-`_llm_json` save-guard (incl. `_llm_json`'s bare-array→`{"items":…}` wrap): empty `{}`, explicit nulls, whitespace-only summary, bare-array drift → ALL preserve the prior cache (raise 502, cache intact); summary-only, ideas-only, full digest → ALL save — 7/7 PASS. (3) `npm run build` GREEN (tsc -b + vite, pre-existing chunk-size warning only; no frontend files touched). Could NOT live-verify against the running bridge: a true repro needs the LLM to actually emit an empty/array reply (non-deterministic) and the process predates this edit (uptime ~45h, restart declined — live operator service); relied on py_compile + the behavioral harness + the confirmed `claude_json`/`_llm_json` shape contract.

- **THE BUG (deliverable-integrity — high; exact sibling of iter-#90, the DELIVERABLE-DESTROY-ON-FAILURE thread):** `scrape_creators` (`POST /api/creators/scrape`) loops Instagram+TikTok via Apify; each `_http_json` failure is swallowed into `errors` (`:3120`). On a transient ALL-platform outage (Apify down / 429 / network) every fetch raises → `items == []`, yet the function called `_save_store("creators-feed", feed)` UNCONDITIONALLY (`:3138` pre-fix), overwriting the last-good viral feed with `{items:[], errors:[…]}`. Both consumers then go blank: `ContentFactory.handleScrape` calls `loadCreators()` (`ContentFactory.tsx:355`) and the Intelligence Deck's VIRAL FEED panel (iter-#89) re-reads the now-empty persisted feed — the deliverable is LOST until the next successful scrape. Unlike #90's sentinel (re-run only when cache ABSENT), this re-runs on demand, so it's not *permanent* poisoning — but every outage still wipes the operator's last good feed.
- **THE DISCRIMINATOR (why a naive `if not items` is wrong):** `items` also legitimately becomes `[]` when a platform RESPONDS but all posts are filtered by the `RECENCY_MAX_AGE_DAYS` floor (`:3104`) — a GENUINE empty result that SHOULD overwrite (stale week-old posts must not linger). So the guard keys on whether any source actually returned data, not on emptiness alone: added `fetched_any` (`:3066`), set True right after a successful `_http_json` (`:3087`). Only `not items and not fetched_any` = true total outage.
- **FIX (`mission-control-bridge.py:3066/3087/3137`, 1 file):** (a) init `fetched_any = False`; (b) set it True on each source that responds; (c) before the unconditional save, if `not items and not fetched_any`, load the prior `creators-feed` and — when it has items — re-save it with THIS run's `errors` merged in (`{**prior, "errors": errors}`) and return it, so the last-good feed survives AND the deck's error banner + ContentFactory's "done with errors" message still fire. No prior good feed → falls through and saves the empty+errors feed (nothing is lost). Happy path + genuine-empty path byte-identical to before.

Fix preserves "save before any decorative/​non-ASCII print" and makes the new empty-path message ASCII-only.

- **Fresh-surface sweep (both DRAINED clean this run):** (1) **transcribe/TTS** — `/api/transcribe` (`mission-control-bridge.py:2113`) cleans its temp clip in a `finally`, validates base64/empty, maps every failure to a real HTTP code; `/api/tts` (`:2528`) caps chars, surfaces ElevenLabs HTTP errors, returns real MP3 bytes; the never-swept frontend voice machine `useVoiceLink.ts` is ref-guarded (alive/phase checks across every await), revokes object URLs, tears down on unmount/Esc, and the spoken turn lands in the shared chat store so the deliverable persists even if TTS fails; `ChatTerminal.tsx` transcribe drops the text into the visible input box. (2) **content-calendar/Metricool** — `add_calendar_item` draft-retain (#84) is real AND visible+retryable: `/api/content/pipeline` synthesizes `planned:true` on every stored item so the ⏱/📎/🔮 buttons render, and ContentFactory auto-refreshes every 30s; `schedule_calendar_item`/`predict_calendar_virality`/`_metricool_schedule`/`_metricool_mcp`/`_llm_json`/`claude_json`/`run_claude` all checked — robust (proper error mapping, no lost-on-failure mutations, careful JSON extraction). No NEW bug on either fresh surface — recorded as DRAINED.
- **THE BUG (security / bug-high — arbitrary `*.json` file read, remotely triggerable):** `get_sentinel_digest_by_date` (`GET /api/sentinel/digest/{date}`, `mission-control-bridge.py:3508`) interpolated the `{date}` path-param straight into `SENTINEL_CACHE_DIR / f"digest_{date}.json"` with NO validation. FastAPI captures URL-encoded `\` into `{date}`, and Windows collapses `..` lexically even through the glued `digest_` prefix (`digest_x\..\..\..` cancels back out of the cache dir), so a crafted date escapes `.mc/cache/sentinel` and reads any `*.json` on disk. With `CORS_ORIGINS` defaulting to `*` + `allow_methods=["*"]` + `allow_credentials=False` (`:36`/`:659`), any page in the operator's browser can issue the GET **and read the response cross-origin** → drive-by exfiltration of arbitrary local JSON (config/secrets/`.mc/data/*`). Sibling `serve_media` (`:2894`) already sanitizes its path-param; this was the lone unguarded instance.
- **FIX (minimal, parity with `serve_media`):** added `if not re.fullmatch(r"[0-9][0-9_-]{0,31}", date): raise HTTPException(404, ...)` before the path build (`mission-control-bridge.py:3508`), pinning `date` to the digit/dash vocabulary real `digest_YYYY-MM-DD.json` names use. `re` already imported. Returns the same 404 the not-found path already used, so the only legit caller (the `/api/sentinel/archive` date list) is unaffected.
- **VERIFIED:** (1) `py_compile` GREEN. (2) standalone harness — 5 real date forms all PASS the guard, 13 attack vectors (`x\..\..\..\Users\...`, `..`, `../../etc/passwd`, `C:\Windows\foo`, `2026-06-21.json`, 40×`a`, empty, …) all BLOCKED. (3) **LIVE pre-fix PoC** on the running (old-code) bridge: `GET /api/sentinel/digest/x%5C..%5C..%5C..%5C..%5Cpackage` returned the repo-root `package.json` body (a file 3 levels OUTSIDE the cache dir) while a normal date `2099-01-01` correctly `404`s — the exact arbitrary-read the guard removes. Could NOT live-verify the FIXED path (running process predates this edit; no unilateral restart per loop rules) — after a restart that same `x\..\..` request `404`s. (4) `npm run build` GREEN (tsc -b + vite, 163 modules; backend-only change, no FE delta).

'warn' : 'good'`, `Systems.tsx:73-75/212-216`) gated its first check on `bool(ver and "Claude" in ver or re.search(r"\d", ver or ""))` where `ver = claude_version()`. The `claude` CLI is now THE backend brain (every agent runs through `run_claude`), so a doctor that can never fail this check tells the operator the brain is healthy even when it's dead — the worst lie for the command center's operational spine. Same swallowed/masked-error family the iter-#85 Next-Targets flagged for `mc_diag`.
- **FIX (1 file, backend, `mc_diag.py:191-196`):** probe the CLI directly — `ver = _run("--version", timeout=10)` (NO fallback) — and gate on `bool(ver and ("claude" in ver.lower() or re.search(r"\d", ver)))`. Now: missing/broken CLI → `''` → check FAILS, text reads `claude CLI: not found`, the Systems diagnostics stat flips to a red ✗ / warn tone; a real `claude --version` ("1.0.88 (Claude Code)" / bare "2.3.1") still passes; shell noise ("command not found", no digit/claude) correctly fails. `claude_version()` itself is untouched (its forgiving fallback is correct for the `overview`/`/api/mc/version` display surfaces — only the doctor needed a strict probe).

- **THE BUG (ui/low) — "Invalid Date" leaks into chat message headers:** `ChatTerminal.tsx:247` `formatTime` wrapped `new Date(iso).toLocaleTimeString(...)` in a try/catch intending a `--:--` fallback. But **`toLocaleTimeString()` does NOT throw on an unparseable date — it returns the literal string `"Invalid Date"`** (Node-confirmed), so the catch is dead for the realistic failure mode. `msgTime()` (`useChatStore.ts:111`) passes ANY non-empty string timestamp through **verbatim, unvalidated** ("keep an already-ISO string as-is" — but it never checks it parses), so a non-ISO bridge/session stamp (schema drift, hand-edited cache, a space/locale format `new Date` rejects) renders "Invalid Date" in every message header instead of the clean placeholder. This is the iter-#82 `safeStamp` class — the `toLocale*` variant, where a try/catch is the WRONG guard.
- **FIX (1 file):** `formatTime` now does `const d = new Date(iso); if (Number.isNaN(d.getTime())) return '--:--';` before formatting (try/catch kept as belt-and-suspenders). Mirrors iter-#82 `safeStamp`.

**The fix (`useLeadStore.ts:57`):** added `'review', 'scheduled', 'triage'` to the `queue` `sumKeys` (kept `queued`/`pending` as defensive legacy aliases), bringing it byte-for-byte in lock-step with the iter-#79 `useGhostStore.mapAgentsToTopology` queue set; terminal/adverse `done`/`completed`/`archived`/`failed` stay excluded. Replaced the bare line with a documenting comment stating the rule + why (matching the #79 `useGhostStore` comment style). Surgical 1-line logic change.
