### 2026-06-20 — Iteration #78 (focus: drained the iter-#77 Next-Targets "un-swept backend: sessions/transcribe/scrape_creators/metricool" lead with the deliverable-integrity + swallowed-error lens. Swept all four; three are CLEAN; found + fixed a PRESENT silent-lost-deliverable on the chat/sessions path.)

**Swept the four iter-#77-flagged un-swept verbs first (graphify-scoped, not blind-grepped):** `transcribe` (`:2097`) — CLEAN, raises precise HTTPExceptions (503 not-installed / 500 load-fail / 400 bad-base64 / 500 transcribe-fail) and unlinks the temp file in `finally`. `scrape_creators` (`:3023`) — robust: per-platform failures are accumulated into a surfaced `errors[]` list (good pattern) and `_http_json` (`:2459`) wraps EVERY exception (incl. non-HTTPError) into an HTTPException so the `except HTTPException` catch covers all network faults; the only residual is a non-dict Apify item escaping the catch (low-probability, latent — left). `_metricool_brand`/`_metricool_schedule`/`sync_metricool_brands` (`:2675`–`2746`) + `_metricool_mcp` — CLEAN, every MCP/HTTP failure raises a 502/400 with `detail`. `sessions_list`/`session_get`/`rename`/`delete` (`:2015`–`2041`) — CLEAN thin delegates (404 on missing).

**The bug (PRESENT, silent lost-deliverable — DELIV class, sessions area):** `chat_message` (`:1895`) persisted the chat turn only under `if sid:` where `sid = resp.get("session_id") or payload.session_id`. `run_claude` (`mc_brain.py:75`) returns `session_id = envelope.get("session_id") or session_id`, and its `--output-format json` parse FALLS BACK to `{"result": stdout}` (`mc_brain.py:150-153`) when the CLI emits non-JSON stdout — that fallback envelope has NO `session_id`. So on a brand-new chat (no `payload.session_id`) whose reply came through the fallback, `sid` is empty and the WHOLE turn (operator message + assistant answer) was silently dropped from the SQLite sessions store: the reply still rendered inline, but the conversation never appeared in the sessions list / transcript view (`GET /api/mc/sessions`, `/sessions/{id}`) — a lost deliverable (the chat transcript) with zero warning.

**The fix (`mission-control-bridge.py:1938`):** removed the `if sid:` gate. When `sid` is empty, persist under a fabricated local id `f"local-{uuid.uuid4().hex[:16]}"` (`import uuid` is file-local style, matching `:2559/2810/2846`) so the transcript ALWAYS reaches its retrievable home. Deliberately do NOT hand that fabricated id back as the response `session_id` (kept `"session_id": sid`) — returning a non-claude id would make the next turn's `claude --resume <local-…>` 502, converting a silent-loss into a broken conversation; instead the conversation just continues fresh while every turn is preserved (worst case: per-turn session fragments, nothing lost, nothing breaks). Normal-path behavior (real session id present) is byte-identical.

**Verified:** `python -m py_compile mission-control-bridge.py` OK. Standalone 3-case proof against the REAL `MCSessions` store (mc_brain): (1) no-session-id new chat → transcript now PRESERVED under a `local-…` id, response `session_id` stays None, auto-title from first user msg, 2 messages retrievable via `.get()` + visible in `.list()` [BEFORE-FIX this turn was LOST]; (2) real session id → persisted under the real id, unchanged; (3) resume existing → appends (4 msgs), no fabricated id. `npm run build` GREEN (`tsc -b` + vite; only the pre-existing >500 kB chunk warning). Backend-only change, no JS lint surface touched. NOT live-verified end-to-end: the running `:8767` predates the edit AND the degraded no-session-id path can't be forced without a real CLI fault — the standalone store test is the proof. Patch note iter-78 (deliverable/medium) added.

**Files touched:** `mission-control-bridge.py` (`chat_message` persistence un-gated + local-id fallback), `.mc/patch-notes.json` (iter-78), `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry + Next Targets + Focus-Area Rotation), `graphify-out/*` (ran `graphify update .`). No commit/push (loop rules; inherited churn left intact).

### 2026-06-20 — Iteration #77 (focus: executed the iter-#76 Next-Targets #2 BACKEND counterpart — the natural sibling #76 just unblocked. With the frontend now reading FastAPI `detail` via `bridgeDetail`, surfaced the REAL reason the Sentinel digest is missing instead of always telling the operator to "wait for next cycle". Swallowed-error / reason-hiding class on the live deliverable path.)

**The bug (PRESENT, reason-hiding / swallowed-error — LIFE-1/#11 + #76 class):** the two Sentinel-fetch endpoints `get_sentinel_digest` (`/api/sentinel/digest`, `:3424`) and its alias `get_mc_sentinel` (`/api/mc/sentinel`, `:3390`) were near-identical: if `latest.json` was absent they ran the `scripts/sentinel_news_pipeline.py` subprocess wrapped in `except Exception: pass`, then — if `latest.json` was STILL absent — raised the SAME 404 "No digest available. Run the Sentinel cron or wait for next cycle." So a genuinely BROKEN scrape (non-zero exit, timeout, or crash) was indistinguishable from a benign "no digest produced yet" — the operator was told to WAIT when waiting would never help. The subprocess `returncode`/`stderr` were captured by `subprocess.run(capture_output=True)` and then thrown away by the bare `except: pass`.

**The fix (`mission-control-bridge.py`):** extracted a shared `_load_sentinel_digest()` helper (`:3403`, placed right after `SENTINEL_CACHE_DIR`) that kills the near-duplication and adds a three-way outcome: (1) **502** "Sentinel pipeline failed — <reason>" when the pipeline actually RAN and FAILED — non-zero exit carries `exit <rc>: <last 400 chars of stderr/stdout>`, a `TimeoutExpired` carries "pipeline timed out after 120s", any other crash carries `str(e)`; (2) **404** "wait for next cycle" reserved ONLY for the benign case (pipeline exited 0 with no data, OR no script present — nothing failed); (3) **500** unchanged for a present-but-unparseable `latest.json`. A cached `latest.json` short-circuits to 200 before the subprocess ever runs (preserved). Both endpoints now just `return _load_sentinel_digest()`. The 502 `detail` reaches the Briefing Terminal's Sentinel panel via #76's `bridgeDetail` (`useBriefingStore.refreshSentinel` → `sentinelError`).

**Verified:** `python -m py_compile mission-control-bridge.py` OK; both call sites resolve (`:3393`, `:3455`). Standalone 8-branch replica proof of the exact decision logic: cached-hit→200 (subprocess never runs), ran-ok-wrote→200, ran-ok-**nodata**→**404** (benign wait preserved — the key non-regression), ran-failed→502+stderr, ran-timeout→502+timeout, ran-crash→502+reason, no-script→404, parse-fail→500 — all as intended. `npm run build` GREEN (`tsc -b` + vite; only the pre-existing >500 kB chunk warning). Backend-only change, no JS lint surface touched. NOT live-verified end-to-end: the running `:8767` predates this fix and currently serves a cached digest (200), so the 502 branch isn't triggerable without a bridge RESTART (not done — won't disrupt a live operator process autonomously). Patch note iter-77 (lifecycle/medium) added.

**Files touched:** `mission-control-bridge.py` (new `_load_sentinel_digest` helper + both endpoints delegate to it), `.mc/patch-notes.json` (iter-77), `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry + Next Targets + Focus-Area Rotation), `graphify-out/*` (ran `graphify update .`). No commit/push (loop rules; inherited churn left intact).

### 2026-06-20 — Iteration #76 (focus: executed the iter-#75 Next-Targets #2 FRONTEND lead — a lifecycle-visibility sweep of the never-this-cycle-swept Briefing/Sentinel store with the "is the reason VISIBLE?" lens. Found + fixed a PRESENT, live-board reason-hiding bug: the Briefing Terminal's daily-briefing AND Sentinel-digest panels swallowed the bridge's ACTIONABLE HTTPException `detail` and showed the operator a useless "Request failed with status code 404" instead.)

**The bug (PRESENT, live-board, reason-hiding — LIFE-1/#11 class):** `src/stores/useBriefingStore.ts` caught both `getMcBriefing()` (`refresh`, L41) and `getSentinelDigest()` (`refreshSentinel`, L58) with `errMessage(err)`, which for an axios error returns only the generic `e.message` ("Request failed with status code 404/500/502") and DISCARDS the FastAPI `detail`. The bridge's `/api/sentinel/digest` (`:3424`) and `/api/mc/sentinel` (`:3390`) deliberately raise 404 with an actionable detail — "No digest available. Run the Sentinel cron or wait for next cycle." — that the operator NEVER saw. The reason a deliverable (the briefing / AI daily digest) was missing was hidden behind a meaningless status string.

**The fix (`src/stores/useBriefingStore.ts`):** swapped both catch blocks `errMessage(err)` → `bridgeDetail(err)` (the existing helper that extracts FastAPI `detail`/`stderr` and gracefully falls back to `e.message`), updated the import (`errMessage`→`bridgeDetail`; errMessage was now unused — tsc would have errored otherwise), added a one-line comment on the `refresh` block. This is the BINDING CONSTRAINT for any backend sentinel-error surfacing: the queued backend `except Exception: pass` distinction (see Next Targets) stays invisible until the frontend reads `detail` — which it now does.

**Verified:** `npm run build` GREEN (`tsc -b` passes → no unused-import error, types sound). `npx eslint src/stores/useBriefingStore.ts` → No issues found. Standalone Node proof with the project's REAL `axios`: a 404 AxiosError carrying `{detail:"No digest available…"}` → OLD `errMessage` = "Request failed with status code 404", NEW `bridgeDetail` = "No digest available. Run the Sentinel cron or wait for next cycle."; a detail-less 500 AxiosError AND a non-axios `Error` both produce IDENTICAL output under both helpers (no regression on the fallback paths). ### 2026-06-19 — Iteration #71 (focus: backend cron-engine `mc_scheduler.py` was flagged "never swept end-to-end" — swept it + `mc_brain.py` + all 5 `src/lib` analytics modules + the notify path; all mature/CLEAN except ONE genuine remaining instance of the recurring **cron-parser lock-step divergence** (#27/#28/#58 class), this time in the TS `expandField` `parseInt` leniency vs the daemon's strict Python `int()`.)

**Audited.** Scoped via the /graphify existing-graph fast path (`graphify query "mc_scheduler cron engine …"`). Swept the never-end-to-end-swept cron engine **`mc_scheduler.py`** (parse_cron / `_expand_field` / parse_interval_seconds / `_cron_matches` / is_due / is_fireable / due_jobs) + its seam in the bridge daemon (`CronScheduler._loop`/`_fire`, `:360-399`) + `mc_store` cron verbs (`create_cron`/`mark_cron_run`/`record_cron_result`/`_next_run`, `:1709-1861`). Also swept **`mc_brain.py`** (`run_claude` error contract + `claude_json` JSON-extraction regex — robust: the non-greedy fenced `\{.*?\}` is anchored by the trailing ``` ``` so it reaches the right brace; the greedy fallback handles nesting) and all 5 **`src/lib`** analytics modules (cycleTime / agingWip / taskThroughput / backlogTrend / agentMetrics — all clean) + the notify path (`TaskNotifier.tsx` / `useNotifyStore.ts` — clean). NON-FINDINGS worth recording: (a) the daemon records `ok=True` after a claude `run_claude` (`:393`) — CORRECT, because `run_claude` RAISES on any failure (caught → `ok=False`), never returns a failed result; (b) `is_due`'s `job["repeat"]` schedule-fallback is intentional & consistent with the frontend (`CronTimeline`/`OperationsCenter` both read `schedule || repeat`); (c) `_next_run` reads only `schedule` (not the `repeat` fallback) but its output is vestigial (UI computes its own countdown via `cronSchedule.ts`) → no operator impact; (d) `agentMetrics` leaves `review`/`scheduled`/`triage`/`archived` unbucketed, but `AgentPerformance.tsx` renders only done/running/failed/rate/24h (not total/ready) → invisible, not worth a metric-definition change.

**The bug (`src/lib/cronSchedule.ts` `expandField`, front — cron-parser lock-step-divergence class; PRESENT on a plausible typo).** The module's whole contract is "in lock-step with the daemon's parser so the operator's countdown and the actual fire agree." `expandField` parsed every numeric token with `parseInt`, which **silently truncates a trailing non-digit** (`parseInt('15m')===15`, `parseInt('5x')===5`), and `range.split('-')` destructuring silently drops a third hyphen-part (`'1-5-7'`→`1-5`). The daemon's `_expand_field` uses Python `int()` (raises on `'15m'`/`'5x'`) and `str.partition('-')`+`int()` (rejects `'1-5-7'`). So a fat-fingered schedule like **`*/15m * * * *`** (mixing the `every 15m` interval shorthand into a cron field — a very plausible mistake) parsed as a healthy `every 15m` cron in the UI, rendering a green next-fire countdown in the Scheduled-Jobs panel + the 24h agenda, **while the daemon rejected the same string and silently never fired the job** — the exact "looks scheduled, never runs" trap the #27/#28/#58 fixes chased (they covered `every`-spacing + unit coverage; this is the last leniency gap: `parseInt` vs `int`). Confirmed live: `mc_scheduler.schedule_kind` returns `unknown` for `*/15m`/`*/2x`/`1-5-7`/`5x` but `cron` for `+5` (Python `int('+5')` is valid).

**Fix (1 file, front).** Added a `strictInt(tok)` helper = `/^[+-]?\d+$/`-gated `parseInt` (mirrors Python `int()`: optional sign + digits, NOTHING else; keeps `'+5'` valid → then bounds-rejected, exactly like the daemon) and routed `expandField`'s step / range-bounds / bare-value parses through it; the range branch now requires **exactly two** hyphen-bounds (matches `partition`+`int`). Valid expressions (`*`, `5`, `1-5`, `*/15`, `1-10/2`, `0,30`, `+5`) parse byte-identically; malformed ones now return `null`→`kind:'unknown'` (honest "unrecognized", no fake countdown) instead of a phantom cron. **Verified:** standalone TS↔Python parity harness (`tsx`, 11 cases) — every case's `parseSchedule(...).kind` matches the live `mc_scheduler.schedule_kind` verdict (4 malformed→`unknown`, 5 valid cron→`cron`, 2 interval→`interval`), ALL PASS. `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) GREEN; `eslint src/lib/cronSchedule.ts` clean (no new issues on the touched file). Pure-logic frontend change → no bridge/DOM needed; the parity-against-the-live-daemon proof is the right verification. Patch note iter-71 added; `graphify update .` ran (2014 nodes / 3778 edges / 88 communities).

**Files touched:** `src/lib/cronSchedule.ts` (`strictInt` helper + `expandField` strict step/bounds/value parsing), `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry + Systemic Threads + Next Targets + Focus-Area Rotation). No commit/push (loop rules; inherited churn left intact).

### 2026-06-19 — Iteration #70 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [board STILL `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` since #35], then drained the iter-#69-queued **`completed_at`-invariant lens** across the STILL-un-swept `mc_store.py` self-heal / maintenance verbs — CLOSED the symmetric counterpart of #69: the AUTO verbs that produce/revive a `blocked` task did NOT maintain `completed_at`.)

**Audited.** Re-probed the live bridge (`/api/mc/kanban/stats` `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` unchanged since #35; `oldest_ready≈10.7d`; bridge still predates the deferred unlocks → no new live state). Scoped via the /graphify existing-graph fast path. Applied the iter-#69 **`completed_at`-invariant lens** (`completed_at` set IFF the task is in an ended state done/blocked/failed; ANY verb → a non-terminal status must clear it, ANY verb → an ended status must set it) to the maintenance/self-heal verbs #69 left for the next run: `claim_task`/`reconcile_board`/`escalate_exhausted`/`route_triage`/`requeue_task`/`reassign_dead_agent`/`cascade_dependencies`/`promote_ready`/`sweep_board`. Grepped every `status"] = "blocked"/"failed"/"done"` + every `completed_at"] =` site to be exhaustive.

**The bug (`mc_store.py` `escalate_exhausted` `:947` + `cascade_dependencies` HOLD `:1355` / PROMOTE `:1366`, backend — completed_at-invariant class; LATENT-for-existing-board, PRESENT-on-trigger).** The canonical `block_task`/`fail_task` stamp `completed_at = _now()`; the revive verbs (`unblock`/`promote`/`schedule`/`requeue`, the last three fixed #69) clear it. But three **auto** paths violated the invariant: (1) `escalate_exhausted` flips a retry-burned task to `blocked` **without** stamping `completed_at`; (2) `cascade_dependencies` HOLD flips a dependency-waiting `todo`/`ready` child to `blocked` **without** stamping it; (3) `cascade_dependencies` PROMOTE revives a held child to `ready` **without** clearing it. (1)+(2) produce a `blocked` task with `completed_at=None` — `get_activity`'s terminal branch (`:920`, gated on `has_completion`) never fires, so the block surfaces only via the iter-#47/#55 *stuck* branch at the task's OLD `started_at` time instead of the block time, inconsistent with a `block_task`-blocked row (which shows at block time). (3) is the load-bearing coupling: the moment HOLD stamps `completed_at` (fix 2), a held→cleared child would carry a STALE stamp → `get_activity` emits a false GREEN "completed" row — the exact #69 bug freshly reintroduced through the cascade path. So HOLD-set and PROMOTE-clear are inseparable and ship together; `escalate` only blocks (revival is via the already-fixed manual verbs), so it needs only the set. `reconcile_board`/`route_triage`/`promote_ready`/`reassign_dead_agent` all transition only running↔ready / triage→todo / todo→ready (statuses that never carry `completed_at`) — CLEAN, no change.

**Fix (1 file, back).** `escalate_exhausted` `:947` + `cascade_dependencies` HOLD `:1355`: `t["status"] = "blocked"; t["completed_at"] = _now()` (mirror `block_task`). `cascade_dependencies` PROMOTE `:1366`: `t["status"] = "ready"; t["completed_at"] = None` (mirror `unblock_task`/#69). Comments on each tie to the invariant + LIFE-3. **Verified:** `python -m py_compile mc_store.py` OK; a standalone end-to-end proof against the REAL `MCStore` (temp root): a `block_task` reference task stamps `completed_at` (baseline); escalate of a retry-exhausted task → `blocked` + `completed_at` is a number (FIX); cascade HOLD of a child with an open parent → `blocked` + `completed_at` set (FIX); cascade PROMOTE after the parent completes → `ready` + `completed_at` is `None` (FIX, no false-green) — all 7 assertions PASS. `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) GREEN (backend-only; pre-existing >500 kB chunk warning unrelated). ### 2026-06-19 — Iteration #69 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [board STILL `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` since #35], extended the iter-#67/#68 null-guard lens to the FRONTEND [TS `?? (`requeue_task`'s only live caller is the dispatch-failure path on a `running` task [`completed_at=None`], so it's defense-in-depth there, but its docstring explicitly covers reviving a FAILED task — which carries the stamp.)

**Fix (1 file, back).** Mirror `unblock_task`'s precedent: add `t["completed_at"] = None` to `promote_task`, `schedule_task`, and `requeue_task`, with comments tying each to the invariant (a task revived to an active state is not ended). `reclaim_task`/`reassign_task(reclaim)` were left untouched — they only transition a `running` task (which never has `completed_at`), so clearing there would be dead code. **Verified:** `python -m py_compile mc_store.py` OK; a standalone end-to-end proof against the REAL `MCStore` (temp root) replicating the actual `get_activity` terminal-branch logic — create→claim→block→promote/schedule, and create→claim→fail→requeue: OLD feed = `'complete'` (false green DONE) for all three, NEW feed = `None` (no terminal row, correct), and a genuinely `complete_task`'d task still reports `'complete'` (no regression). `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) GREEN (backend-only; pre-existing >500 kB chunk warning unrelated). ### 2026-06-19 — Iteration #68 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [board STILL `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` since #35], then carried the iter-#67 **null-guard lens forward** across the Python backend — grepped every `\.get(k, {})\.`/`\.get(k, [])[...]` chained access — and CLOSED the highest-impact sibling: the LLM-synthesis endpoints crash + lose the whole run if the model returns `"ideas": null`.)

**Audited.** Re-probed the live bridge (`/api/mc/kanban/stats` `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` unchanged since #35; `oldest_ready≈10.5d`; `/api/mc/activity` serves `activities`-keyed rows — running bridge still predates the deferred-DOM/blocked-row unlocks pending an operator restart). Scoped via the /graphify existing-graph fast path (graph is coarse for Python internals, so applied the lens mechanically). **Ran the iter-#67 null-guard lens as a concrete grep across all `*.py`** (`\.get([^,)]+,\s*\{\}\)\.` and `\.get([^,)]+,\s*\[\]\)[\[.]`): 6 hits. Triaged each by whether the source can carry an **explicit `None`** (the key distinction — `.get(k, default)` only fires `default` on an ABSENT key, never on a present-but-null value): **`:3083`/`:3126`** `json.loads(latest.json).get("stories", [])[:N]` read the Sentinel cache, whose sole producer (`scripts/sentinel_news_pipeline.py:167`) always writes `"stories": deduped_trends` (a list — `len()` is called on it) — so `stories:null` has no realistic path; **defensive-only, left untouched**. **`:3637`** `data.get("metadata", {}).get("vulnerabilities", {})` already coalesces the inner `vulnerabilities` with `or {}` (the outer `metadata` is from `mc_diag`'s own dict, not external) — **CLEAN**. `scripts/sentinel_news_pipeline.py:95` is a cron script off the live-serving path. **The two genuine defects were the LLM-output sites (below).**

**The bug (`generate_ai_digest` `:3099` + the Idea Engine generator `:3311`, backend — null-guard class, same family as iter #67; PRESENT on any LLM run that returns a null/omitted-as-null ideas list, latent only because the model usually complies).** Both endpoints fire a slow (1-3 min) `_llm_json(...)` synthesis and build their result with `"ideas": parsed.get("ideas", [])[:8]`. `_llm_json` guarantees the top-level value is a **dict** (`:3151` `isinstance(obj, dict)`), but NOT the shape of its values — a model can legitimately emit `{"summary": "…", "ideas": null}` (valid JSON, passes the dict check). Then `parsed.get("ideas", [])` returns `None` (key present, default NOT used), and `None[:8]` raises `TypeError: 'NoneType' object is not subscriptable`. That escapes unhandled → FastAPI 500, and — critically — the crash happens BEFORE `_save_store(...)`, so the entire LLM run is **discarded**: the operator waits minutes, burns LLM quota, and gets no digest / no content ideas at all. The Idea Engine is the content pipeline's synthesis core (trending news × creator viral patterns × brand doc → ranked ideas), so this is a lost deliverable on the most operator-central content endpoint.

**Fix (1 file, back).** `parsed.get("ideas", [])[:8]` → `(parsed.get("ideas") or [])[:8]` at both sites (the established house `(x or [])`/`(x or {})` idiom), which coalesces both an absent key AND an explicit `None` to `[]` before the slice; a null/empty ideas list now degrades to `[]` and the run completes + persists whatever else it produced (summary/strategy_note). Comment added at the ai-digest site explaining the explicit-null trap; the Idea Engine site points back to it. The string fields (`summary`/`strategy_note`) use `.get(k, "")` and a null there is stored harmlessly (no method call) — deliberately left, the crash is slice-on-null only. **Verified:** `python -m py_compile mission-control-bridge.py` OK; a standalone old-vs-new proof over `{"ideas":None}` / `{}` / a 10-item list / `[]` — OLD raises `TypeError` on the null case, NEW yields `[]`, and all three non-null cases are byte-identical (absent→`[]`, list→sliced to 8, empty→`[]`); `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) GREEN (backend-only change; the >500 kB chunk warning is pre-existing and unrelated). Live-HTTP deferred — exercising it needs a real 1-3 min LLM run AND a model that returns null, and the running bridge predates this edit; the exact-expression proof is the right verification for a surgical null-guard. Patch note iter-68 added; `graphify update .` ran.

**Files touched:** `mission-control-bridge.py` (`generate_ai_digest` + Idea Engine generator `ideas` null-guard), `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry + Systemic Threads + Next Targets + Focus-Area Rotation). No commit/push (loop rules; inherited churn left intact).

### 2026-06-19 — Iteration #67 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [board STILL `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` since #35], continued the queued **backend [#6] route-logic pass** over the STILL-un-swept-this-cycle endpoints [boards, decompose, metricool/content-calendar/media writes, ideas consume/skip/generate, ai-digest, sentinel] with the deliverable-integrity + null-guard lens — found + fixed a genuine endpoint-crash on the creator-scrape deliverable path: the #66-NOTED `authorMeta:null` AttributeError.)

Scoped via the /graphify existing-graph fast path (`query` over the boards/decompose/metricool/calendar/digest/sentinel handlers; the Python bridge isn't richly extracted so read the backend directly). The lone real defect was the #66-NOTED creator-scrape null crash (below); `unwatch_creator`'s 200-on-unknown (vs `delete_lead`'s 404) was re-confirmed as a cosmetic consistency asymmetry, NOT fixed (no operator impact — the watchlist ends up correct either way).

**The bug (`scrape_creators`, `mission-control-bridge.py:3029`, backend — deliverable-integrity / null-guard class; PRESENT on any TikTok scrape carrying a null author, latent only because the scrape is Apify-gated + the live watchlist hasn't tripped it).** The per-post creator field was built as `it.get("ownerUsername") or it.get("authorMeta", {}).get("name") or "?"`. Python's `dict.get(key, default)` only returns `default` when the key is **absent** — when a TikTok item carries `authorMeta: null` (JSON null → Python `None`, common for deleted/private/odd-typed accounts the `clockworks~tiktok-scraper` still returns), `it.get("authorMeta", {})` returns `None`, and `None.get("name")` raises `AttributeError`. That error is NOT an `HTTPException`, so it escapes the per-platform `except HTTPException` guard at `:3040`, propagates out of the whole `scrape_creators` handler as a 500, and — critically — **discards every post collected so far across all platforms** AND never reaches `_save_store("creators-feed", …)`. A single bad item therefore poisons the entire creator viral feed, which is the Idea Engine's primary input (`_gather_idea_inputs` reads `creators-feed`) — a lost deliverable that also starves the downstream content-idea generation.

**Fix (1 file, back).** `it.get("authorMeta", {}).get("name")` → `(it.get("authorMeta") or {}).get("name")` — the established house `(x or {}).get(...)` idiom (e.g. `:766-769`, `:2749`), which coalesces both an absent key AND an explicit `None` to `{}` before `.get`. The one bad post now degrades to `creator="?"` and the scrape continues, preserving the rest of the feed. **Verified:** `python -m py_compile mission-control-bridge.py` OK; a standalone old-vs-new proof on a real-shaped `{'authorMeta': None, …}` item — OLD raises `AttributeError: 'NoneType' object has no attribute 'get'`, NEW yields `'?'`, while a real `authorMeta={'name':'creatorX'}` still returns `creatorX` and an `ownerUsername`-bearing IG item is unaffected; `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) GREEN (backend-only change, build unaffected). Live-HTTP deferred — a real scrape requires `APIFY_API_TOKEN` + a live Apify actor run (slow + billable + network), and the running bridge predates this edit; the exact-expression proof is the right verification for this surgical null-guard. Patch note iter-67 added; `graphify update .` ran (1898 nodes/3666 edges/103 communities).

**Files touched:** `mission-control-bridge.py` (`scrape_creators` `authorMeta` null-guard), `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry + Next Targets). No commit/push (loop rules; inherited churn left intact).

Two compounding defects: (a) cap-before-sort drops the newest; (b) the `break` exits only the INNER `for p in paths` loop, so the second root (`research`) could still append entries past the cap. This is the documented cap-priority/signal-survival lens (iters #58 activity `[:50]`, #60 War Room signalLog, #61 Ghost Network feed) applied to a backend endpoint that the prior cap-priority sweep never reached.

**Fix (1 file, back).** `mission-control-bridge.py` `list_deliverables` — removed the in-loop `break`; collect every entry across both roots, **sort by `modified` desc, THEN** `items[:_DELIVERABLE_MAX_ENTRIES]`, so the surviving N are always the freshest and neither root can leak past the cap (mirrors `get_activity`'s collect-all-then-cap discipline). `rglob` already materializes the full path list, so building all dicts adds only O(files) work, no extra walk. **Verified:** `python -m py_compile mission-control-bridge.py` OK; a standalone two-root 600-file synthetic proof (mtime inversely correlated with name order) — OLD drops the newest deliverable (caps at `file_598`, never reaches the freshest `file_599`), NEW keeps the freshest 500 (`== CAP`, includes `file_599`); `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) GREEN. Present impact NIL on the live board (6 deliverable files « 500 → change is a verified no-op: collect+sort+slice = sort+identity, byte-identical to the old sort at low counts), certain-on-trigger above 500 artifacts. Live-HTTP deferred (the running bridge predates this edit; a restart would serve the corrected ordering). Patch note iter-65 added; `graphify update .` ran (1894 nodes/3662 edges/90 communities).

### 2026-06-19 — Iteration #64 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [board STILL `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` since #35], then chased the iter-#63 queued **first-match-vs-sum lens** to OTHER consumers of multi-status agent `counts` maps — found + fixed the predicted SIBLING in `useLeadStore`, a PRESENT, live-board lead-scoring undercount of the same blocked-visibility class.)

**Audited.** Re-probed the live bridge (`/api/mc/kanban/stats` `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` unchanged since #35, `oldest_ready≈10.2d`; `by_assignee` carries `narratrix {blocked:5, done:1, ready:2}` — the exact co-occurring-status case iter #63 fixed in Ghost Network). Scoped via /graphify existing-graph fast path, then grepped every consumer of `.counts`/`by_assignee`/`assignees(` across the stack: `useGhostStore` (fixed #63), backend `mc_store.py:1600/1607` (the `assignees()` `counts` feed; the projections there iterate per-status, no first-match drop), `Systems.tsx`/`OperationsCenter.tsx` `.counts` (diagnostics/sweep result dicts — unrelated, not agent status maps), and **`useLeadStore.ts:33` — a byte-for-byte twin of the iter-#63 `num()` first-match helper**.

**The bug (`useLeadStore.mapAgentToLead`, frontend — present, live-board, blocked-visibility class).** Identical to #63: a `num(counts, ...keys)` helper returned the **first present key's value**, and `queue` called it with five distinct co-occurring statuses: `num(counts, 'ready','queued','pending','todo','blocked')`. Since `a.counts` (mc_store `assignees()` `:441`) is `{status:count}` keyed by a task's SINGLE canonical status, `ready`/`todo`/`blocked` genuinely co-occur per agent, so first-match silently dropped all but the highest-listed present status. `queue` feeds `total = done+running+queue` AND the lead `score = done*12 + running*8 + queue*3 + jitter`, and `leads` is **sorted by score** — so an agent's blocked tasks vanished from its lead weight and pushed it down the ranked Lead Tracker list. Proven on the LIVE board: `narratrix {blocked:5, done:1, ready:2}` → queue read `2` (its **5 blocked dropped**), score `28`; single-bucket agents (gridkeeper/claudelink ready-only, signalscraper/corpnet/scriptwright/neonsurgeon done-only, default blocked-only) were already correct (only one queue key present). The key list already INCLUDED `blocked` (intent: blocked ∈ queue), so the defect is purely `num`'s first-match, not a concept change — same root cause, same surface family as #63.

**Fix (1 file, front).** `src/stores/useLeadStore.ts` — replaced `num` (first-match) with `sumKeys` (sums all present listed keys), mirroring `useGhostStore.sumKeys` (iter #63) with the same correctness comment. Because each task has exactly ONE status, summing a set of DISTINCT statuses can NEVER double-count. Applied to all three call sites (`done`/`running` are alias sets — at most one ever present, so byte-identical there; `queue` is the buggy distinct set). **Verified:** `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) GREEN; `eslint src/stores/useLeadStore.ts` = **No issues found**; standalone Node proof over the REAL live `by_assignee` — narratrix queue `2→7` (5 blocked recovered), score `28→43` (re-ranks it upward in the sorted Lead list); all 7 single-bucket agents byte-identical (no double-count, no regression). Present impact PRESENT + live-provable (narratrix mis-scored on today's board). Live-DOM render deferred (standing Vite-preview blocker: `Claude_Preview` anchors to the parent space-containing cwd). Patch note iter-64 added.

**Files touched:** `src/stores/useLeadStore.ts` (`num`→`sumKeys`; helper + 3 call sites), `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry + Next Targets + Focus-Area Rotation). No commit/push (loop rules; inherited churn left intact).

**The bug (`useGhostStore.mapAgentsToTopology`, frontend — present, live-board, blocked-visibility class).** A `num(counts, ...keys)` helper returned the **first present key's value**, and `queue` called it with FIVE distinct co-occurring statuses: `num(a.counts, 'ready','queued','pending','todo','blocked')`. But `a.counts` (mc_store `assignees()`/`stats()` `:441`/`:454`) is `{status:count}` keyed by a task's SINGLE canonical status — `ready` and `blocked` (and `todo`) genuinely CO-OCCUR per agent. First-match therefore returned ONLY the highest-listed present status and silently dropped the rest. Proven on the LIVE board: `narratrix {blocked:5, ready:2}` → queue_depth = `2` (its **5 blocked tasks dropped**), while `default {blocked:1}` → `1` (blocked counted, since no `ready` to shadow it) — an INCONSISTENT, under-reported queue depth. `queue_depth` drives the per-agent **QUEUE** gauge (`AgentDrillDown.tsx:112`), the Ghost Network deck queue gauge/stat/`{q} queued` card labels (`GhostNetwork.tsx:181`/`:557`/`:584`/`:602`) and the fleet `queue` total (`:238`), and feeds `agentLoad`. So narratrix showed "2 queued" everywhere while sitting on 5 blocked + 2 ready = 7, hiding 5 of the operator's 6 live blocked tasks — directly against the standing blocked-visibility systemic thread. The existing key list already INCLUDED `blocked` (intent: blocked ∈ queue depth, confirmed by `default` surfacing its blocked), so the defect is purely `num`'s first-match dropping co-occurring statuses, not a concept change.

**Fix (1 file, front).** `src/stores/useGhostStore.ts` — replaced `num` (first-match) with `sumKeys` (sums all present listed keys). Because each task has exactly ONE status, summing a set of DISTINCT statuses can NEVER double-count — it yields the count of tasks in any of those states (the true queue depth). Applied to BOTH call sites: `queue` (the buggy one) and `running` (`'running','in_progress','active','started'` — strictly more correct, zero behaviour change on real data since only `running` is ever emitted). **Verified:** `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) GREEN; `eslint src/stores/useGhostStore.ts` = **No issues found**; standalone Node proof over the REAL live agent counts — narratrix `2→7` (5 blocked recovered), fleet queue total `9→14` (all 6 live blocked now represented, was only 1), single-bucket agents (gridkeeper/claudelink ready-only, default blocked-only) byte-identical (no double-count, no regression). Present impact PRESENT + live-provable (narratrix's 5 blocked were hidden on today's board). Live-DOM render of the corrected gauge deferred (standing Vite-preview blocker: `Claude_Preview` anchors to the parent space-containing cwd). Patch note iter-63 added; `graphify update .` attempted but BLOCKED on the missing LLM key (the CLI re-extracts the whole mixed corpus and 47 changed docs/images need semantic extraction — my single changed file `useGhostStore.ts` is AST-only; the graph.json retains the iter-#62 build, harmless for this run's scope).

**THE TWO QUEUED CANDIDATES (iter #60 Next Targets #2):**
- ✅ **Ghost Network `feed` (`src/pages/GhostNetwork.tsx:281`)** — THE REAL DEFECT, now FIXED. The merged Activity Stream did `[...acts, ...chat].sort(asc).slice(-80)`, keeping the newest 80 rows. A still-stuck `blocked`/`failed` activity row carries its OLD blocked/started timestamp, so a long chat session or a burst of recent activity pushes it off the FRONT (oldest end) — silently re-dropping the very rows the backend's iter-#58 cap-priority partition reserved budget to keep, and hiding the "needs attention now" signal from the operator's MAIN live view. **Fix:** mirror War Room `signalLog` (iter #60) — flag activity rows with `status ∈ {blocked,failed}` as `stuck` (new optional `FeedLine.stuck`), then partition the merge: keep ALL stuck rows (cap 80), fill the rest with the most-recent non-stuck rows via a newest-first `slice(0, N)` (avoids the `slice(-0)===whole-array` trap), and re-sort ascending for the scroll-to-bottom feed. `GhostNetwork.tsx:64` (interface), `:283`/`:302` (flag), `:313` (partition).
- ❌ **`EventFeedDrawer` (`src/components/EventFeedDrawer.tsx`)** — re-examined, NOT a cap-priority defect. It requests `getRecentEvents(100)` while the backend `recent_events` cap is 50, so nothing is client-truncated; the `shown` category filter only HIDES rows by category, it never slices by count. Matches the iter-#60 note ("defensive-only, low value"). Do NOT chase.

Standalone Node proof (worst-case busy feed: 6 old blocked rows + 4 recent acts + 120 newer chat rows): OLD `slice(-80)` keeps **0/6** blocked → NEW partition keeps **6/6**, length ≤80, ascending, newest chat row still at the bottom; small-board (<80 total) output **byte-identical** to OLD. LIVE-DOM not confirmable (no preview); the render path was already exercised piecemeal and the change is pure list-ordering. Patch note `iter-61-ghostnetwork-feed-keep-stuck` added (category lifecycle, severity medium).

(2) **frontend feed merges** — found the real one (below). `/graphify query` confirmed `get_events()` @ `mission-control-bridge.py:963` → `STORE.recent_events` (community 9).

**THE BUG (lifecycle-visibility / lost-signal, MED — frontend re-truncation of the backend's protected rows).** `src/pages/WarRoom.tsx` `signalLog` (`:139`) consumed `/api/mc/activity` (which the backend iter-#58 fix deliberately cap-prioritizes so EVERY stuck `blocked`/`failed` row survives its 50-cap) and then did `[...activities].sort(by timestamp desc).slice(0, 40)` — a **pure newest-40 cut that throws away exactly the protection #58 added**. A stuck task's signal carries its OLD blocked/started timestamp; once the operator restarts the bridge to pick up #58 (backend then returns 6/6 blocked rows, 2 of them with ~Jun-9 stamps), a board busy enough to have >40 routine events newer than the oldest blocked row pushes those stuck rows past the `slice(0,40)` tail — re-hiding them from the War Room AGENT SIGNAL feed, the precise operational-spine "is this task stuck?" surface. Present impact is **LATENT on the current live data** (the pre-#58 bridge returns only 4 blocked rows, all at time-ranks 23/26/28/34 < 40, so none drop today), but it is a **certain regression of #58's intent** the moment the bridge is restarted onto a busier board — the frontend was the unguarded twin of the backend cap #58 closed. (Ghost Network's merged `feed` `:313` `slice(-80)` over a ≤50-activity+chat stream is the looser sibling — rarely truncates activity rows; left un-changed, noted.)

**THE FIX (1 file, front).** `WarRoom.tsx` `signalLog`: mirror the backend #58 partition exactly — after the newest-first sort, split into `critical` (status `blocked`/`failed`, lowercased) and `rest`, keep `critical[:40] + rest[:max(0,40-len(critical))]`, re-sort by time, then map to rows. Every currently-stuck signal now survives the 40-row display budget; routine signals fill the remainder. Behaviour is byte-identical when `activities` ≤ 40 (the common small-board case, incl. the current live board), so no present-behaviour change — purely adds the survival guarantee.

**VERIFIED.** `npm run build` green (tsc -b + vite, 801ms; pre-existing chunk-size warning only). `npx eslint src/pages/WarRoom.tsx` = **No issues found**. Standalone Node proof (synthetic worst-case 50-row feed, 6 blocked all OLDer than 44 routine rows): OLD `slice(0,40)` keeps **0/6** stuck rows (all lost), NEW partition keeps **6/6**, feed length 40 both, NEW strictly newest-first, AND a ≤40-row small board is byte-identical OLD-vs-NEW (parity → no regression). Live-DOM deferred — the running bridge predates #58 (so the live feed can't yet exhibit the >40-row truncation) AND the standing Vite-preview blocker is unresolved; the fix rests on the build/lint gates + the deterministic parity/worst-case proof, certain-on-restart-onto-a-busier-board. `graphify update .` ran post-edit.

**NEW STANDING NOTE (iter #60):** the cap-priority / signal-survival lens (#58) now has a FRONTEND corollary — when the backend reserves cap budget for operator-critical rows, any frontend feed that re-slices that stream by time (`slice(0,N)` / `slice(-N)`) must re-apply the SAME partition or it silently undoes the protection. War Room `signalLog` was the acute instance (40 < backend 50); remaining slices to watch under this lens: Ghost Network `feed` `:313` (`slice(-80)`, combined activity+chat — looser), `EventFeedDrawer` (requests 100, client-side category filter applied AFTER the fetch cap). Backend `recent_events` `:1809` is a documented LATENT-only defensive spot (0 stuck-kind events live, total < cap).

### 2026-06-18 — Iteration #59 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [present surface healthy/unchanged], then took the iter-#58-queued **Electron-shell / misconfig [#7]** lead and closed the documented-but-unfixed **fd leak** in the `vite.config.ts` dev-server `bridgeLauncher`: the parent (long-lived Vite dev server) opened the bridge log via `fs.openSync` and handed it to the spawned `mission-control-bridge.py` via `stdio`, but **never closed its own copy** — so every `/__bridge/start` POST that actually spawned a bridge leaked one fd inside the dev server, slowly toward `EMFILE` over a long dev session of restarts. Front/dev-config, 1 file [`vite.config.ts`]; `npm run build` green + eslint **No issues found** on the touched file + a standalone Node spawn-replay proving the parent fd is reclaimed while the child keeps writing to the log via its inherited dup; patch note iter-59 added.)

**LIVE-PROBE.** Bridge UP on :8767 (`/api/ping` ok, uptime ~16075s ~4.5h — predates this edit; dev-config change has no live-board effect anyway). `/api/mc/kanban/stats` = `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` (board **unchanged since #35**, `oldest_ready≈842987s` ~9.76d, 0 failed/archived/todo/cron). No new live state to unlock the long-deferred LIVE-DOM list (Vite-preview blocker still standing). `/graphify query` (existing graph) confirmed `bridgeLauncher()` is a self-contained `vite.config.ts` plugin (community 61, alongside `probeBridge()`); nothing else consumes `logFd` → isolated, single-file fix.

**THE BUG (misconfig / resource leak, LOW — dev-only, certain-on-trigger).** `vite.config.ts` `bridgeLauncher` (`:44`) does `logFd = fs.openSync(logPath, 'a')` then `spawn(py, ['mission-control-bridge.py'], { detached:true, stdio:['ignore', logFd, logFd] })`. Passing a numeric fd in `stdio` makes libuv **dup** it for the child during `uv_spawn`; the **parent's** original fd is NOT auto-closed by Node. The dev server is long-lived and the Bridge Diagnostics panel can POST `/__bridge/start` repeatedly (one spawn per offline-restart), so each real spawn leaked exactly one fd in the Vite process — an unbounded climb over a long session that ends in `EMFILE`. Dev-only (Electron/production uses the preload IPC, not this middleware) and currently NIL present impact (a single dev session rarely restarts the bridge enough to exhaust fds), but a deterministic leak.

**THE FIX (1 file, dev-config).** After `spawn`, close the dev server's copy of `logFd` once the child has inherited its dup: a `closeLogFd()` helper guarded by a `logFdClosed` flag (and a `logFd !== 'ignore'` guard so the openSync-failed fallback is a no-op), wired to `child.on('spawn', closeLogFd)` and folded into the existing `child.on('error', …)` handler. `'spawn'` and `'error'` are mutually exclusive for the spawn outcome, and the flag makes the helper idempotent against any later `'error'` — so it fires exactly once. The child keeps writing to `.mc/bridge.log` through its own inherited dup; only the parent's leaked copy is reclaimed.

**VERIFIED.** `npm run build` green (tsc -b + vite build, 163 modules, 672ms; pre-existing chunk-size warning only). `npx eslint vite.config.ts` = **No issues found**. Standalone Node spawn-replay (temp dir, zero repo mutation, no real bridge): mirrored the exact pattern — after the `spawn` event `fs.fstatSync(logFd)` throws (parent fd **closed**), and the child process still wrote its stdout into the log file via its inherited dup AFTER the parent closed its copy (RESULT: PASS on both facts, run twice). Live dev-server `/__bridge/start` hammer deliberately NOT run (would spawn real `mission-control-bridge.py` processes on the operator's machine + churn the live bridge); the leak fix rests on the build/lint gates + the deterministic spawn-replay proof. `graphify update .` ran post-edit (1882 nodes/3648 edges/89 communities).

**NEW STANDING NOTE (iter #59):** the Electron/dev-shell [#7] surface had ONE concrete documented defect (this fd leak) — now drained. Remaining un-swept-but-noted there (all low value): `vite.config.ts` `bridgeLauncher` has no overall timeout cap beyond its 30×500ms re-probe loop; `desktop`/`desktop:dev` packaging, CSP, and single-instance-lock edge cases in `electron/main.cjs` were only spot-checked (iter #56 audited the IPC/preload/lifecycle contract CLEAN). The macOS `activate`-without-bridge-restart gap (iter #56) stays a noted low-value follow-up.

### 2026-06-18 — Iteration #58 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first, then chased the iter-#57-documented lead "4 `blocked` activity rows vs 6 `blocked` tasks" to ground — found it is NOT the stamp-less #47 edge case but a **lifecycle-visibility LOST-SIGNAL bug in `get_activity`'s `[:50]` cap**: a stuck blocked/failed task's event carries its OLD blocked/started timestamp, so a burst of recent created/claimed/completed events pushes the older stuck rows off the tail of the naive newest-50 cut — hiding still-stuck tasks from the War Room AGENT SIGNAL feed + Ghost Network Activity Stream. Fixed by reserving cap room for EVERY stuck event then filling the rest with the newest other events. Back, 1 file [`mission-control-bridge.py`]; `py_compile` + standalone old-vs-new replay on the REAL live board [OLD 4/6 → NEW 6/6 blocked, feed still 50 rows, still newest-first] + `npm run build` green; patch note iter-58 added.)

**LIVE-PROBE.** Bridge UP on :8767. `/api/mc/kanban/stats` = `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` (board **unchanged since #35**, `oldest_ready≈835758s` ~9.7d, 0 failed/archived/todo/cron). `/api/mc/activity` (50 rows, `activities`-keyed) = `{created 16, running 15, complete 15, blocked 4}` — **only 4 `blocked` rows vs 6 `blocked` tasks on the board**, the exact discrepancy iter #57 flagged-but-deferred. `/graphify query` (existing graph) confirmed the lone owner: `get_activity()` @ `mission-control-bridge.py:874`, community 9.

**THE BUG (lifecycle-visibility / lost-signal, MED) — the activity-feed 50-cap silently drops older still-stuck tasks.** Ran a standalone replay of `get_activity`'s synthesis over the live task list: it produces **74 events pre-cap**, sorted newest-first then hard-cut to `[:50]`. Of the **6** stuck (`blocked`/`failed`) events, **4 land in the top 50** (ranks 23/26/28/34) and **2 are TRUNCATED** — `t_ac3acb98` (rank 61) and `t_4b8bab28` (rank 65) — because their stuck timestamp is the task's OLD blocked/started time (~Jun-9), older than 50 routine created/running/complete events from the recent pipeline burst. So two tasks that are STILL actively blocked, needing operator attention, were **invisible** in both the War Room AGENT SIGNAL feed and the Ghost Network Activity Stream — the precise operational-spine "is this task stuck?" signal those feeds exist to surface. This is distinct from (and downstream of) iter #47's stuck-event EMISSION fix: #47 ensures the event is created; this ensures it SURVIVES the cap. Disproves iter #57's guess that the 2 missing were stamp-less (both carry valid `started_at`).

**THE FIX (1 file, back).** `mission-control-bridge.py` `get_activity` (`:944`): after the newest-first sort, partition into `critical` (status `blocked`/`failed`) and `rest`, keep `critical[:CAP] + rest[:CAP-len(critical)]`, re-sort by time, return `[:CAP]` (CAP=50). Every currently-stuck task's row now survives the cap; the budget is spent on stuck signals first, routine events fill the remainder. Behaviour is byte-identical when total events ≤ 50 or when ≤50 events contain all stuck rows (the common small-board case). Semantically safe: `critical` correctly catches BOTH stuck-branch events and the `has_completion` blocked/failed completion events (both set status to `blocked`/`failed`), and the `[:CAP]` belt bounds the degenerate >50-stuck case.

**VERIFIED.** `python -m py_compile mission-control-bridge.py` OK. Standalone old-vs-new replay over the REAL live `/api/mc/tasks` (zero mutation): total 74 events, 6 stuck → **OLD feed shows 4/6 blocked, NEW shows 6/6**; NEW feed length 50, still strictly newest-first, size ≤ 50 (all assertions pass). `npm run build` green (163 modules, 714ms; pre-existing chunk-size warning only — backend-only change can't affect the TS build). **Live-HTTP deferred:** the running bridge predates this edit, so a live GET still returns the old 4-row result until the operator restarts the bridge — the fix is proven against real data via the in-process replay, certain-on-restart. `graphify update .` ran post-edit.

**NEW STANDING LENS (cap-priority / signal-survival):** any feed/list that hard-caps a merged event stream (`[:N]`) must ask whether the OPERATOR-CRITICAL rows (stuck/blocked/failed/error) can carry an OLD timestamp and be sorted off the tail by routine high-frequency events — if so, reserve cap budget for the critical class before filling with the rest. `get_activity` was the first instance; `get_events`/`recent_events` (`:950`/`:959`) and the frontend feed merges are candidates to re-check under this lens.

### 2026-06-18 — Iteration #56 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [present surface healthy], then opened the NEVER-audited **Electron desktop-shell layer** [`electron/main.cjs` + `preload.cjs`] — absent from the focus-area rotation across all 55 prior runs — and fixed a real app-lifecycle bug: on macOS, closing the last window tore down the supervised bridge and latched `isQuitting`, so a dock-reopened window pointed at a dead, un-supervised backend. Back/shell, 1 file [`electron/main.cjs`]; `node --check` + green `npm run build` [TS app unaffected]; patch note iter-56 added. Present impact LATENT for this Windows operator [macOS-only path], certain-on-trigger for the documented Mac desktop build.)

**LIVE-PROBE.** Bridge UP on :8767; `/api/mc/kanban/stats` = `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` (board **unchanged since #35**, `oldest_ready≈821353s` ~9.5d, 0 failed/archived/todo/cron). `/api/mc/activity` (50 rows) = `{running 19, complete 15, created 12, blocked 4}` — bridge still restarted-past-#47 (live `blocked` rows present, agent `narratrix`, action `blocked · <title>`, valid stamps → iter #47 confirmed at the data layer; **no phantom `running` twin observable in the 50-row window**, consistent with the bridge predating #55 but the window not catching a paired `-s`/`-d` collision). Present-impact surface remains healthy/exhausted; pivoted to never-swept territory.

**THE BUG (latent for this operator; certain on the Mac build) — Electron `window-all-closed` killed the bridge on macOS.** `electron/main.cjs` supervises the local `mission-control-bridge.py` child (auto-restart with backoff; `isQuitting` gates teardown). The `window-all-closed` handler ran `shutdown()` **unconditionally** — setting `isQuitting=true` and `bridgeProc.kill()` — *before* the `if (process.platform !== 'darwin') app.quit()` line. On macOS the app conventionally stays alive in the dock after the last window closes, to be reopened via `app.on('activate')` → `createWindow()`. But `createWindow` never (re)starts the bridge, and `isQuitting=true` permanently disables the `bridgeProc.on('exit')` auto-restart — so a dock-reopened window loaded `dist/index.html` against a **dead, un-supervised backend** (blank dashboard, no recovery short of a full app relaunch). On Windows (this operator) the handler quits the app anyway, so the unconditional `shutdown()` was harmless there — hence LATENT here, but a certain regression on the Mac half of the documented Mac/Windows desktop distribution. **Fix (`electron/main.cjs`, `window-all-closed`, 1 file):** moved `shutdown()` inside the `!== 'darwin'` branch (alongside `app.quit()`); on macOS the app + supervised bridge now stay alive until a real quit, where the existing `before-quit` → `shutdown()` (and `process.on('exit')`) tear the bridge down correctly. No behaviour change on Windows/Linux (still `shutdown()` + `app.quit()`); `app.quit()` itself fires `before-quit` → `shutdown()`, so teardown is preserved everywhere. **Verified:** `node --check electron/main.cjs` OK; `npm run build` green (the file is plain CJS — not in `tsc -b` nor the `**/*.{ts,tsx}` eslint scope, so the build/lint gates only confirm the TS app is unaffected; correctness rests on the deterministic lifecycle reasoning above + the preserved `before-quit`/`process.exit` teardown paths). Live-Electron run not exercised (no macOS host; would require launching the packaged desktop app). Patch note iter-56 added.

**NEW STANDING SURFACE (iter #56):** the **Electron desktop shell** (`electron/main.cjs` bridge supervision + window lifecycle + IPC, `electron/preload.cjs` context-bridge contract, the `vite.config.ts` `bridgeLauncher` dev-twin middleware) was never in the focus rotation. This run audited it: the `bridge:start` IPC ↔ `preload` ↔ `BridgeDiagnostics` ↔ `/__bridge/start` contract is CONSISTENT; `waitForBridge`/backoff/single-instance-lock are sound; the only defect was the macOS teardown above. Remaining un-fixed-but-noted (low value): `createWindow` does not proactively re-probe/restart the bridge on macOS `activate` if it died while no window was open (supervision covers crashes; manual BridgeDiagnostics restart covers the rest); operator-facing string `BridgeDiagnostics.tsx:86` + `api.ts:6` comment still say the stale intermediate name `mc-bridge.py` (real file is `mission-control-bridge.py`) — a forward-migration cosmetic straggler.

But it did **not** suppress the still-firing `{tid}-s` `claimed`/**`running`** event (`mission-control-bridge.py:899-900`) for that same task — and **every live blocked task carries a `started_at`** (verified: all 6 have `started_at` set, `completed_at=None`). So each blocked task emitted BOTH `{-s, running}` AND `{-d, blocked}` **at the identical `started_at` timestamp** → it appears TWICE in the War Room AGENT SIGNAL feed + Ghost Network Activity Stream, once red (blocked) and once amber (claimed/running), so a stalled task STILL masquerades as actively working — the exact operational-spine signal iter #47 set out to fix — and the feed's `running` count is inflated (live: 24 synthesized running rows, 6 of them phantoms from blocked tasks). **Fix (`mission-control-bridge.py`, `get_activity`, 1 file):** compute `has_completion`/`stuck = (not has_completion) and status in {blocked,failed}` once; gate the `-s` `claimed/running` emission on `and not stuck`; reuse `stuck` for the terminal `elif`. The `-s` history row is dropped only for a task currently sitting in a blocked/failed dead-end (its true current signal is the `-d` blocked row); genuinely running tasks and the full done-task lifecycle (`-c/-s/-d`, distinct timestamps) are untouched. **Verified:** py_compile OK; a faithful before/after replay of the exact synthesis loop over the **live** `/api/mc/tasks` payload — OLD `running 24`→NEW `running 18` (exactly the 6 phantoms removed), each blocked task `[blocked,created,running]`→`[blocked,created]`, all `done` tasks byte-identical; `npm run build` green (frontend untouched). **Bug fixed — cron "next run" display hides the next-fire time for valid, firing interval schedules (a THIRD interval-parser location diverging from the daemon — the iter-#27/#28 class, never examined).** `mc_store._next_run` (`mc_store.py:1814`) — the helper that stamps `next_run` onto every cron job surfaced through the cron store (call sites `:1720`/`:1749`/`:1767`, operator-facing) — parsed intervals with its OWN inline regex `\s*(?:every\s+)?(\d+)\s*([mhd])\s*`: it required a **space** after `every` and recognized only the **single-letter** units `m`/`h`/`d`. But the daemon that actually decides whether/when a job fires, `mc_scheduler.parse_interval_seconds` (`:130`), strips the prefix with `removeprefix("every").strip()` (no space needed) and accepts a far richer unit vocabulary (`s|sec|…|seconds|m|min|…|minutes|h|hr|…|hours|d|day|days`). So a job scheduled `30s`, `5min`, `2hr`, `1day`, `30 minutes`, `every 1 day` or `every30m` **fires on the daemon but rendered with NO next-run time** in the UI — a firing job that looks misconfigured/dead (a lifecycle-visibility gap). iters #27/#28 reconciled the OTHER two parsers (`cronSchedule.ts` ↔ the daemon) but never touched this server-side display helper. **Fix (1 file, back):** `_next_run` now **delegates interval parsing to the daemon's `parse_interval_seconds`** (single source of truth — `mc_scheduler` is a pure, leaf, stdlib-only module per its own header, so a function-local `from mc_scheduler import parse_interval_seconds` is safe and cycle-free), then formats `_now() + secs`. Cron expressions, named macros (`@daily`) and garbage still return `None` → the UI falls back to the raw schedule exactly as before (no regression); the degenerate `0m` now correctly returns `None` (daemon rejects `n<1`) instead of falsely showing "now". This guarantees the next-run display can never again disagree with the daemon by construction.

**Verify.** `python -m py_compile mc_store.py mc_scheduler.py` ✓. **Standalone daemon-parity differential** (14 cases): every daemon-firing form now yields a next-run time — **7 previously-hidden forms FIXED** (`30s`/`5min`/`every30m`/`2hr`/`1day`/`30 minutes`/`every 1 day`), the 3 already-working forms unchanged, and `_next_run`'s show/hide decision now **matches the daemon's fire decision on all 14 cases (0 divergences)**; cron/macro/gibberish correctly still return `None`. `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) ✓ green (backend-only change; pre-existing >500kB chunk warning only). **Live-HTTP/live-DOM deferred** — `/api/mc/cron` carries **0 jobs**, so there is no live cron job to render a next-run for; certain-on-use (any operator who creates an interval cron with a seconds/worded/no-space form). Patch note `iter-54-cron-next-run-interval-parity` (lifecycle/low) added.

**STANDING NOTE (cron-parser single-source-of-truth — extends #27/#28):** there were THREE interval parsers — `cronSchedule.ts` (UI countdown, reconciled #27/#28), `mc_scheduler.parse_interval_seconds` (the daemon, canonical), and `mc_store._next_run` (server-side next-run display, reconciled THIS run by delegating to the daemon). All three now agree. The daemon's `parse_interval_seconds` is the canon; any future interval display must route through it (or mirror its grammar exactly), never hand-roll a fourth regex. The cron seam is now fully reconciled across all three locations.

### 2026-06-18 — Iteration #50 (focus: LIVE-PROBE first [no new state], then a FRESH substring-collision sweep applying the prefer-exact-over-`includes` lens that GN-FEEDCOLOR #48 / event-filter #49 established — found + fixed a real deliverable-surface correctness bug: the stuck-task block/fail REASON banner could surface an `unblocked` event's note as the reason a task is *currently* stuck, because `k.includes('block')` also matches the kind `unblocked`. Front, 1 file; build + lint-clean-on-touched-file + standalone old-vs-new reducer proof. Present impact LATENT [the 6 live blocked tasks are the `blocked_no_reason` cohort with zero events], certain-on-trigger for any block→unblock-with-reason→re-block-no-reason task.)

**LIVE-PROBE.** Bridge UP on :8767; `/api/mc/kanban/stats` = `{done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` — **unchanged since #35** (`oldest_ready≈778178s` ~9.0d; 0 failed/archived/todo/cron; narratrix carries 5/6 blocked). `/api/mc/activity` (shape `{"activities":[…]}`, 50 rows) = `{running:19, created:16, complete:15}` — **still 0 blocked rows**, so the running :8767 bridge **STILL predates iter #47** (process not restarted since); #47/#48/#49 remain live-unconfirmed and the long deferred-DOM list (#22/#24/#25/#31/#32/#35/#36/#37/#40/#42/#46/#47) stays unconfirmable in a real DOM. **Bug fixed — stuck-task block/fail REASON banner can surface an UN-block note as the reason it's stuck (deliverable-integrity, substring-collision class; the banner IS a stuck task's primary deliverable per its own DELIV-2 comment).** `src/components/TaskDetailDrawer.tsx:169` computed `blockFailReason` (the prominent BLOCKED/FAILED "why" banner, iter #6) by scanning the task's events newest-first for the first one matching `s === 'blocked' || s === 'failed' || k.includes('block') || k.includes('fail')` then taking its `eventDetail`. **`k.includes('block')` also matches the event kind `unblocked`** — and `mc_store.py:335` emits `event="unblocked", payload={"reason": reason}` (a `reason` payload, exactly what `eventDetail`'s `DETAIL_KEYS` extracts). So for a task that was **blocked-with-reason → unblocked-with-note → re-blocked WITHOUT a reason** (the `blocked_no_reason` re-block is the live-board norm — all 6 live blocked tasks are reasonless), the reducer skips the empty re-block event, then hits the `unblocked` event and surfaces *its* note as the current block reason — actively MISINFORMING the operator (it shows a RESOLUTION note as the cause of the stall). Enumerated every stored event kind (`mc_store.py` `_mutate(event=…)`): only `blocked`/`unblocked` contain "block" and only `failed` contains "fail", so `unblocked` is the lone false positive; `promoted`/`scheduled`/`requeued` also carry `reason` payloads but don't contain block/fail substrings (correctly excluded by both old and new). **Fix (1 file, front, 1 predicate):** `k.includes('block') || k.includes('fail')` → `k === 'blocked' || k === 'failed'` (exact kind match). Strictly a superset-minus-the-collision: still catches every real `blocked`/`failed` event, excludes `unblocked`, and the `s === 'blocked'/'failed'` payload-status checks remain the catch-all for any event that sets status without a block/fail kind. Same lens as GN-FEEDCOLOR (#48): prefer exact status/kind over a `.includes()` substring that collides with sibling vocabulary.

**Verify.** `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) ✓ (green; pre-existing >500kB chunk warning only). `npx eslint src/components/TaskDetailDrawer.tsx` → **No issues found**. **Standalone Node proof** (`.mc/cache/proof_blockreason.mjs`, run then removed) replicating `eventDetail` + the exact banner reducer over a `blocked(no reason) / unblocked(reason:"web access granted") / blocked(reason:"waiting on web access")` history: OLD predicate → banner reads `"web access granted"` (the un-block note — WRONG); NEW predicate → `"waiting on web access"` (the true original block reason); plus regression guards proving NEW still catches a plain `blocked` event, a `failed` event, and a payload-`status==='blocked'` event of a non-block/fail kind. **Live-DOM deferred** — no live task has the triggering event sequence (the 6 live blocked tasks have zero events), and the preview MCP remains anchored to the parent non-repo cwd (standing blocker). Patch note `iter-50-block-reason-banner-unblock-collision` (deliverable/medium) added. Ran `graphify update .` (1856 nodes / 3607 edges / 85 communities).

**BUG (LOGIC, latent footgun on a now-LIVE-rendered metric) — OLDEST READY chip computed via a double-`Date.now()` cancellation (Lead #4, queued since iter #1, ZERO-impact-confirmed #35, now live-exercised).** `OperationsCenter.tsx:247` rendered `ago(Math.floor(Date.now()/1000) - oldestReady)` where `oldestReady = stats.oldest_ready_age_seconds` is **already an age in seconds** (per `KanbanStats` in `api.ts` + the live payload). The module-local `ago(unixSeconds)` helper (`:45`) is semantically "given a unix TIMESTAMP, how long ago" and internally does `Date.now()/1000 - unixSeconds`. So the caller fabricated a fake timestamp (`now - age`) purely so `ago`'s own `now - ts` subtraction would cancel back to `age` — two `Date.now()` reads in different stack frames cancelling. Correct today (live ~8.67d → "8d"), but a genuine trap: any refactor of `ago()` that stops re-subtracting `Date.now()` silently breaks the chip, and the intent is obscured. `ago`'s other caller (`:302` `ago(t.created_at)`) is a genuine timestamp use and is correct. Until iter #35 the field was always `null` (0 ready tasks) so the buggy branch never ran; the board has carried 8 ready tasks since #35, so the chip is now actively rendering a real 8.67-day value through this footgun. **Fix (1 file, front):** extracted a small `fmtAge(seconds)` that formats an elapsed-seconds DURATION directly (same s<60/3600/86400 buckets, `Math.max(0,…)` floor), re-expressed `ago(ts)` as `fmtAge(Math.floor(Date.now()/1000) - ts)` so the single subtraction lives in ONE place, and changed the chip to `fmtAge(oldestReady)` (format the age directly — no fabricated timestamp). **Verified:** standalone Node proof that the OLD fabricated-timestamp path and the NEW direct path render byte-identical for the live value (`8d`) AND across every bucket boundary (0/1/59/60/61/3599/3600/7200/86399/86400/90000/749381/670227/5000000 — all MATCH); `npm run build` (tsc+vite) green; `npx eslint src/pages/OperationsCenter.tsx` → No issues. **No visible change** (the displayed value was already correct) — this is a latent-footgun hardening on a now-live metric, not a display repair. **LIVE-DOM deferred** — same blocker as ~10 prior runs: the Claude_Preview MCP is anchored to the parent session cwd (`…\Mission_Control`, the non-repo folder), not `Mission_Control_Claude`, so `preview_start` can't find the repo's `.claude/launch.json`; working around it means writing a launch config into the parent non-repo dir, which is outside the "touch only your fix + handoff + patch-notes" scope. Patch note iter-46 added (`.mc/patch-notes.json`).

**BUG (INTEGRATION param-semantics seam, LATENT/low present-impact) — `GET /api/mc/tasks/{id}/log` applied `tail` as a LINE count, not the byte cap both clients pass + document.** `mission-control-bridge.py` `task_log` did `log = "\n".join(lines[-tail:] if tail else lines)` — i.e. `tail` = number of EVENT LINES. But the route has exactly two callers, both passing `tail` as a **byte budget** and documenting byte semantics: `WorkerLogStream.tsx` (`const TAIL_BYTES = 8000`; comment "returns the last N **bytes** of the worker's log file") and `TaskDetailDrawer.tsx:130`'s DELIV-3 raw-output fallback (`getMcTaskLog(taskId, 4000)` → a `max-h-52` scroll box). Post-migration there **is no log file** — the log is synthesized from the event timeline, and each event line can carry a large JSON payload (live-confirmed: a real `completed` event embeds a `result_excerpt`, e.g. `t_34d9de94`). So `lines[-8000:]` is effectively NO bound at all — a chatty task ships its entire synthesized log to the DOM, contradicting the clients' "last N bytes" contract. (Present impact is currently LATENT — live tasks have ≤3 events / <400 bytes, well under the cap — so it's a certain-when-a-task-gets-chatty correctness/payload-bound fix, not a live-board repair. Same "stale Hermes-era file/byte assumption survived the migration" class as the `pending`→`todo` and timezone stragglers.)
**Fix (2 files):** (1) `mission-control-bridge.py` `task_log` now joins ALL lines then caps the WHOLE text to the last `tail` chars (`log[-tail:]`), dropping a partial leading line so the tail starts clean — guarded `if tail and tail > 0 and len(log) > tail`; the deliverable-bearing `completed` event (last line) is always preserved, so DELIV-3's raw-output fallback is unaffected. Char-slicing the `str` (not encoded bytes) is intentional — it can't split a multibyte char. (2) `WorkerLogStream.tsx` contract comment corrected ("last N chars of the task's worker log, synthesized from its event timeline; there is no log file post-migration"). **Verified:** `python -m py_compile` clean; a standalone unit-test replicating the exact endpoint body proves: empty→"(no events yet)"; small log under cap returned in full WITH the `result_excerpt`; a 50-event×500-byte log byte-bounded to ≤4000 (3814) vs the OLD line-cap's unbounded 27249, tail starting on a clean `[`-prefixed line. `npm run build` (tsc+vite) green (pre-existing chunk-size warning only); `npx eslint src/components/WorkerLogStream.tsx` clean. **Live-HTTP deferred** — the running :8767 bridge predates this edit; restarting it to confirm would mutate operator state (same constraint as every deferred fix since #35). Patch note iter-45 added (`.mc/patch-notes.json`). `graphify update .` ran (1838 nodes / 3570 edges / 91 communities).

**Bug/gap (LATENT correctness — timezone-math class; completes iter #43's fix).** iter #43 made `ContentFactory.upcoming`'s `today` boundary LOCAL and added a comment asserting "Every `c.date` is a LOCAL calendar date — the bridge derives them with datetime.fromtimestamp/now() (local)". That invariant holds for the PREFERRED bridge path, but is **FALSE on the client-side fallback path**: when `getContentPipeline()` throws, `useContentStore.refresh()` rebuilds the calendar from the task board (`useContentStore.ts:122-128`) with `date: isoDate(t.created_at)`, and `isoDate` (`:64`) was `new Date((unixSeconds||0)*1000).toISOString().slice(0,10)` — a **UTC** date. **Fix (1 file, front, pure, minimal — mirrors #43's `upcoming` local-YMD idiom).** `src/stores/useContentStore.ts:64` — `isoDate` now builds the local YMD from `getFullYear`/`getMonth`+1/`getDate` (zero-padded) instead of the UTC `toISOString().slice(0,10)`, with a comment explaining why local is correct (so both the bridge path and the fallback path agree, and the `upcoming` invariant becomes true on BOTH). Nothing else changed.

### 2026-06-17 — Iteration #43 (focus: iter-#42 priority (a) LIVE-PROBE [done — board STILL `{done 18, ready 8, blocked 6}` unchanged since #35; bridge STILL predates `/raw`, 404] → priority (b) fresh seam hunt. Front, 1 file; build+lint clean, standalone-Node proof of bug+fix)

So every build/logic-verified-only deferred fix (FAIL flow #31/#32, ARCHIVED column #37, cron-run timeout #36, dropdown labels #35, ErrorBoundary #22, CRUD banner #24, BLOCKED notifier #25, DELIV-6 image #40/binary #41/fallback #42) **remains unconfirmable in a real DOM.** Confirmed `src/lib/hermes/` is an **EMPTY straggler dir** (0 files, 0 importers) — inert, NOT a bug, left untouched per cardinal rule. Pivoted to LIVE data: `/api/content/pipeline` returns `campaigns[27]/drafts[13]/calendar[36]`, each calendar item carrying a `date` like `'2026-06-08'`.

**Bug/gap (PRESENT, hidden-deliverable / timezone-math class — the routine's top-priority class).** `src/pages/ContentFactory.tsx` `upcoming` (`:72`) computed the filter boundary as `const today = new Date().toISOString().slice(0, 10)` — the **UTC** calendar date — then filtered the calendar with `c.date >= today`. But every `c.date` is a **LOCAL** calendar date: the bridge derives them with `datetime.fromtimestamp(created_at)` / `datetime.now().strftime("%Y-%m-%d")` (both local) in `get_content_pipeline` (`mission-control-bridge.py:2208,2212`), and `formatDate` (`ContentFactory.tsx:36`) renders them local via `new Date(d + 'T00:00:00')`. So the boundary was the only thing in the calendar pipeline using UTC. For the operator's documented negative offset (UTC-7, per iter #20's 21:33 UTC = 14:33 local), every evening after the local clock passed the point where UTC had already ticked to the next day (~17:00 PDT), `today` became *tomorrow's* date and any post scheduled for **today** was filtered OUT of the UPCOMING list — content silently vanishing ~7h early from the very surface meant to show imminent posts (a lost/hidden deliverable, recurring daily). Symmetric direction (positive offset, early AM) is the harmless one — shows one stale past item.

**Fix (1 file, front, minimal — matches `formatDate`'s local semantics).** `src/pages/ContentFactory.tsx:72` — replaced the UTC `toISOString().slice(0,10)` with a LOCAL YMD built from `new Date()` (`getFullYear`/`getMonth`+1/`getDate`, zero-padded), with a comment explaining why local (not UTC) is correct. Nothing else in `upcoming` changed (the planned-first sort + `slice(0,7)` are untouched). Disjoint from the write-side default-date helpers (`:161`,`:296`) which set a *future* default for a new post and are not visibility filters — deliberately left alone (scope).

**Verify.** `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) ✓ (159 modules, ~638ms; the >500kB chunk warning is pre-existing/unrelated). `npx eslint src/pages/ContentFactory.tsx` ✓ (No issues found). **Standalone Node check PROVES bug+fix:** simulated a UTC-7 operator at 19:30 local 2026-06-17 (= 02:30 UTC 2026-06-18) → buggy UTC filter (`today=2026-06-18`) drops the post dated 2026-06-17 (today, local); fixed local filter (`today=2026-06-17`) keeps it. **Layer STATED UNVERIFIED — live-DOM:** the in-repo preview MCP remains blocked by the space-containing parent-dir path (documented across prior runs), AND triggering the live render requires the specific evening-UTC window; the fix is pure `useMemo` date arithmetic, build/type-verified + standalone-proven. Added patch note `iter-43-content-calendar-local-today` (bug, medium). Ran `graphify update .` (AST re-extract, 113/113 files → 1830 nodes/3560 edges).

**Bug/gap (LATENT but certain-on-first-use — top-priority deliverable-integrity class; the documented DELIV-6 follow-up).** iter #40 gave generated IMAGES a viewable home via `<img src={deliverableRawUrl(...)}>`, but left a documented gap: in `DeliverablesDrawer.tsx`'s non-image viewer branch, the content `<pre>` is gated on `!file.binary`, so when the JSON `/file` endpoint flags a **non-image** binary (PDF, zip, audio, video) as `{binary:true, content:"", note:"binary file — not shown"}`, the operator saw ONLY the amber "not shown" note — with NO open/download affordance — even though the iter-#40 `/api/mc/deliverables/raw` endpoint already streams those exact bytes. A produced PDF/zip deliverable was therefore listed-but-trapped: a lost deliverable in the Systemic-Threads sense.

**Fix (1 file, front, minimal, reuses the existing `/raw` endpoint — no backend change).** `src/components/DeliverablesDrawer.tsx`: (1) added an `isPdf(ext)` helper beside `isImage`. (2) In the non-image branch, added a `file?.binary` block that renders — for PDFs — an inline `<iframe src={deliverableRawUrl(selected.path)}>` (browser-native PDF preview), and for EVERY non-image binary a row of **↗ OPEN IN NEW TAB** + **⬇ DOWNLOAD ({size})** anchors pointing at the same `/raw` URL, preceded by the existing amber note. The text path (`!file.binary` → `<pre>`), the image `<img>` path, truncation, the empty state, and the catch-handler error note (binary:false, content:'') are all preserved — the error-note path still renders its note above an empty `<pre>` exactly as before.

**Verify.** `npm run build` ✓ (tsc -b + vite, built ~615ms; the >500kB chunk warning is pre-existing/unrelated). `npx eslint src/components/DeliverablesDrawer.tsx` ✓ (No issues found). **`/raw` re-confirmed present + correct in-process against CURRENT code via TestClient (read-only, did NOT touch the running :8767 process):** real PNG → **200 `image/png` 25 904 213 B**, `../mission-control-bridge.py` → **403**, missing `.pdf` → **404**; and the path is extension-agnostic (`FileResponse(target)`) so a `.pdf` serves `application/pdf` (iframe-embeddable) and `.zip` `application/x-zip-compressed` (downloadable) — exactly what the new iframe/links depend on. **Layer STATED UNVERIFIED — live-DOM:** the new binary branch cannot be exercised against live data (no PDF/zip/audio/video deliverable on the board), AND the running :8767 bridge predates `/raw`, so a live render needs the operator to (a) restart the bridge and (b) produce a non-image binary deliverable; the render is build/type-verified + reasoned, the `/raw` backend it points at is in-process verified. Added patch note `iter-41-binary-deliverable-retrieval` (deliverable, medium). Updated DELIV-6 thread to FULLY CLOSED. Ran `graphify update .`.

Text deliverables, the empty state, truncation, and task-id badges are untouched.
