### 2026-06-17 — Iteration #39 (focus: iter-#39 priority (a) LIVE-PROBE + (b) finish the migration vocabulary lens on the backend [CLEAN] then re-sweep the pure-lib queue-health layer — found + fixed a self-documented CONTRACT VIOLATION between `agingWip.ts` and `backlogTrend.ts`: the two War-Room queue-health views are documented to agree on "still-open work" but their closed-status sets diverged on `error`. FIXED [front, 1 file, pure lib] — npm build + eslint + standalone-divergence test VERIFIED; deterministic, present impact nil [`error` is not a reachable task status] = certain-on-first-error-task)

**Audited.** Used /graphify (existing-graph fast-path; `graphify-out/graph.json` present, 1.7M) — `query` scoped the status-bucketing/metric cluster (community 1: `agentMetrics`/`agingWip`/`cycleTime`/`taskThroughput`/`AgentPerformance`). **LIVE-PROBED the board first** (via `mc_store` directly — the bridge process holds its own state): `stats()` → `by_status {done 18, blocked 6, ready 8}` (same shape as #35–#38; 0 failed/archived/todo/triage/review/scheduled, `oldest_ready_age_seconds≈699016` ~8.1d). `list_tasks()` → 32 tasks; the 6 blocked are 5×narratrix + 1×default, one (`t_4b8bab28`) has `has_deliverable:true` (a blocked task CAN carry a deliverable — still reachable via the drawer; the board ◆ is done-lane-only by design, no gap). **No new live state** (no `failed`/`archived`/`todo`/cron job) to unlock any of the still-deferred live-DOM/live-HTTP confirmations (FAIL flow #31/#32, ARCHIVED column #37, cron-run timeout #36, dropdown labels #35, ErrorBoundary #22, CRUD banner #24, BLOCKED notifier #25) — all remain build/logic-verified only. **Finished the migration vocabulary lens [priority (b)]:** grepped every `pending`/`ready`/`todo` status comparison across `mission-control-bridge.py` + `mc_store.py` — all backlog buckets are now migration-aware (`stats` trend `:1995` counts `("pending","todo")`; drafts filter `:2152` includes `todo` per iter #38; `specify_task` `:1341` `triage/todo→ready` is intentional; `mc_store` lifecycle sets all use `("todo","ready")`) — **backend lens fully DRAINED, no remaining `'pending'`-without-`'todo'` straggler.** Re-read the pure-lib queue-health layer fresh against the real aged data (8 ready, oldest 8d; 6 blocked): `agentMetrics.ts` CLEAN (folds blocked into the "did-not-yet-succeed" bucket — documented intentional, line 16); `cycleTime.BUCKET_BOUNDS` has an open-ended `>3d` bucket so the 8-day task doesn't overflow; `AgentPerformance.tsx` CLEAN. The finding came from **cross-checking the closed/terminal sets across the three queue-health libs**.

**Bug/gap (CONTRACT VIOLATION — two same-screen queue counts documented to agree, don't).** `agingWip.ts:17-19` defines `TERMINAL = {done, complete, completed, failed, cancelled, canceled, archived, error}` and its comment (`:14-16`) **explicitly states** it "mirrors the closed-set used by `computeBacklogTrend`'s openBacklog so the two queue views agree on what counts as still-in-flight." But `backlogTrend.ts:17` `CLOSED = {done, complete, completed, failed, cancelled, canceled, archived}` — it **omits `error`**. `agentMetrics.ts:28` also treats `error` as a resolved (`FAILED`) outcome. So 2-of-3 queue-health libs treat `error` as closed; `backlogTrend` is the lone outlier. **Consequence (latent):** if an `error`-status task ever existed, `agingWip.openCount` (Aging-WIP panel) would count it closed while `backlogTrend.openBacklog` (backlog burn-down "in-flight" count) would count it open — the two numbers, shown together in the War Room and documented to match, would silently disagree by 1, and the errored task would inflate the instantaneous WIP forever. **Present impact is NIL** — confirmed `error` is not a reachable *task* status: the only producer is `mission-control-bridge.py:474` `record_task_run(status="error")` which records a RUN then immediately `requeue_task()` → the TASK status returns to `ready` (verified by reading the dispatch path + live status histogram = only `{done,ready,blocked}`). So this is a defensive/contract fix, not a live-board repair — same posture as iters #36/#37/#38.

**Fix (1 file, front, pure lib, minimal — align the outlier to the documented contract).** `src/lib/backlogTrend.ts:17` — added `'error'` to `CLOSED` so it matches `agingWip.TERMINAL` exactly, and expanded the comment to name the lock-step contract with the Aging-WIP panel + the rationale (a failed run is resolved, not outstanding WIP). Direction chosen by 2-of-3 majority + intuition (an error is a failure → closed); `agingWip`/`agentMetrics` are the correct side. No shape/type/behavior change for any live task (no `error` task exists); the only changed output is for a hypothetical `error` task, which now correctly counts as closed in both views.

**Verify.** `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) ✓ (157 modules, 630 ms). `npx eslint src/lib/backlogTrend.ts` ✓ (No issues found). **Standalone divergence test** (`node`, no deps): a 4-task board incl. one `error` task → PRE-FIX `agingOpen=2` vs `backlogOpen=3` (diverge=true); POST-FIX both `=2` (agree=true) — proves the divergence existed and the one-line fix reconciles it, with no change to the non-error tasks. **Layer STATED UNVERIFIED — live-DOM:** no dev preview up and no `error` task exists to render the reconciled counts against; the live board's open counts already agree (no error task), so there's nothing to regress. Added patch note `iter-39-backlog-error-consistency` (bug, low). Ran `graphify update .`.

**Bug/gap (DELIVERABLE-VISIBILITY — a content task in the to-do backlog was dropped from the Content Factory Drafts queue; the routine's top-priority class).** `get_content_pipeline()` (`mission-control-bridge.py`, route `/api/content/pipeline`) builds three views from the content-keyword-matched kanban tasks: `campaigns` (all), `calendar` (all), and `drafts` (filtered). The drafts filter was `if status in ("pending", "ready", "blocked", "failed")` — it included the **legacy Hermes-era `pending`** but **omitted `todo`, mc_store's canonical backlog status** (`mc_store.py:132/241` stamp new tasks `todo`/`triage`, never `pending`). So a content task sitting in the to-do backlog produced a `campaign` card (its `campaign_status` falls to the `else→"ready"` branch) and a `calendar` entry, but was **silently excluded from the DRAFTS queue** — planned content work invisible in the Factory's drafts list until promoted to `ready`. This is the **exact same `pending`→`todo` forward-migration straggler class** already fixed twice on the frontend — iter #33 (`summarize()` dropped `todo` from the topbar QUEUE) and iter #34 (the War Room status chart had no backlog bar) — but it had never been caught in this backend endpoint. **Demonstrated-impact, not merely theoretical:** at the iter-#33/#34 board state (`todo 8`, and 27/32 tasks match the content keywords) those 8 todo content tasks would have been missing from the drafts queue; the board has since oscillated those same backlog tasks `todo`→`ready` (iter #35), so present impact is currently nil only because of board state — identical posture to iter #36's deterministic nil-at-this-moment timeout fix.

**Fix (1 file, back, minimal — mirrors the iter #33/#34 pattern exactly).** `mission-control-bridge.py` — the drafts filter is now `if status in ("todo", "pending", "ready", "blocked", "failed")` (added `todo`, kept `pending` as the legacy alias, exactly as `summarize()`/stats count `("pending","todo")`); the section comment was updated from "Drafts = pending/ready tasks" to name the canonical `todo` backlog. No change to `campaigns`/`calendar`/the response shape, no new field, no frontend change. The `campaign_status` computation already routed `todo`→`"ready"` via its `else`, so the draft card's displayed status is unchanged; only the *inclusion* of todo content tasks in the list changed.

**Verify.** `python -m py_compile mission-control-bridge.py` ✓. `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) ✓ (157 modules, 648 ms — backend change, no frontend touched, confirms no regression). **Standalone logic check** of the patched filter over a synthetic board incl. a `todo` content task: OLD drafts = `[ready, blocked, pending]` (todo dropped); NEW drafts = `[todo, ready, blocked, pending]` (todo recovered); `done`/`running` still correctly excluded — no over-inclusion regression. **In-process check against the REAL live tasks (read-only):** 27 content tasks, statuses `{done 14, ready 8, blocked 5}`, 0 `todo` right now → OLD and NEW both yield 13 drafts (confirms zero regression at the current board state; the fix only changes behavior when a `todo` content task exists). **Layer STATED UNVERIFIED — live-HTTP of the NEW behavior:** the running bridge is a separate process that still holds the pre-edit code; restarting it to live-confirm would disrupt the operator's live bridge, and there is no live `todo` content task to exercise it against regardless — so this is a *certain-on-next-todo-content-task* fix, build+compile+logic-verified, in the same verification posture as iters #36/#37. **Bug/gap (PRESENT lifecycle-visibility defect — a terminal status with no board home leaks into the backlog).** `mc_store` defines `TERMINAL = {"done", "archived"}` (`mc_store.py:30`) and `archive_task` sets `status="archived"` (`:349`); `list_tasks()` returns **all** tasks with NO archived filter (`:216`). The Operations Center board groups every task by `colOf(t.status)` into the `COLUMNS` set (`OperationsCenter.tsx:178`), but `COLUMNS` enumerated only `triage/todo/ready/running/review/blocked/failed/scheduled/done` — **`archived` was missing**, so `colOf('archived')` hit the final `... : 'todo'` catch-all (`:34`) and an archived task landed in the **TODO** column. The ARCHIVE verb is fully reachable — wired as a drawer button (`TaskDetailDrawer.tsx:297`) allowed from `todo/ready/running/review/blocked/scheduled/done/triage` (`:51`). **Consequence:** an operator archives a task to retire it from the active board, and on the next board refresh it reappears in TODO masquerading as brand-new unstarted work — directly contradicting the archive action's purpose AND inflating the visible backlog. This is the exact same class as the pre-iter-#7 `failed`→`blocked` fold (a real status with no dedicated lane). It went undetected for 36 runs because the live board has never carried an archived task.

**Fix (1 file, front, minimal — mirrors iter #7's FAILED-column addition exactly).** `src/pages/OperationsCenter.tsx` — added `{ key: 'archived', label: 'ARCHIVED', tone: '#4b5563' }` to `COLUMNS` (after DONE; muted grey-600 tone to read as "retired"), with a comment explaining why a terminal status MUST have its own column. `colOf` is unchanged — its `COLUMNS.some((c) => c.key === status)` check now routes `archived` to its own lane naturally, while the `todo` fallback still catches genuinely-unknown statuses. The archived task's deliverable stays fully retrievable (its card still opens `TaskDetailDrawer`). No backend/shape/type change.

**Verify.** `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) ✓ (157 modules, 629 ms). `npx eslint src/pages/OperationsCenter.tsx` ✓ (No issues found). **Standalone logic check** of the ported `colOf` over all 13 statuses: `archived→archived` (was `→todo`), `completed→done`, `pending→todo`, `weird_unknown→todo` (catch-all preserved), every canonical status → its own column. Board container is `overflow-x-auto` (`:265`) so the 10th column is consistent with the existing design (which already renders empty TRIAGE/REVIEW/SCHEDULED/FAILED columns). **Layer STATED UNVERIFIED — present impact currently nil:** 0 archived tasks live and no dev preview was up; a live-DOM render of a *populated* ARCHIVED column would require creating an archived task = mutating operator data, deliberately not done. This is a *certain-on-first-archive* fix for a deterministic, reachable defect (same verification posture as iter #36's nil-impact timeout fix). **Bug/gap (PRESENT integration defect — deterministic timeout mismatch on a real operator button; the routine's explicitly-flagged "axios per-endpoint timeout vs real latency" class).** `runMcCron` (`src/lib/api.ts:632`) POSTed `/api/mc/cron/{id}/run` with **no timeout override → the global axios default of 30 000 ms (30s)**. But the backend route `run_cron` (`mission-control-bridge.py:1626`) is **synchronous** — for a `claude`-kind job (the default; `kind or "claude"`) it BLOCKS on `run_claude(prompt, timeout=300)` (up to **300s**) before returning, then records the result via `record_cron_result(...)`. So pressing the **RUN** button (`OperationsCenter.tsx:599`, `void runMcCron(j.id)` — fire-and-forget, no feedback) on any non-trivial Claude cron job aborts client-side at 30s with a timeout while the bridge keeps running to completion: the operator sees a (silent, unhandled-rejection) failure for a job that actually SUCCEEDS, the `message: resp["result"]` return never reaches the UI (a lost interaction), and a re-click spawns a second concurrent agent turn. This is the lone unmatched sibling — every other `run_claude`-backed endpoint already clears its backend ceiling (specify 180→190s, decompose 120→125s, chat 180→185s, `/api/mc/spawn` 120→125s, agent spawn 600→605s); cron-run was missed.

**Fix (1 file, front, minimal — mirrors the sibling pattern exactly).** `src/lib/api.ts:632` — `runMcCron` now passes `{ timeout: 305000 }` (backend 300s + the same 5s margin spawn uses), with a comment tying it to the synchronous `run_cron` route. One line of behavior change; no handler/shape change.

**Verify.** `npm run build` (tsc -b + vite) ✓ (157 modules, 640 ms). `npx eslint src/lib/api.ts` ✓ (No issues found). **Live premise confirmed non-destructively:** bridge up, `run_cron` route code is unambiguously synchronous (reads the `run_claude(timeout=300)` call inline before the return). **Layer STATED UNVERIFIED — present impact currently nil:** `/api/mc/cron` returns **0 jobs** on the live board (consistent with the standing "no `cron.json`" note), so the RUN button isn't rendered for any job right now and I did NOT trigger a real run (it would fire a real billable agent turn + mutate operator data). This is therefore a *certain-on-first-use* fix for a deterministic defect, not a repair of something broken on the current board — distinct from (and higher-value than) the never-reachable Arsenal/WorkflowBuilder latent hardenings, and it is exactly the integration bug class the routine asks to hunt. Added patch note `iter-36-cron-run-now-timeout` (bug, medium). Ran `graphify update .`.

**Bug/gap (PRESENT-IMPACT, lifecycle-visibility — the operator's at-a-glance "how much work is waiting?" counter read 0 while 8 tasks sat queued).** `useTaskStore.summarize()` (`src/stores/useTaskStore.ts:142`) computes `summary` from the raw `McTask[]`. Its backlog bucket was `pending: ht.filter(is('pending'))` — counting only the literal Hermes-era status `'pending'`. But `mc_store`'s canonical backlog status is **`todo`** (the live board is `todo`-only; `OperationsCenter.colOf` already aliases `pending → todo`, and `mapMcToOp` maps every unknown status incl. `todo` to `'pending'`). So `summarize` dropped all 8 live `todo` tasks: `summary.pending = 0`. The topbar **QUEUE = `summary.pending + summary.ready`** (`Layout.tsx:245`, the ONLY consumer of `summary.pending` — grep-confirmed) therefore rendered **0** despite 8 queued tasks — the counter looked empty while real work waited. (OperationsCenter's chips read the authoritative backend `stats.by_status`, so only the client-side `summary`/topbar was affected.) This is the same QUEUE counter iter #1 fixed for double-counting; the Hermes→mc status rename re-broke it in the opposite direction (under-count) — a forward-migration straggler, exactly the class the cardinal rule says to migrate forward (the `'pending'` vocabulary → mc's `'todo'`).

**Fix (1 file, front, minimal).** `summarize()` backlog bucket now counts BOTH statuses: `pending: ht.filter((t) => t.status === 'pending' || t.status === 'todo').length` — mirroring `colOf`'s existing `pending↔todo` aliasing, kept disjoint from `ready` (preserving iter #1's no-double-count invariant). No consumer other than the topbar QUEUE reads `summary.pending`, so zero collateral. Extended the bucket comment to document the todo-is-canonical migration.

**Verify.** In-process replication of the patched `summarize` against the REAL live tasks: OLD `pending=0 ready=0 → QUEUE 0`; NEW `pending=8 ready=0 → QUEUE 8` (the 8 live todo tasks now counted). `npm run build` ✓ (156 modules, 630 ms). `npx eslint src/stores/useTaskStore.ts` ✓ (no issues). **Layer relied on reasoning — STATED UNVERIFIED:** a live-DOM render of the topbar `● QUEUE` span was NOT performed — it would require standing up a Vite preview, and the consumer is a trivial literal `summary.pending + summary.ready` already compiled by the build; the fix is pure data-layer arithmetic confirmed against the exact live HTTP payload the frontend consumes. Added patch note `iter-33-queue-counts-todo` (bug, medium). Ran `graphify update .` (1759 nodes / 3449 edges / 79 communities).

**Bug/gap (OPERATIONAL-SPINE — answers the routine's "are failed tasks distinguishable from blocked?" in the LAST surface that still said no).** `get_activity()` (`mission-control-bridge.py`) synthesizes the live activity stream from task lifecycle timestamps. For a terminal task (`completed_at` stamped) it computed `status = "blocked" if t.get("status") in ("blocked","failed") else "complete"` and `verb = "blocked" if status=="blocked" else "completed"` — so a **`failed` task was emitted as `"blocked · {title}"` with status `"blocked"`**, identical to a deliberate block. Both `block_task` (`mc_store.py:319`) and `fail_task` (`:329`) stamp `completed_at`, so any API-driven failure DOES reach this feed — and the moment the operator uses the iter-#31 FAIL button, the resulting failure showed up in the **War Room AGENT SIGNAL feed** + **Ghost Network Activity Stream** as "blocked", silently undoing the distinguishability that iters #7 (FAILED column/chip), #25 (amber notifier), #6/#29 (drawer reason banner) and #30/#31 (the FAIL action itself) had built everywhere else. The frontend activity vocab already renders a `failed` status (`WarRoom STATUS_COLORS.failed = '#ef4444'` :20; Ghost Network classifies `s.includes('fail')` → 'warn' kind and appends `· {status}` to the text) — only the backend was collapsing it.

**Fix (1 file, back, minimal).** `mission-control-bridge.py` `get_activity()`: replaced the failed→blocked fold with an explicit 3-way map — `failed → ("failed","failed")`, `blocked → ("blocked","blocked")`, else `→ ("complete","completed")`. Done/blocked output is byte-identical to before; only a `failed` task now emits the honest `failed` verb + status. No frontend change needed (the vocab already supports it). Added a comment tying it to the FAIL-STATE surface.

**Verify.** `python -m py_compile mission-control-bridge.py` ✓. **Zero-mutation in-process synthesis test** on the REAL board (replicated the patched block on a copy, no store/disk mutation): the 11 live completed events all emit `complete`; a simulated API-driven failed task (status `failed` + `completed_at`) now emits `verb='failed' status='failed'` where the OLD code gave `('blocked','blocked')` — `NEW failed distinguishable from blocked: True`; a simulated blocked task still emits `blocked`/`blocked`. `npm run build` ✓ (156 modules, 623 ms — frontend untouched, confirms no contract break). **Layer relied on reasoning — STATED UNVERIFIED:** a live-HTTP render of a real `failed` activity event was NOT performed — the live board has 0 failed tasks and the live bridge runs the pre-edit code (uptime ~8680s); creating/restarting to exercise it would mutate operator data or churn the running bridge (loop write-action caution). The render side of a `failed` activity row was already structurally covered by the frontend vocab (iter #17 CF-COLOR) and the in-process logic proof. Added patch note `iter-32-activity-failed-vs-blocked` (lifecycle, medium). Ran `graphify update .`.

### 2026-06-16 — Iteration #30 (focus: operational-spine / FAIL-STATE — took the documented iter-#30 TOP PRIORITY: shipped option (A)'s smallest slice, making the structurally-absent `failed` task status REACHABLE for the first time. Added a `fail_task(reason)` transition + `POST /api/mc/tasks/{id}/fail` mirroring `block_task`; FIXED [back, 2 files] — py_compile + in-process zero-mutation trace + route-registration check + build VERIFIED, live-HTTP + frontend-trigger stated unverified/deferred)

**Audited.** Per the iter-#29 top priority: LIVE-PROBED the real board FIRST (read-only `MCStore(repo).stats()`), confirming `by_status: {todo 8, ready 1, done 10, blocked 6, triage 1}` — **0 failed**, unchanged from iter #29 (6 live blocked tasks, no failures). Used /graphify (existing-graph fast path; `query "block_task fail_task task lifecycle status transition blocked failed mc_store"`, BFS 80 nodes) to scope rather than blind-grep — located the task-op cluster (`_task_op`/`block_task` at `mission-control-bridge.py:744/764`, `BlockTaskPayload` :129) and the `mc_store` lifecycle (`block_task` :309). Re-confirmed the fully-characterized **FAIL-STATE** thread: `mc_store.py` had NO `failed` setter anywhere (claim→running, complete→done, block→blocked, unblock/promote→ready, schedule/archive/reassign — grep+read confirmed), so the `failed` status was structurally unreachable; yet `failed` is *read* in ≥5 places (briefing/activity/pipeline/stats) PLUS the iter-#7 FAILED column + chip, the iter-#25 notifier `failed→'failed'` outcome, and the iter-#6/#29 drawer reason banner — an entire already-built cluster that was permanently dead because nothing could set the status it keys on.

**Bug/gap (OPERATIONAL-SPINE — the routine's core "are failures distinguishable from blocks / can a task reach a recorded dead-end?" question, answered NO in the data model).** A delegated task that genuinely fails could only ever be recorded as `blocked` (the same state as a recoverable wait-on-human), so the FAILED column/chip were permanently 0 and a failure was indistinguishable from a deliberate block. Iter #25 made the *blocked* path notify (partial mitigation in the bell), but the structural setter gap remained: there was no API at all to assert "this task FAILED." iter #17 explicitly left the FAILED machinery as "a hook for an external process" — but that hook had no endpoint to call.

**Fix (option A, smallest slice — 2 files, backend, mechanical mirror of the proven `block` path).** (1) `mc_store.py:314` — new `fail_task(self, task_id, reason)`: `t["status"]="failed"; t["completed_at"]=_now()` via `_mutate(..., event="failed", payload={"reason": reason})` — identical shape to `block_task` (terminal `completed_at` stamp like done/blocked so cycle-time + the activity feed treat it as ended; the `failed` event carries the reason the drawer banner already renders). (2) `mission-control-bridge.py:769` — new `POST /api/mc/tasks/{task_id}/fail` reusing `BlockTaskPayload` (both carry a single required `reason`), wired through the existing `_task_op` so a missing id maps to the same 404 as every sibling route. **Deliberately deferred to a follow-up run (the operator-facing TRIGGER):** the frontend `failTask` store verb (`useTaskStore`), the `api.ts` `failTask()` client fn, and a drawer **FAIL** button (mirror of the BLOCK button) — kept out of this slice to keep verification airtight + ZERO-mutation (the only way to live-exercise a button is to actually fail a real task). This slice is the load-bearing precondition: it makes `failed` reachable at the API for the first time, so the moment any caller (the deferred drawer button, or the documented external process) fails a task, the entire dead cluster — FAILED column, FAILED chip, amber/red notifier outcome, drawer reason banner — lights up correctly with no further read-side work.

**Verify.** `python -m py_compile mc_store.py mission-control-bridge.py` ✓. **In-process zero-mutation trace** on a throwaway `tempfile.mkdtemp()` MCStore (NEVER touched the live board): seeded a synthetic task via `create_task`, called `fail_task` → status `failed`, `completed_at` set, `by_status` flips `{todo:1}`→`{failed:1}`; the recorded event is exactly `{"kind":"failed","payload":{"reason":"agent exhausted retries: upstream API 500"}}` — byte-identical to `block_task`'s `blocked` event (what `TaskDetailDrawer`'s iter-#6 banner reads); `show_task` exposes the `failed` status + the reason event; a missing id raises `KeyError` (→ bridge 404). **Route-registration check** (imported the bridge module, inspected `app.routes`, ZERO endpoint invocation): `/api/mc/tasks/{task_id}/fail` registered `POST`, mirroring `/block`, and `STORE.fail_task` callable. `npm run build` ✓ (tsc -b + vite, 156 modules, 587 ms — no frontend regression; backend-only). **Layers relied on reasoning — STATED UNVERIFIED:** (1) no live `POST` against the running `:8767` bridge — it would require restarting the live bridge (disrupting operator functionality, against loop rules) AND, because its module-level `STORE` is bound to the real board, any live call would MUTATE operator data; covered instead by the in-process trace on identical code + the route-registration check (same discipline as the iter #26/#27 backend slices). (2) The operator-facing trigger is the explicit next-run remainder (below) — until it ships, the endpoint is reachable only by an external caller, so the FAILED column stays 0 on the live board this run (no regression — it was already 0). Added patch note `iter-30-fail-task-endpoint` (lifecycle, medium). Ran `graphify update .`.

Use the actions below to unblock, reassign, or route it."* — mirroring the backend's `blocked_no_reason` vocabulary and pointing the operator at the ACTIONS grid (unblock/reassign/route are all reachable). Recorded-reason path is byte-unchanged; pure additive fallback.

### 2026-06-16 — Iteration #28 (focus: area #6/operational-spine — the DEEPER cron-semantics differential between `mc_scheduler.py` and `cronSchedule.ts`, the queued iter-#28 top target (a). Closed the documented **interval-anchor display mismatch**: interval cron jobs showed NO next-fire countdown + their CronTimeline ticks were phase-offset from the daemon's real fire times; FIXED [front, 4 files] — build+lint+17-assertion daemon differential VERIFIED, live-DOM stated unverified [zero live cron jobs])

**Audited.** Took the iter-#28 queued top target (a): the deeper cron differential now that the seam is open (iter #27 fixed only the `every`-prefix). Read both engines end-to-end — UI `src/lib/cronSchedule.ts` (`parseSchedule`/`upcomingFires`/`parseInterval`/`expandField`/`nextCron`) and the daemon `mc_scheduler.py` (`is_due`/`parse_interval_seconds`/`_expand_field`/`_cron_matches`). The cron-EXPRESSION halves are sound: `expandField`↔`_expand_field` agree on `*/0`→null, `5/2`→hi=max, `1-10/2`, out-of-range, `0,30` (the only residual divergence is `parseInt`-leniency on GARBAGE like `*/2x` — TS keeps `2`, Python rejects — malformed-input-only, not worth a fix); the DOM/DOW OR-rule matches (`dayMatches`↔`_cron_matches`, both normalize cron-Sun 7→0). **The real, documented seam was the INTERVAL anchor.** Confirmed ground truth first: no `cron.json` on the live board (`.mc/data` has agents/calendar/creators/etc. but zero cron jobs — area is LATENT, present impact nil), and `_now()`=`time.time()`=epoch **seconds**, so cron jobs carry `last_run`/`created_at` as epoch seconds (verified `mc_store.create_cron`:1247 / `record_cron_result`:1280).

**Bug/gap (LIFECYCLE-VISIBILITY + display-correctness — provable, low present impact [no live cron jobs], same latency class as iter #26/#27 cron fixes).** The daemon `is_due` (`mc_scheduler.py:190-196`) fires an interval one period after its anchor = `last_run ?? created_at ?? now`, so an interval job's next fire is fully DETERMINISTIC and the daemon knows it. But the UI threw that away: `parseSchedule` returned `nextMs:null` for ALL intervals, so `OperationsCenter`'s `CronNextFire` showed only "↻ repeats" with **no countdown** — the operator could not see WHEN a repeating job next runs (a direct "is the lifecycle visible?" failure, in the cron spine), even though `McCronJob` already ships `last_run`. Worse, `upcomingFires` anchored interval ticks at `nowMs`, so `CronTimeline`'s next-24h marks were **phase-offset from the daemon's real fire times by the time-since-last-run** (quantified: 10-min offset for a 30m job fired 10m ago) — the agenda showed fires that don't happen, and hid the ones that do.

**Fix (`src/lib/cronSchedule.ts` + 3 consumers, 4 files).** Added a single exported helper `cronAnchorMs(lastRunSec, createdAtSec)` — the ONE source of truth for the daemon's `last_run ?? created_at` precedence + the seconds→ms conversion (mirrors `is_due` exactly; returns `undefined` when both absent → callers stay un-anchored, the pre-fix behavior). `parseSchedule(raw, nowMs, anchorMs?)`: interval branch now returns `nextMs = anchorMs + intervalMs` when anchored (an overdue anchor → past `nextMs` → caller renders "now", matching the daemon firing on the next tick), `null` when un-anchored (back-compat). `upcomingFires(raw, nowMs, windowMs, maxFires, anchorMs?)`: interval series now phase-aligned to the anchor, computed directly via `k = max(1, floor((now-anchor)/period)+1)` so a long-past anchor with a short period stays O(maxFires) (no per-period catch-up loop). Wired the anchor in `OperationsCenter.cronView` (→ `CronNextFire` now renders a live `↻ {countdown}` for anchored intervals, "↻ repeats" only when truly anchorless) and `CronTimeline` (ticks now land on real fire times). `McCronJob` (`api.ts`) gains optional `created_at?: number`. Non-destructive direction: aligns the UI to the firing behavior already live; the daemon is untouched.

**Verify.** `npm run build` ✓ (tsc -b + vite, 156 modules, 649 ms). `npx eslint` on all 4 touched files ✓ **No issues found**. `python mc_scheduler.py` self-test ✓ **ALL PASS** (daemon untouched). **17-assertion differential trace** (faithful port of `is_due`'s interval branch vs the new UI math, `/tmp/cron_diff.mjs`): **17/17 PASS** — (A) recently-fired 30m job: UI `nextMs` == daemon next-due, 20m countdown, daemon due exactly at `nextMs`, first timeline tick == `nextMs`, AND the OLD nowMs-anchored tick was 10m off the real phase; (B) never-fired 2h job anchors at `created_at` == daemon; (C) overdue job → past `nextMs`→"now" == `is_due` true now, all forward ticks within one period; (D) un-anchored == legacy byte-identical + `nextMs` null; (E) year-old anchor + 1m period → capped 300, all forward (no blow-up). **Layer relied on reasoning — STATED UNVERIFIED:** no live DOM render of an interval job showing the new countdown, because the live board has **zero cron jobs** (staging one mutates operator data + costs an LLM fire) and the Claude-Preview MCP still roots at the near-empty parent folder (documented misdirection iters #10–#27). The change is a deterministic pure-parse fix conclusively covered by the 17-assertion daemon differential + build + lint. A future run with a live interval cron job (e.g. `30m`) should confirm the row shows `↻ {countdown}` instead of "↻ repeats" and a CronTimeline tick at `last_run + period`. Added patch note `iter-28-interval-cron-countdown` (lifecycle, medium). Ran `graphify update .` (1490 nodes / 2902 edges / 76 communities).

**Files touched:** `src/lib/cronSchedule.ts`, `src/pages/OperationsCenter.tsx`, `src/components/CronTimeline.tsx`, `src/lib/api.ts`, `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry). No commit/push (loop rules; working tree carries unrelated `mission-control-evolve` + Hermes→Claude rename churn — left intact).

### 2026-06-16 — Iteration #27 (focus: area #6/operational-spine — the NEVER-audited cron engine seam `mc_scheduler.py` ↔ `cronSchedule.ts`; found + fixed a lock-step divergence where the daemon FIRES an interval the UI calls "unknown" / inert; FIXED [front, 1 file] — build+lint+differential-trace VERIFIED, live-DOM stated unverified [no live cron jobs])

**Audited.** Continued the area-#6 backend route-logic pass (iter #25/#26 priority). First drained the documented JSON-shape seams: re-read the metricool (`_metricool_brand`/`_metricool_schedule`/`_normalize_metricool_brand`/`sync_metricool_brands`), idea (`_gather_idea_inputs`/`_llm_json`/`_idea_deck_view`/consume/skip/generate), sentinel (`get_mc_sentinel`/digest/archive), creators (`scrape_creators`/`_post_age_days`), ai-digest (`get_ai_digest`/`generate_ai_digest`), content-pipeline + calendar + virality endpoints — **all robust** (`.get()`-guarded, isinstance/try-except, hallucination guard on blogId; the bare-subscript leads `s['title']`/`v['creator']`/`t['title']` are all safe vs their real producers — `sentinel_news_pipeline.py` always stamps title/url/source/score; the idea-taste/viral producers always set their keys — so they stay LATENT/hand-corruption-only as documented). Also confirmed `mc_store` stamps `created_at`/`last_run`=epoch float, `next_run`=formatted **string** (`_next_run` :1105 `strftime`), `last_status`="ok|error" — so the briefing forecast `next run {nxt}` renders a clean string and there is no sibling of the iter #26 `.lower()`-on-float crash anywhere else. **Live in-process VERIFIED** (imported the bridge, ran every GET on the real 26-task board): briefing/content-pipeline/content-calendar/ai-digest/content-ideas all 200, no crash; briefing counts reconcile with `STORE.stats()` (done 10 / blocked 6 / 0 failed — `failed` still structurally unreachable per FAIL-STATE). Source is clean UTF-8 (546 non-ascii bytes, 0 U+FFFD — the `·`/`—` "mojibake" in my terminal was cp1252 render only, NOT a source bug). `OperationsCenter.colOf` surfaces every live status (triage has its own column, unknowns → todo) — no lost tasks. **Then opened the never-audited cron-engine seam**: `mc_scheduler.py` (the in-bridge daemon that ACTUALLY fires due jobs, wired at `mission-control-bridge.py:343` `_loop`→`due_jobs`→`_fire`→`run_claude`) vs `src/lib/cronSchedule.ts` (the operator's next-fire countdown). Its docstring CLAIMS "identical semantics … so the operator's countdown and the actual fire agree" — but it has appeared in ZERO of the 26 prior runs. A faithful differential port of both interval parsers over 12 schedule strings found a real divergence.

**Bug/gap (LIFECYCLE-VISIBILITY / invisible firing — provable, low present impact [no live cron jobs], same latency class as the iter #26 cron fix).** The interval-prefix strip diverged: the daemon's `parse_interval_seconds` (`mc_scheduler.py:131`) uses `str.removeprefix("every")` (trailing whitespace OPTIONAL), while the UI's `parseInterval` (`cronSchedule.ts:188`) used `.replace(/^every\s+/, '')` (whitespace REQUIRED). Consequence for the no-space shorthand `every30m` / `every2h` / `every5days` (a natural input — the bare `30m` form already works): the **daemon parses it as an interval and FIRES it every period**, but the **UI parser falls through to kind `'unknown'`** → the job renders with label = the raw string and **no next-fire countdown** (`parseSchedule` returns `nextMs:null`), AND `upcomingFires` returns `[]` so it's absent from `CronTimeline`. So a job the operator was shown as inert/unparseable is silently firing on schedule — the exact "is the lifecycle visible?" failure the routine targets, in the cron spine. Differential trace (daemon vs faithful-TS port, 12 inputs): `every30m`/`every2h`/`every5days` were the 3 DIVERGENCES (daemon fires, UI `unknown`); all spaced/bare forms agreed.

**Fix (`src/lib/cronSchedule.ts:188`, one file, one regex char + comment).** `\s+` → `\s*` in the `every` strip, bringing the UI parser into lock-step with the daemon — the **non-destructive direction**: it aligns the displayed countdown with the firing behavior that is already live, rather than removing the daemon's ability to fire `every30m` (which would be reducing live functionality, against the loop rules). `parseInterval` is the single feeder for BOTH the countdown (`parseSchedule`) and the timeline (`upcomingFires`), so one change fixes both surfaces. Verified the strip doesn't over-match: `everyday`→`day`→regex fails→still `unknown` (agrees with daemon); `every`→``→`unknown`.

**Verify.** **Differential trace BEFORE** (daemon `parse_interval_seconds` vs faithful TS port): 3 divergences (`every30m`/`every2h`/`every5days`). **AFTER** the `\s*` fix (re-ran the same 12-input matrix incl. `30m`/`every 30m`/`5 min`/`every  15m`/`45 min`/`every 1 d`/`everyday`/`every`): **0 divergences** — daemon-seconds×1000 == UI-ms on every input. `npm run build` ✓ (tsc -b + vite, 156 modules, 582 ms). `npx eslint src/lib/cronSchedule.ts` ✓ **No issues found**. `python mc_scheduler.py` self-test ✓ **ALL PASS** (daemon untouched, still green). **Layer relied on reasoning — STATED UNVERIFIED:** no live DOM render of an `every30m` job showing a countdown, because the live board has **zero cron jobs** (per CF-NEXTRUN; staging one would mutate operator data + cost an LLM fire) and the Claude-Preview MCP still roots at the near-empty parent folder (documented misdirection iters #10/#14/#18/#20–#26). The change is a deterministic pure-parse fix conclusively covered by the before/after differential matrix + build + lint. A future run with a live `every30m` cron job should confirm the dashboard now shows its `every 30m` label + a live countdown (and a CronTimeline tick) instead of `—`. Added patch note `iter-27-cron-countdown-every-shorthand` (lifecycle, medium). Ran `graphify update .` (1475 nodes / 2857 edges / 70 communities).

**Files touched:** `src/lib/cronSchedule.ts`, `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry). No commit/push (loop rules; working tree carries unrelated `mission-control-evolve` + Hermes→Claude rename churn — left intact).

### 2026-06-16 — Iteration #26 (focus: area #6 — FRESH backend route-logic re-sweep [not swept since #19]; found + fixed a guaranteed-crash + dead-logic bug in `/api/mc/briefing`'s cron-failure detection; FIXED [back, 1 file] — build+py_compile+standalone-trace VERIFIED, live-bridge stated unverified)

**Audited.** Took queued iter #25 priority (b) — a fresh backend route-logic pass of `mission-control-bridge.py` + `mc_brain`/`mc_diag`/`mc_store` (not swept since iter #19). Scoped via /graphify (existing-graph fast path; `query "Zustand stores polling … useTaskStore"` to first re-confirm priority (a), then read the backend). First completed a clean re-sweep of priority (a), `src/stores/*.ts` — **ALL CLEAN**: `useTaskStore` (mutate/error surfacing sound, `mapMcToOp` lossy-but-latent per Lead #1, `summarize` disjoint per iter #1), `useActivityStore` (singleton pollTimer, exclusive-route refcount dismissed iter #20), `useContentStore` (platformFor full-name vocab = documented degraded-mode-only watch), `useHealthStore` (ms seam correct, iter #25), `useSentinelStore`/`useLeadStore`/`useSystemStore`/`useBriefingStore`/`useCapabilitiesStore` (allSettled + per-domain loading/error, deterministic hashes, clamped). Then swept the backend: `mc_brain` (run_claude arg/timeout/JSON-envelope handling — CLEAN), `mc_diag` (doctor `kanban.json` check is CORRECT — mc_store's canonical `tasks_file` IS `root/kanban.json` :70, so the live-board "kanban.db" memory note is stale Hermes-era — CLEAN), `mc_store` lifecycle (claim→`started_at`, complete/block→`completed_at`, confirms the activity feed's field names :682-683 — CLEAN), workspace endpoint (path-traversal guards solid), activity/content-pipeline/`_detect_platform`/`_extract_date` (all already-fixed or documented-latent). Landed the one real present bug in the briefing route.

**Bug/gap (LOGIC + CRASH on the operator's daily Briefing — present, reachable, HIGH impact).** `/api/mc/briefing` (`mission-control-bridge.py:1496`) built its `failed_jobs` list with `"error" in (j.get("last_run","") or "").lower() or "failed" in (...).lower()`. Two defects: **(1) it reads the wrong field** — a cron job's outcome lives in `last_status` ("ok"|"error"), stamped by `mc_store.record_cron_result` (`mc_store.py:969`); `last_run` is a stamp, not a status — so the failed-job detection that drives the briefing's `arc` line + the HIGH-sev "cron job failure detected" directive **never matched a real failure**, it was dead logic. **(2) it CRASHES** — `last_run` is set to `_now()` (a float epoch) by both `record_cron_result` (:968) and `mark_cron_run` (:953); `(float or "")` is the float (truthy), and `float.lower()` raises `AttributeError`, **500-ing the ENTIRE briefing endpoint**. Reachable the moment ANY cron job has run once — including the operator clicking RUN NOW (`run_cron` :1161 → `record_cron_result`). `/api/mc/briefing` feeds BOTH the Briefing page (`useBriefingStore.refresh`) and the Sentinel digest (`useSentinelStore` via `getMcBriefing`), so one fired cron job would blank both surfaces (the iter #22 ErrorBoundary contains it to the pane, but the data is gone). Zero present impact ONLY because the live board still has no cron jobs (per CF-NEXTRUN) — a latent guaranteed crash, not a hypothetical.

**Fix (`mission-control-bridge.py:1496`, one file, one expression).** Replaced the `last_run` substring search with `failed_jobs = [j for j in cron_jobs if (j.get("last_status") or "").lower() == "error"]` (+ a 5-line comment explaining the field). This (1) reads the purpose-built outcome field so failed jobs are ACTUALLY detected, and (2) is type-safe on every shape `last_status` takes — string "ok"/"error", `None`, or absent (the `mark_cron_run` path sets `last_run` but not `last_status`) — so no `.lower()`-on-float crash is possible. Response shape unchanged (still `arc`/`directives` with the same structure); pure backend logic, no endpoint/type/frontend change.

**Verify.** `python -m py_compile mission-control-bridge.py` ✓. **Standalone Python trace** over 4 representative cron-job shapes (ran-ok / ran-error / never-ran[`last_run`=None] / scheduled-via-`mark_cron_run`[`last_run`=float, no `last_status`]): the OLD expression **CRASHED** with the exact `'float' object has no attribute 'lower'` on the ran-ok job; the NEW expression returns `['b']` — exactly the one `last_status=='error'` job — and never raises on float/None/missing. `npm run build` ✓ (tsc -b + vite, 156 modules, 627 ms — no frontend regression; the change is backend-only). **Layer relied on reasoning (not a live request) — STATED UNVERIFIED:** no live `GET /api/mc/briefing` against a running bridge with a real fired cron job (the live board has zero cron jobs, and staging one would mutate operator data — out of scope for an audit run). The fix is deterministic Python conclusively covered by py_compile + the 4-shape trace + build. A future run with the bridge up and a fired cron job should curl `/api/mc/briefing` and confirm a 200 with the failed job named in `arc`/`directives`. Added patch note `iter-26-briefing-cron-failure-crash` (bug, high). Ran `graphify update .`.

**Files touched:** `mission-control-bridge.py`, `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry). No commit/push (loop rules; working tree carries unrelated `mission-control-evolve` + Hermes→Claude rename churn — left intact).

### 2026-06-15 — Iteration #25 (focus: area #5 — finished the never-dedicated `src/components/*.tsx` sweep [all 4 CLEAN], then fixed the lifecycle-visibility hole it surfaced: failed/blocked tasks fired NO notification at all; FIXED [front, 3 files] — build+lint+standalone-trace VERIFIED, live-DOM stated unverified)

Only residue: async setState after a mid-flight close (60s+ gateway restart) — a React-18 silent no-op, not worth a guard.

All four are genuinely well-built — the area-#5 component sweep is now **fully closed** with no bug in the four targets. Pivoted to the routine's higher-priority lifecycle-visibility track (the 🔔 center, referenced in `ShortcutsHelp` as the "completed / **failed** task feed") and landed a real, present operational-spine bug.

**Bug/gap (LIFECYCLE-VISIBILITY / lost terminal signal — present, reachable, HIGH operator impact).** `TaskNotifier.tsx` (mounted once in `Layout`, watches the 7 s-polled `useTaskStore.mcTasks`) fired a notification only on a transition into `TERMINAL = {done, completed, failed}` (`:15`). But — per the fully-characterized **FAIL-STATE** thread — **`mc_store.py` has NO `failed` setter** (grep-confirmed this run: the only status writes are `running` `:260`, `done` `:265`, `blocked` `:270` [which even stamps `completed_at` like `done`], `ready` `:275/:280/:500`; `scheduled`/`archived` elsewhere). A delegated task that fails or dead-ends — **including the retry circuit-breaker / Kimi quota-burn path** — is recorded as **`blocked`**, which was NOT in `TERMINAL`. Consequence: when delegated work failed, the operator got **zero notification** — no OS desktop toast AND no in-app Notification Center history entry — so a failure was invisible unless they manually scrolled the BLOCKED column. The bell literally advertises a "failed task feed" (`NotifyCenter` empty-state + `ShortcutsHelp :43`) that was **silently dead**. This is the operational-spine's core "are failures distinguishable from blocks / does a task reach a dead-end the operator can't see?" question, failing in the live data model.

**Fix (front, 3 files — minimal, accurate).** (1) `TaskNotifier.tsx`: replaced `TERMINAL` with `NOTIFY_ON = {done, completed, failed, blocked}` + `isNotify`, and added `outcomeOf(status)` mapping `blocked→'blocked'`, `failed→'failed'`, else `'done'`; the transition guard is now "saw it before in a non-notify state, now in a notify state" (so a pre-existing/already-blocked task on first poll still only seeds — no startup burst — and a task staying blocked across polls does NOT re-fire); the OS toast `fire()` now titles `⚠ Task blocked` / `✕ Task failed` / `✓ Task complete`. (2) `useNotifyStore.ts`: `NotifyEvent.outcome` widened to `'done' | 'failed' | 'blocked'` (kept `failed` for forward-compat). (3) `NotifyCenter.tsx`: a new `OUTCOME_TONE` map renders each outcome distinctly — DONE green ✓, FAILED red ✕, **BLOCKED amber ⚠** — so the operator can tell a block from a completion at a glance; empty-state hint reworded to "Finished & blocked tasks will appear here." No backend / endpoint / new-bridge-call change (the watcher is pure client logic over already-live `mcTasks`).

**Verify.** `npm run build` ✓ (tsc -b + vite, 156 modules, 599 ms — the widened union typechecks across all three files). `npx eslint src/components/TaskNotifier.tsx src/components/NotifyCenter.tsx src/stores/useNotifyStore.ts` ✓ **No issues found**. **Standalone Node trace** of the pure transition state-machine (6 cases, ALL PASS): (1) pre-existing `blocked` on first poll → seed only, no notify; (2) `running→blocked` → one `blocked` outcome; (3) staying `blocked` across polls → no re-fire; (4) `blocked→ready→running→done` → two DISTINCT notifications (`blocked` then `done`, distinct keys); (5) `running→done` → completion still fires (no regression); (6) new task appearing already-`done` → no burst. **Layer relied on reasoning (not pixels) — STATED UNVERIFIED:** no live DOM walk of an actual toast / amber BLOCKED row, because staging it needs a real `running→blocked` transition on the live board (zero-mutation staging of an OS Notification + a Zustand-history render is impractical, and the Claude-Preview MCP still roots at the near-empty parent folder — documented misdirection iters #10/#14/#18/#20–#24). The change is deterministic client logic conclusively covered by build + lint + the 6-case trace (same verification shape as iter #23/#15). A future run with a working in-repo preview (or a live blocked task) should confirm the amber ⚠ BLOCKED row in the bell + a `⚠ Task blocked` toast when notifications are enabled. Added patch note `iter-25-notify-blocked-tasks` (lifecycle, high). Ran `graphify update .`.

**Files touched:** `src/components/TaskNotifier.tsx`, `src/components/NotifyCenter.tsx`, `src/stores/useNotifyStore.ts`, `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry). No commit/push (loop rules; working tree carries unrelated `mission-control-evolve` + Hermes→Claude rename churn — left intact).

So a rejected delete/spawn (e.g. "agent 'x' has running tasks", "task 't_…' not found", agent not on disk) left the modal open with **zero operator-visible reason** — a dead button. Reachable through normal click-around on the Agent Network detail panel; agent-lifecycle CRUD is operational spine.

No store/endpoint/type change — `crudError` is already wired (`useGhostStore((s) => s.error)`), already cleared on each op start (`set({ error: null })`) and each successful poll, so no new stale-error behavior beyond what create/edit already accept. Now all four CRUD dialogs surface the bridge's real reason.

### 2026-06-15 — Iteration #23 (focus: area #4 — deeper logic in GhostNetwork/ChatTerminal — Agent Network reroute control leaks a stale target/confirmation across agent switches; FIXED [front, 1 file] — build+lint+standalone-trace VERIFIED, bridge up)

**Audited.** With the un-swept-pages backlog + the route-level ErrorBoundary closed (iter #22), advanced to the next queued priority: **deeper logic in `ChatTerminal.tsx` / `GhostNetwork.tsx`** (iter #20 only cleared their effects + obvious seams; the message/stream/reducer/command logic was un-swept). Scoped via /graphify (existing-graph fast path; `query "ChatTerminal GhostNetwork message stream reducer logic send receive transcript session command bar reroute topology state"`, BFS depth 2, 118 nodes). Read both pages end-to-end plus `useGhostStore.ts`:
- `ChatTerminal.tsx` — **CLEAN**. All three media effects (SpeechRecognition, MediaRecorder, Whisper-status probe) have unmount cleanup + the `alive` guard; `addFiles` size-caps at 25 MB and try/catches each read; `handleSend` snapshots input+pending before the await; attachments/timestamps null-guarded; `formatTime` try/catches a bad ISO. No race/leak.
- `useGhostStore.ts` — **CLEAN**. `mapAgentsToTopology` (id===name, lowercased compares hold), `agentLoad`/`num`/`hash` pure & clamped, `pushCapped` caps history at 48, all CRUD verbs return a boolean and stash `bridgeDetail(err)`. Matches the iter #20 finding.
- `GhostNetwork.tsx` — feed merge (`norm` seconds→ms, ascending sort, slice(-80)), `selectedTasks` sort (running-first then recency), `deriveStatus`, `kind` classification (handles the activity display vocab), zoom/pan pointer effect (full teardown) — all CLEAN. Landed on the **reroute control** as the one real present-tense bug.

**Bug/gap (LOGIC / cross-agent state leak on a MUTATING delegation control — present, reachable).** The detail panel's reroute box is backed by two component states — `rerouteTo` (the destination profile, `:142`) and `rerouteMsg` (the "moved N tasks → X" confirmation, `:144`) — that were **only ever set inside `handleReroute`** and **never reset when the selected agent changed**. `select()` (`:248`) only toggled `selectedId`; the CLOSE button (`:596`) called `setSelectedId(null)` directly. So after picking a reroute target for agent A (and/or running a reroute), switching to a different agent C left `rerouteTo` pointing at the OLD target — and because the dropdown filters options to `x.id !== selected.id` (`:625`), that stale target stays a valid, *selected* option under C. Hitting **Reroute** (`:629`) then reassigns **C's** pending queue to a destination chosen for A — a real kanban `reassign` verb (`reassignTask`), i.e. silently MISROUTED delegated work, the operational-spine's core concern. Secondary: the stale `rerouteMsg` (`:638`) showed A's "2 tasks → bob" confirmation under C's panel. Reachable through normal click-around; no error needed.

**Fix (`src/pages/GhostNetwork.tsx`, one file, 2 edits — event-handler reset, NOT an effect).** (1) `select()` now also clears `setRerouteTo('')` + `setRerouteMsg(null)` on every selection change (toggle-off included), so a target/confirmation chosen for one agent never carries to the next. (2) the CLOSE button routes through `select(null)` (which always deselects — `cur===null ? null : null`) so closing the panel clears the control too. Deliberately done in the handlers rather than a `useEffect(... [selectedId])`: an effect-based reset trips the repo's `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` rule (would add NEW lint), and the handler reset is the idiomatic, render-free fix. No backend/endpoint/type change.

**Verify.** `npm run build` ✓ (tsc -b + vite, 156 modules, 599ms — types OK). `npx eslint src/pages/GhostNetwork.tsx` ✓ for the change — the file reports **1 pre-existing** `react-hooks/set-state-in-effect` at **:140** (the untouched `richUI`→`setLayout` effect, confirmed by `sed`), and my edits (in `select` + the CLOSE handler) add **zero** new issues; my bar is "no NEW lint in touched files" → met. **Standalone Node state-machine trace** ✓: modelled `select()` OLD vs NEW across `select(alice)→pick rerouteTo=bob→reroute→select(carol)` — OLD leaves `rerouteTo="bob"` + stale msg (misroute=true), NEW clears both (misroute=false); `select(null)` (CLOSE) deselects + clears → **PASS**. **Layer relied on reasoning (not pixels) — STATED UNVERIFIED:** no live DOM walk of the click sequence. The bridge IS up (:8767, `/api/mc/agents` 200, left untouched/read-only), but this is a precise client-state interaction (pick-target → switch-agent → would-be-reroute) and the Claude-Preview MCP still roots at the near-empty parent folder (documented misdirection iters #10/#14/#18/#20/#21/#22); the fix is pure client-state logic whose outcome is deterministic and conclusively covered by build + lint + the standalone trace (same verification shape as iter #15's chat-store race). A future run with a working in-repo preview should select an agent, pick a reroute target, switch to another agent, and confirm the dropdown resets to "reroute to…" and the old "moved N" note is gone. Added patch note `iter-23-ghost-reroute-stale-target` (bug, medium). Ran `graphify update .`.

**Files touched:** `src/pages/GhostNetwork.tsx`, `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry). No commit/push (loop rules; working tree carries unrelated `mission-control-evolve` + Hermes→Claude rename churn — left intact).

### 2026-06-15 — Iteration #22 (focus: area #5/#4 — finished the un-swept-pages sweep, then shipped the systemic fix it kept pointing at: a route-level React ErrorBoundary so one crashing panel no longer blanks the whole app; FIXED [front, +1 new file +1 edit] — build+lint VERIFIED, live-DOM stated unverified)

**Audited.** Continued the iter #20/#21 area-#5/#4 sweep and **closed out the un-swept-pages backlog** queued in Next Targets (`LeadTracker`/`WorkflowBuilder`/`Systems`/`Arsenal`/`Uplink`). Scoped via /graphify (existing-graph fast path; `query "LeadTracker WorkflowBuilder Systems Arsenal Uplink pages render crash null undefined map key effect cleanup error boundary"`, BFS depth 2, 80 nodes — confirmed all five pages + `App.tsx`). Read all five end-to-end:
- `LeadTracker.tsx` — CLEAN (interval has cleanup; all actions try/catch into `actionErr`; `statusColor[...] || fallback` guarded; reduce over `l.score` is store-shape-dependent but typed).
- `Uplink.tsx` — CLEAN (uniformly `?.` / `?? []` guarded; derives `effectiveTarget` instead of setState-in-effect).
- `Systems.tsx` — CLEAN (both effects have cleanup; `Math.max(1, ...(x ?? []))` seeds; `fmtTokens` type-guards).
- `Arsenal.tsx` — two **latent** nested-array crash sites (`curator.most_active.map` :212, `memory.providers.map` :191 — guarded by `curator &&`/`memory &&` but NOT on the inner array; would throw only if the bridge ever sends the parent object without the array).
- `WorkflowBuilder.tsx` — `t.title.length` (:129) throws if a task has no title (SVG render path).
These are **individual latent render-throw sites**, and they all share the exact root the last two iters kept hitting: **there is NO React error boundary anywhere in the app** (grep across `src`: 0 `ErrorBoundary`/`componentDidCatch`, confirmed again this run; `App.tsx` routes render straight through `Layout`'s `<Outlet/>`). The handoff explicitly flagged a route-level boundary as "arguably higher-leverage than hunting each throw site one at a time." Picked that as the single highest-operator-impact item.

**Bug/gap (RESILIENCE / whole-app crash containment — systemic).** With no boundary, an uncaught throw during *any* page's render propagates to the React root and **unmounts the entire tree** — not just the offending panel, but the sidebar, topbar and every other route — leaving a blank screen until a manual reload. iter #21 fixed one trigger (`BriefingTerminal`'s `new URL`); this run found two more (Arsenal nested arrays, WorkflowBuilder titleless task) and the class is open-ended (any future null-deref / bad-payload / bad-date in a render). So the operator can lose the *entire* command center to one bad RSS link or one malformed task — the worst-case blast radius for a monitoring dashboard.

**Fix (front, 2 files — 1 new + 1 edit).** (1) NEW `src/components/ErrorBoundary.tsx` — a minimal class component (the only way to use `getDerivedStateFromError`/`componentDidCatch`); on a caught render error it logs the stack to console (so the trace isn't lost) and renders a **dependency-free** cyberpunk fallback panel (⚠ MODULE RENDER FAULT + the error message in a `<pre>` + a "▷ Retry render" button that clears boundary state). Fallback is intentionally plain `<div>`s (no `Panel`/store imports) so it cannot itself throw while reporting a crash. (2) `src/components/Layout.tsx` — imported it and wrapped the routed `<Outlet/>` (`:341`) in `<ErrorBoundary key={location.pathname}>` (`location` was already in scope, :64). **Keying on `location.pathname`** remounts the boundary with fresh state whenever the operator navigates, so a crashed route auto-recovers on nav-away (no stuck fallback). No state-loss regression: route changes already swap the Outlet's element (distinct component type → React already remounts per page); Zustand stores are module-level and unaffected. No backend / endpoint / type change.

**Verify.** `npm run build` ✓ (tsc -b + vite, **156** modules — was 155, the new file; 659ms, types OK incl. the class component + `key` prop). `npx eslint src/components/ErrorBoundary.tsx src/components/Layout.tsx` ✓ ("No issues found"). `node` JSON check ✓ (`.mc/patch-notes.json` still valid, 20 notes, newest `iter-22-route-error-boundary`). **Layer relied on reasoning (not pixels) — STATED UNVERIFIED:** no live DOM render of a contained crash. A runtime React test would need jsdom + a client renderer (error boundaries do NOT fire under `react-dom/server`/SSR), and only `react-dom` is installed — adding a test runner would mutate `package.json`/`node_modules`, out of scope per loop rules; the Claude-Preview MCP still roots at the near-empty parent folder (documented misdirection iters #10/#14/#18/#20/#21). The change rests on the **canonical, documented React error-boundary contract** (`getDerivedStateFromError` sets fallback state; `componentDidCatch` logs; a changed `key` forces remount) + green build/lint. A future run with a working in-repo preview should force a throw (e.g. temporarily render a titleless task in WorkflowBuilder) and confirm the fallback shows while the sidebar + other routes stay alive, then that nav-away clears it. Bridge :8767 left untouched (not contacted this run — pure front change). Added patch note `iter-22-route-error-boundary` (ui, high). Ran `graphify update .` (1368 nodes / 2653 edges — picked up the new component).

**Files touched:** `src/components/ErrorBoundary.tsx` (new), `src/components/Layout.tsx`, `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry). No commit/push (loop rules; working tree carries unrelated `mission-control-evolve` + Hermes→Claude rename churn — left intact).

### 2026-06-15 — Iteration #21 (focus: area #5/#4 — metric components swept CLEAN; un-swept pages → Briefing Sentinel feed crashes on a malformed RSS link; FIXED [front, 1 file] — build+lint+standalone VERIFIED, producer-path proven reachable)

**Audited.** Continued the iter #20 area-#5/#4 sweep. Scoped via /graphify (existing-graph fast path; `query "metric components CycleTimeSLA AgingWip BacklogBurndown TaskThroughput CronTimeline AgentPerformance date math percentile bucketing seconds vs ms now"`, community 1+2). **First swept the TOP-PRIORITY (a) targets — the six metric components — and found them CLEAN:** `CycleTimeSLA`/`AgingWip`/`BacklogBurndown`/`TaskThroughput`/`AgentPerformance`/`CronTimeline` all consume `nowMs` (ms) consistently, the libs interpret task stamps as epoch **seconds** and convert correctly (`taskThroughput.ts:53` `nowSec = nowMs/1000`, bucket compares are second-vs-second), `bucketIndexOf` handles the not-found `-1` safely, histogram bodies are gated on `count===0`/`openCount===0`, empty-array `Math.max(1, ...)` seeds are present everywhere, sort comparators sink nulls. No off-by-one / seconds-vs-ms / empty-array bug in the metric layer — it's genuinely well-built (matches the iter #15 pure-lib CLEAN finding, now confirmed at the component seam too). Advanced to TOP-PRIORITY (b) the un-swept pages (`BriefingTerminal`/`LeadTracker`/`WorkflowBuilder`/`Systems`/`Arsenal`/`Uplink`) and landed a **present, reachable render-crash on a primary monitoring surface**.

**Bug/gap (CODING / crash-on-untrusted-data — reachable, high-blast-radius).** `BriefingTerminal.tsx`'s `SentinelFeed` renders, for each news story, the originating site via `new URL(story.url).hostname.replace(/^www\./,'')` (was `:79`). The Sentinel stories are produced by `scripts/sentinel_news_pipeline.py` from **uncontrolled external RSS** (HN / Reddit / Google-News / generic RSS); the RSS fetcher sets `"url": link_text` where `link_text = link.text if link is not None else ""` (`sentinel_news_pipeline.py:128,131`) — i.e. it **emits `""` whenever a feed item lacks a `<link>`** (and could emit a relative/garbage link). `new URL("")` (and any non-absolute string) **throws `TypeError: Invalid URL`** at render time. **There is NO error boundary anywhere in the app** (grep: 0 `ErrorBoundary`/`componentDidCatch`) — confirmed `Layout.tsx:23`'s sibling `new URL(BRIDGE_BASE_URL)` is already try/caught (iter #14), but this one was bare — so one malformed story URL would throw out of the render and **blank the entire Briefing route** (React unmounts the subtree; in prod a white page until reload), not just the one row. Secondary same-root issue: the story `<a href={story.url}>` with `target="_blank"` opened a dead tab to the app root on an empty url. **Severity HIGH** (whole-surface crash on a monitoring page), **latent-but-guaranteed-reachable**: the live cache is currently clean (7 digests / 23 stories each, 0 bad urls — checked) so it isn't firing *today*, but the producer demonstrably ships `""` and Google-News/Reddit links are the most variable — it's a question of when, not if.

**Fix (`src/pages/BriefingTerminal.tsx`, one file).** Added a module-level `safeHost(url)` helper that wraps `new URL(...).hostname.replace(/^www\./,'')` in try/catch and returns `''` on any parse failure (matches the surrounding local-helper style, e.g. `useTypewriterLines`). The story map now computes `const host = safeHost(story.url)` once and (1) renders the host `<span>` only when `host` is non-empty (`{host && <span…>{host}</span>}` — no more bare `new URL`), and (2) sets `href={host ? story.url : undefined}` so an unusable url degrades to a non-navigating anchor instead of reloading the app. Valid urls render byte-identically to before (www-stripped hostname). No type/endpoint/backend change.

**Verify.** `npm run build` ✓ (tsc + vite, 155 modules, 582ms — types OK). `npx eslint src/pages/BriefingTerminal.tsx` ✓ ("No issues found"). **Standalone Node logic check** ✓ (6 cases): `""`→`""`, `/relative`→`""`, `"not a url"`→`""` (all previously THREW, now degrade), `https://www.example.com/...`→`example.com`, HN/Google-News absolute urls → exact hostname — proving no throw on bad input and identical output on good input. **Live data probe (read-only):** the operator's 7 cached sentinel digests + `latest.json` (23 stories each) currently hold **0** empty/non-http urls, so the crash is not firing on today's data — the fix is preventive against the proven producer path. **Layer relied on reasoning (not pixels):** no live before/after DOM render — the bridge is up (:8767, `/api/mc/sentinel` 200) but the live cache has no bad url to reproduce the crash with, and the Claude-Preview MCP roots at the near-empty parent folder (documented misdirection, iters #10/#14/#18/#20); the fix is a render-pure guard whose deterministic JS behavior (`new URL("")` throws) is conclusively covered by the standalone check + build + lint. A future run that catches a live malformed story should visually confirm the feed survives with that one host label hidden. Bridge :8767 left untouched. Added patch note `iter-21-briefing-feed-bad-url-crash` (bug, high). Ran `graphify update .` (1360 nodes / 2644 edges).

**Files touched:** `src/pages/BriefingTerminal.tsx`, `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry). No commit/push (loop rules; working tree carries unrelated `mission-control-evolve` + Hermes→Claude rename churn — left intact).

### 2026-06-15 — Iteration #20 (focus: area #5 components / #4 un-swept pages — War Room activity feeds printed UTC not local time; FIXED [front, 1 file] — LIVE-data before/after VERIFIED)

**Audited.** Advanced off the now-closed backend content seams (iter #19 drained sentinel/metricool/virality) to the never-dedicated-pass focus areas: #5 `src/components/*.tsx` and #4 the big un-swept pages. Scoped via /graphify (existing-graph fast path; `query "GhostNetwork ChatTerminal components useEffect cleanup intervals null crash key collisions stale state polling subscriptions"`, BFS depth 2, 121 nodes). **Swept the un-swept surfaces and dismissed several candidates before landing the real one:** (1) `useActivityStore` module-level `pollTimer` start/stop is refcount-free, but only `WarRoom` + `GhostNetwork` drive it and they are **exclusive routes** (`AgentDrillDown` only one-shot `fetchActivities`, never the timer) — single-consumer, the `if (pollTimer) return` guard holds, NOT a bug. (2) `GhostNetwork` reroute passes the agent `id` while tasks are filtered by `assignee == name` — looked like a mismatch, but `mapAgentsToTopology` sets `id === name` (`useGhostStore.ts:113`) and every compare lowercases both, so the rerouted task still resolves to the target agent — NOT a bug. (3) `WorkerLogStream`/`NotifyCenter`/`AgentDrillDown`/`TaskNotifier`/`ChatTerminal` effects all have correct cleanup + null guards — CLEAN. (4) `TaskNotifier`/`NotifyCenter` `failed` outcome branch is dead (FAIL-STATE: `failed` status unreachable) — already a documented deliberate decision, not re-touched. Landed on a **present, operator-visible correctness bug on the primary monitoring surface**.

**Bug/gap (LOGIC / timezone — present, visible).** The two bottom feeds in the War Room — **TASK ACTIVITY · mc kanban** (`log`) and **AGENT SIGNAL · mc activity** (`signalLog`) — formatted each row's time as `new Date(sec*1000).toISOString().slice(11,19)` (`WarRoom.tsx:109,123`). `toISOString()` always prints **UTC**, so every line in both feeds was shifted by the operator's whole UTC offset. The kicker: the **same** `/api/mc/activity` events render in the **Ghost Network** "Activity Stream" via local `getHours()/getMinutes()/getSeconds()` (`GhostNetwork.tsx:655`), and Chat (`toLocaleTimeString`) + NotifyCenter (relative-to-local) are local too — so an operator cross-checking the two screens saw the **same event at two different times**, with War Room's the wrong (UTC) one and **unlabelled** (the topbar clock is UTC too but is explicitly tagged `ZULU` — `Layout.tsx:332`; these per-event rows are not). Secondary: `toISOString()` on a non-finite stamp throws `RangeError`, which would crash the entire War Room render (latent — the bridge always emits numeric stamps). Also folded in a `(a.status || '')` guard on the adjacent `signalLog` colour lookup (`:125` — the sole `a.status` consumer that wasn't already null-guarded vs its two siblings; latent since the bridge guarantees `status`).

**Fix (`src/pages/WarRoom.tsx`, one file).** Added a module-level `hms(sec)` helper that renders an epoch-SECONDS instant as **local** `HH:MM:SS` (byte-identical to Ghost Network's formatter — `pad(getHours)/getMinutes/getSeconds`) and returns `--:--:--` on a non-finite stamp instead of throwing. Both feeds now call `hms(...)` (`log` :124, `signalLog` :138) and the signal colour lookup null-guards `a.status` (:140). Net: War Room's feeds agree with Ghost Network's Activity Stream for the same events, in the operator's own time, and a bad stamp degrades gracefully instead of blanking the panel. No backend/endpoint/type change; feeds an unchanged `LogTail` render path a corrected string.

**Verify.** `npm run build` ✓ (tsc + vite, 155 modules, 569ms — types OK). `npx eslint src/pages/WarRoom.tsx` ✓ ("No issues found"). **Standalone Node logic check** ✓: at the run host's tz (offset 420 min = 7 h) a real instant rendered OLD `15:06:40` (UTC) vs NEW `08:06:40` (local), NEW **matches** the Ghost Network formatter exactly, OLD **throws `RangeError`** on `NaN` while NEW returns `--:--:--`. **LIVE before/after on the real bridge (:8767 up, 200, read-only):** pulled `/api/mc/activity` (50 events) and computed both — e.g. "completed · Research direct competitors" rendered OLD `21:33:12` (UTC) vs NEW `14:33:12` (local), the latter matching what Ghost Network already shows for that same event. **Layer relied on reasoning (not pixels):** no Vite/DOM screenshot — the Claude-Preview MCP roots at the near-empty parent folder (documented misdirection, iters #10/#14/#18), and this is a pure string-formatting change into the unchanged `LogTail` component; build + lint + standalone + live-data before/after are conclusive. Bridge :8767 left untouched. Added patch note `iter-20-warroom-feed-local-time` (bug, medium). Ran `graphify update .`.

Operator-visible inconsistency on a deliverable surface.

### 2026-06-15 — Iteration #16 (focus: backend route logic — Content Factory platform badge mis-detection; FIXED [back, 1 file] — LIVE-VERIFIED over HTTP)

**Audited.** The deliverable/lifecycle track + the whole pure-lib layer are CLOSED/CLEAN (iters #14/#15), so this run advanced to the **fresh-hunt suggestion**: sweep the un-swept-since-migration backend (`mission-control-bridge.py`) route logic (focus area #6), prioritizing the deliverable surfaces. Read end-to-end: `mc_brain.py` (run_claude/claude_json — CLEAN, careful: closed stdin, timeout→124, is_error→ClaudeError, tolerant JSON extraction), the bridge's ClaudeError→HTTP mapping (chat correctly maps quota/429→503 else 502), `mc_store.py` full lifecycle + `stats()`/`diagnostics()`/`_has_deliverable` (CLEAN), the component effect-cleanup sweep (all intervals/listeners have teardown; only `ModelPicker` flash `setTimeout`s lack cleanup — cosmetic, no leak of consequence), and the `/api/mc/activity` synth (always emits a non-empty `status`, so WarRoom's `a.status.toLowerCase()` is safe). Landed on the **Content Factory pipeline** (`get_content_pipeline` → `_detect_platform`), a deliverable surface.

**Bug/gap.** `_detect_platform` (`mission-control-bridge.py:1485`) classified a content task's platform by testing the **two-letter codes as bare substrings** — `"ig" in text`, `"tt" in text`, `"li" in text`, `"yt" in text`, plus a spaced `" x "`. Those codes occur inside ordinary words, so the badge fired on noise: `"ig"` inside "agencies"/"strategic", `"tt"` inside "captions" **and inside "twitter"** (so "twitter post" returned **TT/TikTok**, never reaching the X branch), `"li"` inside "deliverables"/"pillars". This is operator-visible: `_detect_platform` feeds the platform **Pill badge** on Content Factory campaign cards (`ContentFactory.tsx:481`), draft rows (`:524`) and calendar entries (`:607`). **Proven against the REAL board (read-only):** of 22 content tasks, the current code emits `{IG:16, LI:4, TT:2}` and the fix changes **12 of 22 (55%)** to correct values — every changed one a clear false positive (e.g. "Draft hooks and captions for all scheduled posts" → TT→MULTI; "Find direct competitor agencies…" → IG→WEB). The live operator bridge at :8767 served the identical buggy `{IG:16, LI:4, TT:2}`, confirming the bug is live in production now.

**Fix (`mission-control-bridge.py`, one file, one function).** `_detect_platform` now matches full platform NAMES as substrings (unchanged) but the short codes only as **whole words** via a small `code(abbr)` = `re.search(r"\b"+abbr+r"\b", text_l)` helper. Operator shorthand ("post for IG", "the TT cut", bare "post on X") still resolves; the "x" branch is now `\bx\b` (a strict superset of the old `" x "`/`startswith("x ")`, so no regression). A task with no real platform signal honestly falls through to **MULTI** instead of an invented badge. `re` is already imported. No frontend, no new endpoint, no behavior change to the keyword filter.

**Verify.** `python -c ast.parse` on the bridge ✓. **Standalone regression of the patched function extracted from the edited file (12 cases) ✓** — operator shorthand IG/TT/bare-x preserved, full names preserved, and twitter→X, agencies→MULTI, captions→MULTI false positives all gone (ALL PASS). `npm run build` ✓ (tsc + vite, 155 modules, 759ms — backend-only change, build unaffected, no NEW lint as no TS touched). **LIVE end-to-end over HTTP:** the operator's :8767 (OLD code) served `{IG:16, LI:4, TT:2}`; a **throwaway bridge on :8799 (NEW code, BRIDGE_PORT=8799, same data files, read-only)** served the corrected `{WEB:4, IG:9, MULTI:7, LI:1, TT:1}` with the watch tasks fixed ("Plan Instagram…"→IG kept; "Find direct competitor agencies…"→WEB; both caption-drafts→MULTI). Operator's :8767 re-confirmed 200 and untouched throughout; :8799 killed, `git status`-clean of temp artifacts (none written). Added patch note `iter-16-content-platform-badge` (bug, medium). Ran `graphify update .`.

### 2026-06-15 — Iteration #15 (focus: stores — Lead #5 chat-send error lands in wrong conversation; FIXED [front, 1 file])

**Audited.** The deliverable/lifecycle track is FULLY CLOSED (iter #14), so this run advanced to the **focus-area rotation #1/#2: `src/lib/*.ts` pure logic + `src/stores/*.ts` stores**. Scoped via /graphify (existing graph fast-path; `query "OperationsCenter oldest ready age seconds ago format Date.now stats rendering cycle time backlog metrics lib pure functions"`, BFS depth 2, 100 nodes — surfaced every lib metric module + the stores). **Read the ENTIRE pure-lib layer end-to-end** to clear focus area #1: `agentMetrics.ts`, `taskThroughput.ts`, `cronSchedule.ts` (the cron stepper/`expandField`/`nextCron`/`upcomingFires`), `cycleTime.ts` (percentile interp), `backlogTrend.ts`, `agingWip.ts` — **ALL CLEAN** (date math seconds-vs-ms consistent, `nowMs` injected not `Date.now()`, percentile linear-interp correct, cron OR-semantics + 7→0 dow normalize correct, bucket boundaries half-open). Then evaluated the three remaining store/page leads (#1, #4, #5) for which is a *real present-tense* bug vs. latent.

**Bug/gap.** Lead #5 is the only genuine present bug. `useChatStore.send` (`src/stores/useChatStore.ts`): the user message is appended to `key` (`:199`, computed BEFORE the `await sendMcChat`), but on failure the catch appended the `COMMS FAILURE` system line to `get().activeId || DRAFT_KEY` (`:235`), **re-derived AFTER the await**. If the operator switches conversations (`selectSession`/`newSession`) while a send is in flight and that send then throws, `activeId` has moved on, so the error lands in a **different conversation than the user's message** — a stale-key/race bug in the chat surface (Claude Chat + Agent Network command bar). (Leads #4 OLDEST-READY = correct-by-accident, displays right today; #1 lossy status projection = latent, only `tasks.length` consumed — both left as documented watch items, NOT fixed.)

**Fix (`src/stores/useChatStore.ts`, one file, one edit).** The catch now appends to `key` (the same transcript the user message went to) instead of the freshly re-derived `activeId`, with a comment explaining the race. Guarantees the error line is always co-located with the message that failed, regardless of any navigation during the await. No backend, no new state, no behavior change on the no-navigation path.

**Verify.** `npm run build` ✓ (tsc + vite, 155 modules, 640ms). `npx eslint src/stores/useChatStore.ts` ✓ ("No issues found"). **Standalone Node simulation of the catch-key selection across 4 cases** ✓: draft→switch-to-S2, session-S1→switch-to-S2, draft→no-nav, S1→no-nav — OLD code misplaces the error into the wrong conversation in BOTH navigation-race cases; NEW code co-locates with the user message in **4/4, 0 misplaced**. **Not live-verified in the Vite preview:** the bug is a precise client-state race (a send must FAIL at the exact moment the operator has navigated away) that can't be triggered deterministically through the UI; the fix is pure client-state logic (bridge-independent), fully proven by build + lint + the standalone simulation, so a preview adds no signal. Added patch note `iter-15-chat-error-wrong-conversation` (bug, medium). Ran `graphify update .` (one-line function-body change → no topology delta, outputs unchanged — expected).

**Files touched:** `src/stores/useChatStore.ts`, `.mc/patch-notes.json`, `.mc/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` (this entry). No commit/push (loop rules; working tree carries unrelated `mission-control-evolve` + Hermes→Claude rename churn — left intact). NB: the log's older entries cite `.hermes/patch-notes.json`/`.hermes/BUGHUNT_LOG.md` — those files now live under **`.mc/`** (verified this run); the `.hermes/` text is stale pre-migration straggler wording, the canonical paths are `.mc/*` (Claude ecosystem, per the cardinal rule).

### 2026-06-15 — Iteration #14 (focus: LABEL-1 — hardcoded topbar bridge port; FIXED [front, 2 files] — LIVE-VERIFIED at an alternate port)

with no explicit port); changed the label to `● BRIDGE :{BRIDGE_PORT}`. No backend, no new component, no behavior change on
the default config (still renders `:8767`).
